Adult video store means any establishment having a substantial or significant portion of its stock and trade in videotapes, movies or other reproductions, whether for sale or rent, which are distinguished or characterized by their emphasis on matter depicting, describing, or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas or an establishment with a segment or section thereof, comprising 20 percent of its total floor space, devoted to the sale or display of such material or which derives more than 20 percent of its net sales from videotapes, movies or other reproductions which are characterized or distinguished by an emphasis on specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas. 
Church means a body of communicants gathered into church order, united under one form of government by the profession of the same faith and the observance of the same ritual and ceremonies. 
Convicted shall include an adjudication of guilt, a plea of guilty, or a plea of nolo contendere. 
Employed as an adult entertainment establishment employee and work at any licensed premises mean all work done or services performed while in the scope of employment on the licensed premises or elsewhere. 
Encounter center or rap establishment means any business, agency or person who, for any form of consideration or gratuity, provides a place where two or more persons may congregate, assemble or associate for the primary purpose of engaging in, describing or discussing specified sexual activities, or exposing specified anatomical areas. 
Escort bureau or introduction services mean any business, agency or person who, for a fee, commission, hire, reward, or profit, furnishes, or offers to furnish, names or persons, or who introduces, furnishes or arranges for persons who may accompany other persons to or about social affairs, entertainments or places of amusement, or who may consort with others about any place of public resort or within any private quarters. 
Good moral character means a person has not been convicted of a drug-related crime, an alcohol-related felony, a sex-related crime, or a crime of moral turpitude in the past five years. 
Independent contractors means employees of adult entertainment establishments and they shall be licensed as employees regardless of the type of business relationship with the owner or licensee of the adult entertainment establishment. 
Minor means any person who has not attained the age of 21 years. 
Parcel of land means any quantity of land capable of being described by location and boundary, designated and used or to be used as a unit. 
Partial nude dancing means appearing or dancing at an adult entertainment establishment, as defined herein, partially nude, but at a minimum with the human male or female genitals, pubic area and buttocks and all of the nipples of the breasts of a female being at least shielded and covered by a fully opaque covering. 
Public indecency , as it relates to an adult dancing establishment, means: 
(1)	Engaging in sexual intercourse; 
(2)	Engaging in deviate sexual conduct; 
(3)	Engaging in a state of total nudity as opposed to partial nudity; 
(4)	Fondling the genitals of oneself or another person; or 
(5)	Dancing with the male genitals covered, but in a discernible turgid state. 
Specified anatomical areas means any of the following: 
(1)	Less than completely and opaquely covered human genitals or pubic region, buttock, or female breast below a point immediately above the top of the areola; or 
(2)	Human male genitalia in a discernable turgid state, even if completely and opaquely covered. 
Specified sexual activities means any of the following: 
(1)	Actual or simulated sexual intercourse, oral copulation, anal intercourse, oral anal copulation, bestiality, direct physical stimulation of unclothed genitals, flagellation or torture in the context of a sexual relationship, or the use of excretory function in the context of sexual relations, and any of the following sexually oriented acts or conduct, anilingus, buggery, coprophagy, coprophilia, cunnilingus, fellation, necrophilia, pederasty, pedophilia, piquerism, sapphism, zooerasty; 
(2)	Clearly depicting human genitals in a state of sexual stimulation, arousal or tumescence; 
(3)	Use of human or animal ejaculation, sodomy, oral copulation, coitus, or masturbation; 
(4)	Fondling or touching of nude human genitals, pubic region, buttocks or female breast; 
(5)	Masochism, erotic or sexually oriented torture, beating or the inflicting of pain; 
(6)	Erotic or lewd touching, fondling or other sexual contact with an animal by a human being; or 
(7)	Human excretion, urination, menstruation, vaginal or anal irrigation. 
Such activities shall be deemed to be acts of public indecency under the terms of this chapter. 
Total nude dancing means appearing or dancing at an adult dancing establishment, as herein defined, without the protection or benefit of the minimal coverings required for partial nude dancing. 
Sec. 6-3. - Unlawful operation declared a nuisance. 
Any adult entertainment establishment operated, conducted or maintained contrary to the provisions of this chapter shall be and the same is hereby declared to be unlawful and a public nuisance. The city may, in addition to, or in lieu of prosecuting a criminal action hereunder, commence an action or actions, proceeding or proceedings for abatement, removal or enjoining thereof, in the manner provided by law. The city shall further be authorized to take such other steps and apply to such court or courts as may have jurisdiction to grant such relief as will abate such nuisance and restrain and enjoin any person from operating, conducting or maintaining an adult entertainment establishment contrary to the provisions of this chapter. In addition, violation of the provisions of this chapter shall be per se grounds for suspension or revocation of any permit granted hereunder. 
Secs. 6-4—6-24. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - LICENSING 

Sec. 6-25. - Limitation on number of licenses issued. 
Should there be a sufficient number of current licenses to meet the needs and desires of the inhabitants of the city, no new licenses shall be issued. In determining the needs and desires of the inhabitants, the standard of review shall be that the market is virtually unrestrained as defined in Young v. American Mini Theaters, Inc., 427 U.S. 50, 96 S.Ct. 2440, 49 L.Ed.2d 310 (1976). 
(Ord. of 10-1-1990) 
Sec. 6-26. - License required. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in, conduct or carry on, or operate in or upon any premises within the city an adult entertainment establishment as defined in this chapter, without a license to do so. 
(b)	No license so issued shall condone or authorize, or be deemed to condone or authorize, any activity if the same is deemed illegal or unlawful under state, federal, or municipal law. Any such license must be currently valid or the licensee shall have made proper application for renewal within the time required therefor under this chapter. 
Sec. 6-27. - Application for license. 
(a)	Any person desiring to obtain a permit to operate, engage in, conduct or carry on any adult entertainment establishment business shall make application to the city chief of police. Prior to submitting such application, the nonrefundable fee, established by this article, shall be paid to the city clerk to defray, in part, the cost of the investigations and reports required by this article. Upon payment thereof, the city clerk shall issue a receipt showing that such application fee has been paid. 
(b)	The application for such a license shall not authorize the engaging in, operation of, conduct of or carrying on of any adult entertainment establishment business until the approval of the application as herein provided. 
Sec. 6-28. - Application contents. 
Each application for an adult entertainment establishment license shall contain, at a minimum, the following information. 
(1)	The applicant's full name, social security number, and date of birth. 
(2)	The present address and telephone number of the applicant. 
(3)	Acceptable written proof that the applicant is at least 21 years of age. 
(4)	The business, occupation and employment history of the applicant for the five years immediately preceding the date of application. 
(5)	The business license history of the applicant and whether such applicant, in previous businesses in this or any other city, state or territory, has had any license or permit for an adult entertainment business or similar type of business revoked or suspended, the reason therefor, and the business activity or occupation of the applicant subsequent to such action of suspension or revocation. 
(6)	If the applicant is a corporation, the name of the corporation shall be set forth exactly as shown in its articles of incorporation and charter, together with the place and date of incorporation, all states or other jurisdictions in which the applicant is authorized to do business (including written evidence of such authorizations), and the names and addresses of each of its current officers and directors. 
(7)	If the applicant is a partnership, the applicant shall set forth the name, residence address and dates of birth of the partners. 
(8)	If the applicant is a limited partnership, it shall furnish a copy of its certificate of limited partnership. 
(9)	If one or more of the partners is a corporation, the provisions of this section pertaining to corporations shall apply to the corporate partner. 
(10)	The applicant corporation or partnership shall designate one or more of its officers or general partners to act as its responsible managing officer. Such designated person shall complete and sign all application forms required of an individual applicant under this article, but only one application fee shall be charged. 
(11)	Whether the applicant, any partners or any corporate officers or directors, if the applicant is a corporation, have been convicted of any crime evidencing a lack of good moral character, as defined in this chapter, in the past five years and, if so, a complete description of any such crime, including date of violation, date of conviction, jurisdiction where the crime or act occurred, and any disposition thereof, including any fine or sentence imposed and whether terms of any court-imposed sentence have been fully completed. 
(12)	If the applicant is a person doing business under a trade name, a copy of all trade name documents properly recorded as required by law. 
(13)	If the applicant is a corporation, a copy of the articles of incorporation, trade name affidavit, if any, and last annual report to the Georgia Secretary of State. 
(14)	At least three character references from individuals who are in no way related to the applicant or individual shareholders, officers or directors of a corporation and who are not and will not benefit financially in any way from the operation of the business if the license is granted and who have not been convicted of any crime involving moral turpitude. The city clerk shall prepare forms consistent with the provisions of this section for the applicant who shall submit all character references on such forms. 
(15)	The address of the premises to be licensed. 
(16)	Whether the premises are owned or rented by the applicant. 
(17)	A plat by a registered surveyor, licensed by the state, showing that the location of the proposed premises is in accordance with the provisions of this article and chapter 94, zoning. 
(18)	Each application for an adult entertainment establishment license shall be verified and acknowledged under oath to be true and correct: 
a.	If the applicant is an individual, by the individual; 
b.	If a partnership, by the manager or general partner; 
c.	If a corporation, by the president of the corporation; 
d.	If any other organization or association, by the chief administrative official of such organization or association; 
(19)	In addition to the information required herein, the application shall disclose the name, address, social security number and date of birth of all persons who have a financial interest of any type in the business that is applying for the license, and any other matter reasonably required by the chief of police. 
Sec. 6-29. - Applicant to appear. 
The applicant, if an individual, or the designated responsible managing officer, if a partnership, corporation, or other entity, shall personally appear at the city police department, before the chief of police, or his designee, and produce proof that the nonrefundable application fee, established by this article, has been paid, and shall also present the completed license application containing the required information to the chief or his designee. 
Sec. 6-30. - Application; investigation; recommendations. 
(a)	The city shall have 45 days to investigate the application and the background of the applicant. Upon completion of the investigation, the chief shall report his findings and recommendations to the mayor and city council, which shall consider the application within 30 days of receipt of the report from the chief. 
(b)	After a hearing on the application, at which any interested persons present may be heard, the mayor and city council shall grant or deny the permit at its next regular meeting; but the mayor and city council may only recommend the granting of such permit if it finds: 
(1)	The required application fee has been paid. 
(2)	The application conforms in all respects to the provisions of this chapter. 
(3)	The applicant has not knowingly made a material misrepresentation in the application. 
(4)	The applicant has fully cooperated in connection with the investigation of his application. 
(5)	The applicant, if an individual, or any officers or directors of the applicant, if the applicant is a corporation, or any of the partners, including limited partners, if the applicant is a partnership, have not been convicted, entered a plea of guilty or nolo contendere, in a court of competent jurisdiction to an offense involving a sex-related crime or drug-related or alcohol-related felony or have been convicted, entered a plea of guilty or nolo contendere, of an attempt to commit any of the aforementioned offenses, or convicted, entered a plea of guilty or nolo contendere in any other state as to an offense which, if committed or attempted in this state, would have been the same or substantially the same offense as one or more of the stated offenses. 
(6)	The applicant has not had an adult entertainment establishment license or other similar license or permit denied or revoked for cause in this city or in any other local government jurisdiction located in or out of this state prior to either the date of the application or the date of the granting of the application. 
(7)	The building, structure, equipment, and location of such business, as proposed by the applicant, would comply with all applicable zoning and distance laws and would qualify to receive a certificate of occupancy under the law of this state and the articles of this city. 
(8)	The applicant is at least 21 years of age. 
(9)	That neither the applicant, nor any of the applicant's employees, agents, partners, directors, officers, or managers, has within five years of the date of the application, knowingly allowed or permitted any of the specified sexual activities defined herein to occur in or upon the premises where such adult entertainment establishment is to be located, nor has such applicant or other persons knowingly allowed or permitted the proposed licensed premises to be used as a place in which solicitations for any of the specified sexual activities occurred within the said time period. 
(10)	That on the date the business for which a permit is required herein commences, and thereafter, there will be a responsible person actually on the premises to act as manager at all times during which the business is open. 
(11)	That the proposed premises shall not be located at any location not authorized by this article or by chapter 94, zoning. 
(12)	That the grant of such license will not result in a violation of this article or any other article or regulation of the city, or of any laws, rules or regulations of the state, or the United States. 
(13)	Any other inquiry deemed necessary or desirable by the city to ensure the health, safety and welfare of the citizens of the city or the preservation of its neighborhoods. 
(14)	That all of the requirements of this article, including, but not limited to this section, have been met by the applicant. 
(c)	All hearings regarding such application shall be open to the public and advertised in the legal organ of the county as required by law. 
Sec. 6-31. - Additional license requirements. 
(a)	The licensee shall maintain with the city police department at all times a written statement of the name, address, and phone number of the manager or assistant manager in charge of the licensed premises and there shall at all times be a manager in charge and on the premises during operating hours. 
(b)	Each licensee shall have a continuing obligation to comply with all provisions of this chapter. 
(c)	The applicant may be required to appear at any hearing on the issue of the grant, denial, suspension, or revocation of the requested license governed by this article. 
Sec. 6-32. - Persons prohibited as licensees. 
Subject to the other requirements of this chapter, no license authorized by this chapter shall be issued to or held by: 
(1)	An applicant who has not paid all required fees and taxes, including ad valorem taxes, for a business at that location; 
(2)	Any person who is not of good moral character as defined in this chapter; 
(3)	Any corporation, any of whose officers, directors, or shareholders are not of good moral character as defined in this chapter; 
(4)	Any partnership or association, any of whose partners or members are not of good moral character as defined in this chapter; 
(5)	Any person employing, assisted by or financial in whole or in part by, any person who is not of good moral character as defined in this chapter; 
(6)	Any applicant who is not qualified to hold and conduct a business according to the laws of the United States, the state or the city. 
Sec. 6-33. - License renewal. 
Licenses for adult entertainment establishments shall be renewed on a calendar year basis, provided that the licensee continues to meet the requirements set out in this article. The renewal fee for the adult entertainment establishments licenses shall be as established by this article. Renewal applications shall be submitted by November 15 of each year prior to the year for which such license is requested. 
Sec. 6-34. - Licenses nontransferable. 
No adult entertainment establishment license may be sold, transferred or assigned by a licensee, or by operation of law, to any other person. Any such sale, transfer or assignment, or attempted sale, transfer or assignment, shall be deemed to constitute a voluntary surrender of such licensee and such license shall thereafter be null and void; provided, however, that if the licensee is a partnership and one or more of the partners should die, one or more of the surviving partners may acquire, by purchase or otherwise, the interest of the deceased partner without effecting a surrender or termination of such license, and in such case, the license, upon notification to the city, shall be placed in the name of the surviving partner, subject to compliance with all other requirements of this article. 
Sec. 6-35. - Change of name. 
(a)	No licensee shall advertise, operate, conduct, manage, engage in, or carry on an adult entertainment establishment business under any name other than the name of the business as specified on the license. 
(b)	Any application for an extension or expansion of a building or other place of business where an adult entertainment establishment is located shall require inspection and shall comply with the provisions and regulations of this chapter, and all other articles, rules and regulations of the city. 
Sec. 6-36. - Display of license. 
An adult entertainment establishment licensee shall conspicuously display all licenses required by this chapter. 
Sec. 6-37. - Annual report. 
No later than March 1 of each year, an adult entertainment establishment licensee shall file a verified report with the city clerk showing the licensee's gross receipts and amounts paid to dancers for the preceding calendar year. 
Sec. 6-38. - Revocation and appeal. 
(a)	After notice and hearing, the chief of police shall be authorized to suspend or revoke a license previously granted hereunder. In the event the chief of police seeks to suspend or to revoke a license, the chief of police shall give written notification to the licensee of such action. 
(b)	The notice shall contain a specification of the violation upon which such suspension or revocation is based and shall be served upon the licensee, by registered mail, return receipt requested, at least five days prior to the date of the hearing. The licensee shall be given written notice of the time and place of the hearing. 
(c)	The chief of police shall be authorized to suspend or revoke a license in the event of the occurrence of any one or more of the following: 
(1)	A licensee provided false or misleading information in the original or subsequent application process; 
(2)	A licensee has knowingly allowed possession, use, or sale of controlled substances on the premises; 
(3)	A licensee has knowingly allowed the violation of an article of the city or a violation of any criminal law of the state or of the United States to occur on the premises; 
(4)	A licensee has violated any provision of this article; 
(5)	A licensee has been convicted, during the license period, of any drug-related, alcohol-related or sex-related crime by the state, the city, or the United States regarding an offense which was committed on the premises, or which would otherwise violate the provisions of this chapter when such offense would serve to prohibit the licensee from obtaining a permit under this article; 
(6)	A licensee fails to pay any fee, license fee, fine or other amount of money due the city under this article or any other license or occupational taxation article of the city. 
(d)	In the event the chief of police shall suspend or revoke any license hereunder, the suspension or revocation shall be for a period of not less than one day nor more than 365 days, within the sound discretion of the chief of police; provided, however, that the licensee shall be authorized to continue his business operations until the date of any hearing scheduled in accordance with this article. 
(e)	No licensee or other applicant may apply for a license during any period of suspension or revocation. In any hearing or investigation conducted by the chief of police, in connection with a possible suspension or revocation of a license issued hereunder, the chief shall consider, among other things, the severity of the allegations, the evidence submitted and the testimony presented, in making any decision on suspension, revocation and the duration of any suspension or revocation. 
(f)	In the event of a suspension or revocation by the chief of police, the licensee may appeal the decision of the chief of police to the city council by filing a written notice of appeal within ten days from the date that the licensee receives written notification of the decision of the chief of police. 
(g)	The written notification shall be mailed to the licensee by certified mail, return receipt requested. Thereafter, a hearing shall be scheduled before the city council within 45 days after the filing of the notice of appeal by the applicant. 
(h)	After hearing by the city council, the city council may take such action as it finds warranted from the evidence submitted to it, including, but not limited to, the affirming of the action of the chief of police, the reversal of such action, or the imposition of modified sanctions upon the licensee. 
Sec. 6-39. - License fees. 
(a)	Application and renewal fees shall be paid to the city clerk upon application or renewal, as the case may be. The amount of the fees shall be as established from time to time by the city council. 
(b)	Any licensee shall also be subject to all business license fees and occupational taxes imposed by the city pursuant to chapter 22. 
Secs. 6-40—6-67. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - EMPLOYEES 

Sec. 6-68. - Qualifications. 
Employees of an adult entertainment establishment shall be at least 21 years of age. Any applicant for employment who has been previously convicted within the preceding five years of a sex-related crime, a drug-related crime, or an alcohol-related felony, or a crime involving moral turpitude shall not be eligible for employment as an adult entertainment establishment employee, and any employee who is convicted of a sex-related crime, drug-related crime, or alcohol-related felony while employed as an adult entertainment establishment employee shall not thereafter work at any premises requiring licenses under this chapter for a period of five years from the date of such conviction, unless a longer time is ordered as part of a court-ordered sentence. 
Sec. 6-69. - Approval for employment. 
Before any person may be employed at a licensed premises by a licensee hereunder, he shall file a notice with the chief of police of his intended employment on forms that require the information set forth in section 6-68. The city shall have 45 days to review and investigate the application submitted by the employee. If the employee is found to be qualified for such employment by the terms of this article, the chief of police shall grant approval of the employment. Upon approval, the employee may be employed by the licensee. If approval is denied, the prospective employee may, within ten days of said denial, apply to the chief administrative officer of the city for a hearing. The decision of the chief administrative officer after hearing the appeal shall be final. 
Sec. 6-70. - Investigation fee. 
An investigation fee in the amount established by the city council, or a receipt from the city clerk evidencing the payment of such fee at the time the notice is filed, shall accompany the notice of intended employment submitted to the chief of police. 
Sec. 6-71. - Retention of employee records. 
An adult entertainment establishment licensee shall maintain and retain for a period of two years the names, addresses, and ages of all persons employed therein. 
Sec. 6-72. - Employment of minors prohibited. 
No adult entertainment establishment licensee shall employ or contract with a person under the age of 21 years or a person not licensed pursuant to this chapter. 
Secs. 6-73—6-102. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - PREMISES, LOCATION, AND BUSINESS HOURS 

Sec. 6-103. - Advertising and posting. 
The premises for which the license herein is sought either as an initial license or a renewal thereof, shall be posted with a notice in a form prescribed by the city chief administrative officer for at least 21 days prior to any hearing on such application. In addition, a newspaper advertisement shall be published in the county legal organ in a form prescribed by the city chief administrative officer at least two times during the ten days prior to any hearing on such license application or renewal. The posted notice and newspaper advertisements shall notify all interested persons of the date, time, location and purpose of the hearing on such application. 
Sec. 6-104. - Lighting. 
(a)	Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Full lighting shall mean illumination equal to 3.5 footcandles per square foot. 
(b)	Required. All areas of an establishment licensed hereunder shall be fully lighted at all times patrons are present. 
Sec. 6-105. - Premises open for inspection. 
The licensed premises shall be open at any and all reasonable times for inspection by the city to establish and ensure compliance with this article. 
Sec. 6-106. - Lot size; road frontage; zoning. 
Adult entertainment establishment businesses shall be located only in a commercial zoning district as now or hereafter defined by the city's zoning articles and regulations on a parcel of property not less than three acres in size, with no less than 100 feet of road frontage. 
Sec. 6-107. - Proximity to other buildings and facilities. 
No adult entertainment establishment business shall be located: 
(1)	Within 1,000 feet of any parcel of land which is zoned for multifamily or single-family uses or purposes; 
(2)	Within 1,000 feet of any parcel of land upon which a church, school, governmental building owned or occupied by such government, library, civic center, public park or neighborhood playground is located; 
(3)	Within 1,000 feet of any parcel of land upon which another establishment regulated or defined hereunder is located. 
Sec. 6-108. - Measurements of distance. 
For the purpose of this article, distance shall be by airline measurement from property line to property line, using the closest property lines of the parcels of land involved. 
Sec. 6-109. - Permitted hours of operation. 
All adult entertainment establishments shall be closed between 12:45 a.m. and 8:00 a.m. each day. They shall also be closed every Sunday and on Christmas Day. 
Secs. 6-110—6-131. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - PROHIBITED ACTS AND PERFORMANCES 

Sec. 6-132. - Nude dancing; public indecency. 
Total nude dancing, appearing nude or dancing involving acts of public indecency as defined by this chapter are hereby prohibited in any adult dancing establishment. Any other dancing or acts of public indecency prohibited by other applicable laws of the state or articles of the city as now or hereinafter enacted, or the violation of any of the other criminal laws of the state or of the city, are likewise prohibited. 
Sec. 6-133. - Touching of employees or patrons. 
No adult entertainment establishment licensed employee shall fondle or caress any patron and no patron shall fondle or caress any adult entertainment establishment employee on the licensed premises. 
Sec. 6-134. - Dancing platform required; distance from patrons. 
All dancing by an employee at an adult dancing establishment shall occur on a platform intended for that purpose which is raised at least two feet from the level of the floor. No dancing shall occur closer than four feet to any patron. 
Sec. 6-135. - Sexual activities. 
No adult entertainment establishment licensee shall allow or permit an employee or any other person on the premises to engage in any of the following sexual activities: 
(1)	Actual or simulated sexual intercourse, oral copulation, anal intercourse, oral anal copulation, bestiality, direct physical stimulation of unclothed genitals, flagellation or torture in the context of a sexual relationship, or the use of excretory functions in the context of sexual relations, and any of the following sexually oriented acts or conduct: anilingus, buggery, coprophagy, coprophilia, cunnilingus, fellation, necrophilia, pederasty, pedophilia, piquerism, sapphism, zooerasty; 
(2)	Clearly depicting human genitals in a state of sexual stimulation, arousal or tumescence; 
(3)	Use of human or animal ejaculation, sodomy, oral copulation, coitus, or masturbation; 
(4)	Fondling or touching of nude human genitals, pubic region, buttocks or female breasts; 
(5)	Masochism, erotic or sexually oriented torture, beating or the inflicting of pain; 
(6)	Erotic or lewd touching, fondling or other sexual contact with an animal by a human being; or 
(7)	Human excretion, urination, menstruation, vaginal or anal irrigation. 
Sec. 6-136. - Gratuities prohibited. 
No patron shall directly pay or give any gratuity to any dancer. No dancer shall solicit any pay or gratuity from any patron. 
Sec. 6-137. - Alcohol prohibited. 
No adult entertainment establishment shall be authorized to serve, sell, distribute or allow the consumption or possession of any beer, wine, or other intoxicating liquor or controlled substances upon the premises of the licensee, and no license for the sale of beer, wine, or other intoxicating liquor may be issued by the city to an adult entertainment establishment as herein defined. 
State Law reference— Certain nude and sexual conduct prohibited on premises licensed for sale of alcoholic beverages, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-40 et seq. 
Secs. 6-138—6-157. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - MINORS 

Sec. 6-158. - Admission of minors unlawful. 
It shall be unlawful for a licensee to admit or permit the admission of minors into a licensed premises. 
Sec. 6-159. - Sales to minors unlawful. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to sell, barter or give, to any minor any service, material, device or thing sold or offered for sale from an adult bookstore, adult motion picture theater, adult massage parlor or adult dancing establishment or other adult entertainment enterprise. 
Chapter 10 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Power to license and regulate alcoholic beverages, O.C.G.A. § 36-31-7; alcoholic beverages generally, O.C.G.A. § 3-1-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 10-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Alcoholic beverage means any beverage containing alcohol, however sold, and shall include, but shall not be limited to, malt beverages, wines, and spirituous liquors. 
Malt beverage means any fermented beverage made in whole or in part from malt, or any similar fermented beverage, containing any amount of alcohol. 
Manager means any person who supervises the regular operations of a business licensed under this chapter. 
Mixed drink means any distilled spirits or spirituous liquors served for consumption on the premises by the drink that may or may not be diluted by any other liquid. Any sales of mixed drinks in the city must be approved by referendum as required by state law. 
Nuisance means anything that causes hurt, inconvenience or damage to another, and the fact that the act done may otherwise be lawful shall not keep it from being a nuisance. The inconvenience complained of shall not be fanciful, or such as would affect only one of fastidious taste, but it shall be such as would affect an ordinary reasonable person. 
Owner means any person, partner or stockholder owning any percentage of a business. 
Premises means the space or area owned, leased or controlled by the licensee and used by the licensee for the purpose of operating under the license. 
Restaurant means any establishment which is licensed under this chapter, which establishment derives at least 30 percent of its total annual gross sales from the sale of prepared meals and which is publicly held out as a place where hot meals are prepared and served at least five days a week, excluding holidays. 
Spirituous liquors or distilled spirits means all beverages containing alcohol obtained by distillation or containing more than 21 percent alcohol by volume, including fortified wines. 
Wine means any wine, fortified or unfortified, produced either within or without the state and containing not more than 21 percent alcohol by volume. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-1) 
Sec. 10-2. - Applicability of and conflict with state law. 
(a)	Governing law. The Georgia Alcoholic Beverage Code, O.C.G.A. § 3-1-1 et seq., wherever applicable to municipalities, is hereby adopted and made a part of this chapter. 
(b)	Conflict of laws. Any provisions of this chapter in conflict with the cited state code, shall be invalid and the state code section dealing with the same subjects shall control. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-2) 
Sec. 10-3. - Activity declared a privilege. 
Notwithstanding anything in this chapter to the contrary, the sale of alcoholic beverages in the city is a privilege, and not a right, and the issuance of a license hereunder shall not create any property rights in the license holder. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-3) 
State Law reference— Similar provision, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-1. 
Sec. 10-4. - Responsibility for enforcement. 
It shall be the responsibility of the chief of police or the chief's agents to enforce the provisions of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-4) 
Sec. 10-5. - Familiarity and compliance with chapter. 
Any licensee hereunder shall ensure that the licensee and all employees of the licensee are advised of and comply with the provisions of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-53) 
Sec. 10-6. - Availability of telephone. 
Every premises licensed hereunder must have a telephone and have such telephone available during the hours of operation. Failure to have a telephone shall constitute grounds for suspension or revocation of all licenses. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-57(d)) 
Sec. 10-7. - Illegal drugs or narcotics. 
For every license issued pursuant to this chapter, it shall be the duty and responsibility of the licensee, or licensee's agent or employee to report to the police department any usage or possession of illegal drugs or narcotics on a licensed premises. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 10-57(e)) 
Secs. 10-8—10-32. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - LICENSING[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Local authority to regulate manufacture, distribution, and package sales, O.C.G.A. § 3-4-40 et seq.; municipal authority to adopt regulations and determine location, O.C.G.A. § 3-4-49; local licenses for sale of distilled spirits by the drink, O.C.G.A. § 3-4-110; local licenses regarding malt beverages, O.C.G.A. § 3-5-42; local licenses for sale of wine, O.C.G.A. § 3-6-40. 

Sec. 10-33. - Required. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to manufacture or sell or offer for sale at wholesale or retail in the city any alcoholic beverage without having the required alcoholic beverage license. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-30) 
State Law reference— Authority for local licensure generally, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-2. 
Sec. 10-34. - Licenses for nonprofit organizations. 
Any patriotic organization, charitable organization, or fraternal organization that has been in operation in the city for a period of five years under a national or state charter and that is nonprofit, in that the individual members do not receive any dividends or share in the profits, shall be licensed in order to make retail sales of spirituous liquors to its members. No license shall be issued unless the organization is approved by the city for the issuance of such license. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-31(a)) 
Sec. 10-35. - Bona fide private clubs. 
(a)	Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Fixed salary means the amount of compensation paid any member, officer, agent or employee of a bona fide club as may be fixed for the person by its members at a prior annual meeting or by the city council of the organization out of the general revenue of the club and shall not include any commission on any profits from the sale of alcoholic beverages. For the purpose of this definition, tips or gratuities that are added to charges under club regulation are not considered to be from the sale of alcoholic beverages. 
(b)	License and city approval required. Any bona fide private club that is nonprofit, in that the individual members do not receive any dividends or share in the profits, shall be licensed in order to make retail sales of spirituous liquors to its members. No license shall be issued unless the club is approved by the city for the issuance of the license. 
(c)	Qualifications for licensure. To qualify for licensure, the bona fide private club must be a nonprofit corporation or association, organized under the laws of this state, that: 
(1)	Has been in existence at least one year prior to the filing of its application for a license to be issued pursuant to this chapter; 
(2)	Has at least 50 regular dues-paying members; 
(3)	Owns, hires or leases a building or space within a building for the reasonable use of its members with suitable kitchen and dining room space and equipment and sufficient number of employees for cooking, preparing and serving meals for its members and guests; 
(4)	Has no member, officer, agent or employee directly or indirectly receiving, in the form of salary or other compensation, any profit from the sale of alcoholic beverages, beyond a fixed salary. 
(d)	Preexisting clubs. However, any private club previously holding any type of alcoholic beverage license issued by the city at the time of the effective date of the ordinance from which this section is derived shall not be required to meet all of the criteria set out for a bona fide private club. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-31(b)-(c)) 
State Law reference— Authority for local regulation and licensing of private clubs for sale of alcoholic beverages, O.C.G.A. § 3-7-40. 
Sec. 10-36. - Qualification of licensee. 
No alcoholic beverage license required by the provisions of this article shall be issued: 
(1)	Residency; exception. To any person, unless the person, or the person's manager actually in charge of the operation of the business, is a resident of the county and a citizen of the United States or has designated a resident of the city who is responsible for any matter relating to the license; provided, however, that where the applicant is a corporation, incorporated pursuant to the laws of the state or authorized to do business in the state, that has an alcoholic beverage license or licenses presently in force and issued by another municipality, the county residency requirement shall not apply if the corporation appoints its local store manager or manager as an additional agent and representative of the corporation. 
(2)	Good moral character and reputation. To a person who, in the opinion and judgment of the city council, is not of good moral character and reputation in the community in which the person resides. 
(3)	Fitness for conduct of business. To a person who by reason of reputation, character or mental or physical capacity is not, in the judgment of the city council, a fit or qualified person to conduct such a business. 
(4)	Criminal convictions related to alcohol. To a person found by the city council to have been guilty of the violation of any federal, state or local law or regulation respecting the manufacture, possession or sale of any alcoholic beverage, or who has forfeited a bond to appear in court to answer charges for any such violation. 
(5)	Other criminal convictions. When the applicant, or any employee of the applicant has been convicted of a felony or of a violation of the laws or regulations of any state or political subdivision relating to the use or sale of drugs or alcoholic beverages or has been convicted of a misdemeanor involving the use of firearms, theft, violence or a crime of moral turpitude. The forfeiture of bond or collateral or a plea of nolo contendere or a plea of guilty shall be considered a conviction for the purpose of this section. 
(6)	Applicability to partnerships. To a partnership, if any member of the partnership is disqualified under this section. 
(7)	Applicability to corporations. To a corporation, if any officer, stockholder, manager or director thereof would not be eligible to receive a license hereunder for any reason other than nonresidence in this county. 
(8)	Managers and agents. To a person whose place of business is conducted by a manager or agent, unless the manager or agent possesses the same qualifications as required of the license holder. 
(9)	Previously licensed persons. To a person who is the previous holder of an alcoholic beverage license and is, in the judgment and discretion of the city council, an unfit person to have a license because of the manner in which the person conducted business thereunder as to the necessity for unusual police observation and inspection in order to prevent the violation of any laws or regulations relating to the business. 
(10)	Unsuitable location. For a location: 
a.	Not suitable in the judgment and discretion of the city council because of traffic congestion, general character of the neighborhood, or by reason of the effect which such an establishment would have on the adjacent and surrounding properties or on the neighborhood. 
b.	Within an area where, in the judgment of the city council, the number of alcoholic beverage licenses already granted makes it contrary to the public interest and welfare of the citizens of the city. 
c.	At which the operation of the proposed establishment would be in violation of the zoning laws of the city. 
d.	At which a previous alcoholic beverage license has been denied, revoked or suspended, and where, in the judgment of the city council, the problems which have arisen from the operation of an alcoholic beverage license at the location indicate that it is not in the best interest of public health, safety, welfare or morals that the sale of alcoholic beverages be permitted at the location. 
e.	That fails to meet state and local fire and health codes. 
f.	Within 300 feet of a location at which an alcoholic beverage license is in effect, except for locations that already have a bona fide private club license and except for locations operated as a hotel as hereinafter defined; provided, however, that this subsection shall only apply to applicants for an alcoholic beverage license for consumption on the premises. For purposes of this subsection, the term "hotel" shall mean a building, or a portion of a building, including any motel, motor hotel, auto court or inn, containing guestrooms, which is occupied or is intended or designed for occupancy by guests, and which serves food, as part of its business, to guests or to members of the general public on a daily basis. 
(11)	License would violate law. When the granting of the license would constitute a violation of state law or regulation. 
(12)	Past due alcoholic beverage fees. To any person who has past due alcoholic beverage fees owed to the city. 
(13)	False statements. To any person who has made any false statement on an application for a license under this article, or any previous application for a license under this article. 
(14)	Family relationship. To any person to which the applicant, or any partner, officer, stockholder or director of the applicant is related within the first degree of consanguinity and affinity as computed according to the canon law, to any person who has been previously denied a license or had a license revoked or suspended, if the previous applicant or holder of a license has any ownership interest in the applicant's business. 
(15)	Managers of former licensees. To a person who was a manager of a previous license holder, whose license was denied, revoked or suspended, if the person was the manager of the license holder at the time that any act occurred which formed the basis for the denial, revocation or suspension. 
(16)	License previously denied. To a person who has previously had a license denied, revoked or suspended or was a partner, officer, director or stockholder of a previous license holder, whose license was denied, revoked or suspended. 
(17)	Ineligibility of owner, lessor, or lessee. To an owner, lessor or lessee of the premises where the business is to be located, where an owner, lessor or lessee of the premises or any partner, officer, stockholder or director of an owner, lessor or lessee of the premises where the business is to be located would not be eligible to receive a license hereunder for any reason other than nonresidency in this county. 
(18)	Sanitary facilities. For premises not containing sanitary facilities as required by city code. 
(19)	Prior application denied. To any person or entity for any location with respect to which a prior application has been submitted and denied, withdrawn or otherwise disposed of within the preceding 30 days. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, §§ 3-32, 10-33) 
State Law reference— Local discretion and due process as to grant or suspension of licenses, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-2. 
Sec. 10-37. - Application. 
Applications for licenses to sell alcoholic beverages of any kind shall be made to the city clerk and treasurer in writing on forms furnished by the city clerk and treasurer. They shall be signed by the applicant if an individual, by all partners if a partnership, or by a duly authorized agent if a corporation, and verified by oath or affidavit. All applications shall contain the following statements and information: 
(1)	Individual identification. The name, age and address of the applicant in case of an individual; in case of a partnership, the general partners or persons entitled to share in the profits thereof, their ages and addresses; in the case of a corporation, the names, ages and addresses of all the officers and stockholders. 
(2)	Business location. The location and description of the premises or place of business that is to be operated under the license. 
(3)	Previous applications. A statement of whether the applicant or any member of the partnership, or any officer or stockholder of the corporation, has made application at any previous time for any alcoholic beverage license in the city, and the disposition of the application. 
(4)	Criminal history. Whether any of the persons signing the application, or if a corporation, any of the officers or stockholders, have ever been convicted of a crime other than for violation of traffic laws. 
(5)	Prior license revocation. Whether a previous license issued to the applicant by any state or subdivision thereof or by the federal government has been revoked, and the reason therefor. 
(6)	Financial interest. Whether any other person is to be interested directly or indirectly in the profits or losses or both of the proposed business. 
(7)	Residency information. The length of residence of the applicant, or members of the partnership, or officers, directors and stockholders of the corporation, in the city, and if the residence is less than one year prior to the date of application, the last prior place of residence of the parties. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-33) 
Sec. 10-38. - Fingerprinting. 
Any applicant for a license to be issued pursuant to this article shall accompany the application with two complete sets of fingerprints of the applicant and applicant's manager, if the regular operations of the business will be conducted by one other than the applicant; if the applicant is a partnership, of all partners of the partnership; if the applicant is a corporation, of all officers and directors of the corporation. The foregoing provisions shall apply to transfers of licenses, to changes in partners, officers or directors of corporations. The fingerprints shall be taken by the police department on forms to be provided by the department and the applicant shall pay a fee in the amount established by the city council for each individual fingerprinted. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-34) 
State Law reference— Fingerprints of applicants to be furnished, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-2. 
Sec. 10-39. - Designation of corporate agent. 
All applications for alcoholic beverage licenses required by this article shall name in the application one or more persons resident in the state and county as the agent and representative of the corporation to receive all communications, notices, service of process or other papers or documents on behalf of the corporation in connection with the issuance, holding, suspension, revocation or other action with respect to any such license. The application shall give the mailing address of the person and the mailing to any such person at the address of any notice required to be given under this article shall be sufficient notice to the corporation. If any such person shall cease to be a resident of the state and county, another person shall immediately be appointed in writing in such person's place, and written notice shall be given to the city stating the name and address of the new agent. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-35) 
Sec. 10-40. - When applications due. 
All applications for alcoholic beverage licenses shall be filed with the city clerk prior to December 1 of the particular year of filing. Applications for alcoholic beverage licenses submitted to the city clerk between December 1 and December 31 shall not be considered by the council until the first regularly scheduled meeting in the following January. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-36) 
Sec. 10-41. - False statements. 
The making of any untrue or misleading statement in the application for an alcoholic beverage license shall be sufficient cause of the refusal, suspension, revocation or cancellation of the license by the city council. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-37) 
Sec. 10-42. - Notice for distilled spirits license. 
No application for a distilled spirits license shall be acted upon by the city council until the applicant shall have run a notice of the application in a newspaper published in the county, at least ten days prior to the meeting of the city council at which the application is to be presented and considered. The notice shall contain the names of all persons named in the application, and the location of the proposed business. The notice shall not be required from an existing license holder making application for the renewal of an existing distilled spirits license at the same location. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-38) 
Sec. 10-43. - Fees—Imposed; credits. 
(a)	Fee to accompany application. All applications for alcoholic beverage licenses shall be accompanied either by lawful money of the United States, certified check or cashier's check, payable to the city for the proper amount of the license fee. In the event that the license is refused, the same shall be returned to the applicant. 
(b)	Credit for prior license. Any present retail dealer, package only license holder who is approved for a mixed drink license and no longer desires to continue sales by the package only, may turn in the person's retail dealer, package only license and receive a pro rata credit towards the purchase of the mixed drinks license of mixed drinks, bona fide private club license. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, §§ 3-39, 3-41) 
State Law reference— Maximum fees for municipal liquor license, O.C.G.A. § 3-4-50. 
Sec. 10-44. - Same—Proration. 
Any person who is doing business or begins to do business at any time after January 1 and before July 1 shall pay the full annual license fee. Any person who begins to do business on or after July 1 shall pay one-half of the annual license fee unless otherwise provided. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-40) 
Sec. 10-45. - Investigation. 
Upon receipt by the city treasurer of any application for an alcoholic beverage license, or for the transfer of any license, the officer shall forward the same to the chief of police for investigation. The chief, following the investigation, shall either approve or disapprove the application, and shall attach thereto the entire police record of every person named in the application. The chief of police shall forward the application with the chief's recommendation to the city council. The city council shall approve or disapprove the issuance of the license. An investigation fee in the amount determined by the city council shall accompany the application; it shall not be refundable. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-42) 
Sec. 10-46. - Bond required. 
(a)	Amount of bond. Before any license for spirituous liquors is granted, the applicant must file with the city treasurer a corporate surety bond in a surety company licensed to do business in the state, conditioned to pay all taxes due the state in amounts as follows: 
(1)	Manufacturers ..... $4,000.00 
(2)	Wholesalers ..... $3,000.00 
(3)	Retailers ..... $2,500.00 
(b)	Approval by council. The bonds are to be approved by the city council and shall be executed on forms that may be prescribed by the city council. 
(c)	Bond conditions. The bonds shall be conditioned, among other things, that the applicant when granted a license to sell distilled liquors, shall pay all sums due to the city and comply with all the rules and regulations governing the sale of spirituous liquors and the other conditions as the city council may require in its rules and regulations. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-43) 
Sec. 10-47. - Licenses issued with special conditions. 
Any alcoholic beverage license issued by the city council may contain certain special conditions that the license holder will have to meet prior to or during the term the alcoholic beverage license is in effect. In the event the special terms and conditions are not met by the license holder, the license issued with the special terms and conditions may be suspended or revoked, or denied when the license holder seeks a renewal of the license. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-44) 
Sec. 10-48. - Manufacturer's location restricted. 
A manufacturer's license in any category issued under the provisions of this article will entitle the licensee to manufacture only the alcoholic beverage for which the license is issued, at one location only. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-45) 
Sec. 10-49. - Wholesaler's activities restricted. 
A wholesale dealer's license in any category issued under the provisions of this article will entitle the licensee to sell only the alcoholic beverage for which the license is issued, and only in the original unbroken container, to persons holding a retail license for the sale of that alcoholic beverage, for the purpose of resale only. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-46) 
Sec. 10-50. - Package dealers. 
(a)	Permitted sales; unopened containers. A retail dealer (sale by package only) license in any category issued under the provisions of this article will entitle the licensee to sell only the alcoholic beverage for which the license is issued, at one location only, and only in the original and unopened container. It shall not permit the opening of containers in the package store where sold, and shall not permit the drinking of the contents of the containers in the package store where sold. All spirituous liquors possessed by a licensee shall be kept in the package store. 
(b)	Entrances and exits. No retailer's place of business shall have more than one entrance, which must open on a public street, and the place of business shall have no other entrance except as approved by state laws, and shall contain no vestibule, closet, booth, room or other place where persons may consume alcoholic beverages. 
(c)	Vicinity to other businesses. The place of business operated under this license shall not be operated in conjunction with or open into or have access to or from any lunchroom, dining room, dance hall or store. The windows in the retail place of business shall not be obstructed or obscured, but shall be so arranged that a passerby on the street can view the premises of the retailer by looking through windows opening on the street. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-47) 
Sec. 10-51. - Package and consumption on-premises malt beverage dealers. 
A malt beverage retail dealer license (package and for consumption on premises) issued under the provisions of this article will entitle licensee to sell at one location malt beverages to consumers to take out or to consume on the premises. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-48) 
Sec. 10-52. - Package malt beverage dealers. 
A malt beverage retail dealer license (package only) issued under the provisions of this article will entitle the licensee to sell at one location malt beverages only in the unopened container, and will not authorize or permit the drinking of the contents on the premises where sold. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-49) 
Sec. 10-53. - Transferability. 
All alcoholic beverage licenses shall be personal to the licensee to whom issued. Upon proper application, the city council may permit the license to be transferred upon payment of a transfer fee equal to one-half the original license fee, provided that the transferee meets all of the qualifications which would have been required had the transferee been an applicant for an alcoholic beverage license. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-50) 
Sec. 10-54. - Death of license holder. 
Upon the death of any license holder, the person's personal representatives or heirs may continue to operate under the license for the balance of the year without the payment of any fee, if otherwise qualified as license holders, or the license may be transferred to a qualified transferee within 30 days after the date of death of the license holder upon payment of the transfer fee referenced in section 10-53. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-50) 
Sec. 10-55. - Sale of interest by licensee. 
Where the license holder is a partnership or corporation, one or more partners, or one or more stockholders, as the case may be, it or they may withdraw from the partnership or the corporation in favor of one or more of the partners or stockholders who were partners or stockholders at the time of the issuance of the license. The sale by a partner or a stockholder of the person's interest in the partnership or the corporation to a person who is not at the time of the sale already a partner or a stockholder shall constitute a ground for revocation of the license unless the new partner or stockholder is a person qualified to hold a license, and unless the transaction is approved by the city council. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-51) 
Sec. 10-56. - Change of location. 
The location named in the licensee's application shall not be changed without permission and approval of the city council upon written application made therefor. Approvals as to change of location shall be at the discretion of the city council. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-52) 
Sec. 10-57. - Duration of license; fee refunds. 
No license shall be issued under this article for less than a calendar year, or the remainder thereof. In case of the revocation, suspension or surrender of the license before the expiration of the calendar year, the holder thereof shall not be entitled to receive any refund. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-54) 
Sec. 10-58. - Expiration of license. 
All alcoholic beverage licenses shall expire at 12:00 a.m. on December 31 of the year in which issued. All applications for a renewal of the license for the ensuing year shall be treated as applications for new licenses, except that they need not be advertised as required by this article. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-55) 
Sec. 10-59. - Days and hours of sale. 
(a)	Sunday sales. No person may sell or offer to sell any distilled spirits, wine or malt beverages on Sundays. 
(b)	Election days. The sale of any distilled spirits, wine or malt beverages is specifically authorized on election days. 
(c)	Package sales. No retail sales of spirituous liquors or distilled spirits for off-the-premises consumption shall be made in the city, except between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 11:00 p.m. 
(d)	By the drink sales. No retail sales of spirituous liquors or distilled spirits by the drink, or malt beverages or wine shall be made in the city in any establishment licensed for on-the-premises consumption, except between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 1:30 a.m. the following day, except that on Saturday, no sales of such alcoholic beverages shall be made after 12:00 midnight. Additionally, it shall be the responsibility of licensee's agent or employee to see that all patrons are out of the premises within 30 minutes after the time prescribed for closing; provided, however, in the case of licensed restaurants, motels and bona fide private clubs, the establishments may be kept open for business after times provided in this section, but no mixed drinks, malt beverages or wine may be sold to the public after times stated herein. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-15) 
State Law reference— Municipal authority to prohibit Sunday sales, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-7; sale of alcoholic beverages on Sundays and election days, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-20. 
Sec. 10-60. - Grounds for revocation. 
The following shall be grounds for the suspension or revocation of an alcoholic beverage license. Whether the grounds exist shall be determined by the city council at its sole discretion. 
(1)	The violation by the license holder or license holder's employee of any federal, state or local law or ordinance relating to the use and sale of drugs or alcoholic beverage or involving the use of firearms, theft, violence or a crime of moral turpitude. The determination of whether any such violation has occurred shall be made by the city council, and actual conviction in a court for the offense shall not be necessary in order to suspend or revoke the license. 
(2)	The failure of the license holder or license holder's employee to report promptly to the police department any violation of law or municipal ordinance, breach of the peace, disturbance or altercation, occurring inside the premises, or the removal by the license holder or license holder's employees of any customer from inside the premises. 
(3)	Any conduct on the part of the license holder or license holder's employee contrary to the public welfare, safety, health or morals of the citizens of the city. 
(4)	Operating or conducting the business on the licensed premises in a manner contrary to the public welfare, safety, health or morals of the citizens of the city, or in the manner as to constitute a nuisance. 
(5)	All licenses are issued subject to revocation or suspension if the fingerprint records accompanying the application reveal past criminal activity on the part of any applicant or other person whose fingerprints are required by this article to be furnished with the application. 
(6)	Upon the business or the operation or location thereof, or the owner or any person connected therewith, ceasing to meet any of the qualifications for the issuance of a license as stated in this article. 
(7)	The failure of the license holder or license holder's employees to keep the licensed premises free and clear of any disturbances of the peace, loud or boisterous conduct, lewd, obscene or immoral entertainment, violation of any federal, state or local law or ordinance relating to the use and sale of drugs or alcoholic beverages or involving the use of firearms, theft, violence or a crime of moral turpitude. The determination of whether the license holder or license holder's employee has violated this section shall be made by the city council; actual conviction in a court for any offense shall not be necessary in order to suspend or revoke the license. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-58) 
Sec. 10-61. - Procedure for denial, suspension or revocation of license. 
(a)	Notice to applicant or license holder. After the city council shall deny any application for a license or for the transfer of any license, or shall suspend or revoke any existing license, the applicant or license holder, as the case may be, shall be given notice in writing with the reasons therefor stated. 
(b)	Request for hearing. Any applicant or license holder aggrieved by the decision of the city council shall have the right to request, within ten days after receipt of notice, a hearing on the decision. 
(c)	Scheduling and notice of hearing. Upon receipt by the city council of a request for the hearing, a hearing shall be scheduled within 20 working days and the applicant or license holder, as the case may be, shall be notified of the date, time and place of the hearing. 
(d)	Conduct of hearing; evidence. At the hearing, the licensee or applicant shall have the right to appear in person and by attorney, and to have witnesses appear in the appellant's behalf, and to cross examine opposing witnesses. The witnesses shall testify under oath and technical rules of evidence shall not apply. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-59) 
Secs. 10-62—10-81. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - EXCISE TAXES 

Sec. 10-82. - On malt beverages. 
(a)	Amount of tax. The city has levied and imposed upon all wholesale dealers selling malt beverages within the city specific excise taxes as follows: 
(1)	Bottles, cans, containers. Five cents per 12-ounce container or any portion thereof so as to graduate the tax on bottles, cans and containers of various sizes of malt beverages sold by each wholesale dealer within the city. 
(2)	Tap or draft beer. Six dollars on tap or draft beer for each container sold, as hereinafter specified, containing not more than 15½ gallons, and at a like rate for fractional parts where the beverage is sold in or from a barrel or bulk container, the beverage being commonly known as tap or draft beer. 
(b)	Payment of tax. Each wholesale dealer selling malt beverages within the city shall file a report by the tenth day of each month following the preceding calendar month setting out the exact quantities of malt beverage, by size and type container, constituting a beginning and ending inventory for the month sold within the city. Each such wholesale dealer shall remit excise taxes due to the city on the tenth day of the month next succeeding the calendar month in which the sales were made. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-16) 
State Law reference— Local excise taxes on malt beverages, O.C.G.A. § 3-5-80 et seq. 
Sec. 10-83. - On wine. 
(a)	Amount of tax. The city has imposed and levied the following specific excise tax upon all retail dealers in wine within the city excise taxes as follows: 
(1)	Five cents on each one-half pint bottle or container. 
(2)	Ten cents on each one pint bottle or container. 
(3)	Twenty-one cents on each one quart bottle or container or on bottle or container known as a fifth. 
(4)	Twenty-two cents on each liter bottle or container. 
(5)	Forty-two cents for each one-half gallon jug or bottle or container. 
(6)	Eighty-three cents on each one gallon jug or container. 
(7)	Eighty-three cents per gallon of wine in other containers. 
(b)	Collection and payment. At the time of delivery of the wine for sale to the retail dealer, the wholesale dealer shall collect from the retail dealer the amount of the taxes the retail dealer is obligated for under this section, and the wholesale dealer shall pay the tax collected to the city treasurer on or before the 20th day of the month following delivery of the wine to the retail dealer and send an accurate record of all wine sold the previous month with the payment. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-17) 
State Law reference— Local excise taxes on wine, O.C.G.A. § 3-6-60. 
Sec. 10-84. - On distilled spirits for sale by package. 
(a)	Amount of tax. The city has levied and imposed upon all retail dealers of distilled spirits for sale by the package within the city an excise tax computed at the rate of $0.22 per liter or pro rata portion thereof upon all distilled spirits for sale by the package within the city. 
(b)	Collection and payment. At the time of delivery of the distilled spirits for sale by the package, the wholesale dealer shall collect from the retail dealer the amount of the taxes the retail dealer is obligated for under this section, and the wholesale dealer shall pay the tax collected to the city treasurer on or before the 20th of the month following delivery of distilled spirits for sale by the package and send an accurate record of all distilled spirits sold the previous month with the payment. This excise tax shall apply only to retail dealers of distilled spirits for sale by the package within the city and shall not apply to holders of any type of mixed drink license issued by the city. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-18) 
State Law reference— Local excise taxes on distilled spirits package sales, O.C.G.A. § 3-4-80. 
Sec. 10-85. - Identifying marks. 
No decal, stamp or other identifying mark shall be required on alcoholic beverages sold in the city. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-16(b)) 
Sec. 10-86. - Taxes are in addition to license fees. 
The excise tax provided for herein shall be in addition to any license fee, tax or charge that may now or in the future be imposed upon the business of selling alcoholic beverages at retail or wholesale within the city. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-16(c)) 
Sec. 10-87. - Penalties for late payment. 
The failure to make a timely report and remittance shall render a licensee liable for a penalty equal to 20 percent of the total amount due during the first 30-day period following the date the report and remittance were due and a further penalty of ten percent of the amount of the remittance for each successive 30-day period or any portion thereof during which the report and remittance are not filed. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-16(d)) 
Sec. 10-88. - Penalty for false or fraudulent reports. 
The filing of a false or fraudulent report shall render the licensee making the report liable for a penalty equal to 50 percent of the amount of the remittance that would be required under an accurate and truthful report. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-16(d)) 
Secs. 10-89—10-111. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - PROHIBITED ACTS 

Sec. 10-112. - Public nuisance; disturbing the peace. 
It shall be unlawful for the holder of any license issued under the provisions of this chapter to permit any disturbance of the peace or obscenity or any lewd, immoral or improper entertainment, conduct or practices in the licensed premises or to operate the business carried on in the licensed premises in such a manner as to constitute a nuisance. It shall be unlawful for any licensee, or licensee's agent or employee to fail to report to the police department any disturbance that occurs immediately outside the licensed premises or in the parking facilities, of which any of them have knowledge. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-57(a)-(b)) 
Sec. 10-113. - Hiring persons with criminal convictions. 
It shall be unlawful for any licensed establishment to employ any person who has been convicted of, entered a plea to, or has otherwise been found guilty of a felony, a misdemeanor involving moral turpitude or alcoholic beverage violation. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-57(c)) 
Sec. 10-114. - Failing to assist law enforcement officers. 
It shall be unlawful for any licensee, or licensee's agent or employee to fail to assist any law enforcement officer in the performance of the person's duty while the officer is on a licensed premises. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-57(f)) 
Sec. 10-115. - Refusal to admit law enforcement officers. 
It shall be unlawful to refuse to grant law enforcement officers admission to any licensed premises at any time upon the verbal request of any law enforcement officer who displays proper identification for the purpose of inspecting the premises to ensure compliance with this chapter. It shall be unlawful to refuse to open any cabinet, storage room or any other area within the licensed premises at the request of such officers. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-57(g)) 
Sec. 10-116. - Advertising restricted. 
It shall be unlawful for the holder of any alcoholic beverage license to advertise in any news media, or by any other means, the fact that alcoholic beverages may be purchased at the establishment except as permitted by state law and by regulations duly promulgated thereunder. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-56) 
Sec. 10-117. - Proximity to school or church. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or offer to sell any distilled spirits, wine or malt beverage within the prohibited distances to a church building, school building, educational building, school grounds or college campus as set out in the Georgia Alcoholic Beverage Code, O.C.G.A. § 3-1-1 et seq. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-5) 
Sec. 10-118. - Furnishing to minors. 
(a)	Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Proper identification means any document issued by a governmental agency containing a description of the person, such as the person's photograph or other written description, and giving the person's date of birth, and includes, without being limited to, a passport, military identification card or driver's license. 
(b)	Prohibited. It shall be unlawful for any person holding an alcoholic beverage license or any other person, or any licensee's agent or employee, to sell, or give away, or permit the sale of or gift of any alcoholic beverage to any person under the age specified by state law, except for medical purposes pursuant to a prescription given by a physician duly authorized to practice medicine in this state, or in connection with a religious ceremony, or in the home with parental consent. 
(c)	Proper identification required; defense. No person shall be convicted under this section if the person has been furnished with the proper identification showing the person who is being furnished alcoholic beverages is over the age required by state law. 
(d)	Prohibited entry; duty of licensee. It shall be the duty and responsibility of the licensee, and licensee's agent or employee, to inspect the identification of all patrons to ensure that no person is allowed to enter the premises where entry is prohibited. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-10) 
State Law reference— Furnishing alcoholic beverages to minors, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-23. 
Sec. 10-119. - Consumption, possession by minors. 
Except as hereinafter provided, it shall be unlawful for any person under the age specified by state law to purchase or possess any alcoholic beverages except for medical purposes pursuant to the prescription of a physician duly licensed to practice medicine in this state, or in connection with a religious ceremony, or in the home with parental consent. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-11) 
State Law reference— Unlawful possession by minors of alcoholic beverages, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-23.1. 
Sec. 10-120. - Acquiring for minors. 
(a)	Prohibited. No person shall knowingly and intentionally act as an agent or otherwise purchase or acquire any alcoholic beverage for or on behalf of any person under the age required by state law, or otherwise procure or furnish to any person under the age required by state law any alcoholic beverage, except for medical purposes under the prescription of a physician duly licensed under the laws of the state. 
(b)	Duty of licensee to report. It shall be the duty and responsibility of the licensee, and licensee's agent or employee, to report known or suspected violations of this section to the city police department. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-12) 
Sec. 10-121. - Employment of minors; entering licensed premises. 
(a)	Employment prohibited; exceptions. No licensee shall allow or require a person in the licensee's employment under the age required by state law to dispense, serve, sell or take an order for any alcoholic beverage; provided, however, the provisions of this section shall not prohibit persons under the age required by state law who are employed in supermarkets, convenience stores, breweries or drug stores from selling or handling alcoholic beverages which are sold for consumption off the premises. 
(b)	Prohibited entry; exceptions. It shall be unlawful for any licensee or licensee's agent or employee to allow any person who is not authorized by law to purchase, possess or consume alcoholic beverages to enter a licensed premises; provided, however, the provisions of this subsection shall not apply to restaurants, convenience stores, drug stores, supermarkets or bona fide private clubs. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-13) 
State Law reference— Persons under 18 not allowed to serve, sell, or take orders for alcoholic beverages, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-24. 
Sec. 10-122. - Misrepresentation of age. 
(a)	Prohibited.
