It shall be unlawful for any person in any manner whatsoever to falsely misrepresent that the person is of the age required by state law to purchase alcoholic beverages, or that the person is of the age required by state law and in military service for the purpose of buying or possessing alcoholic beverages in violation of this chapter, and the penalty for the misrepresentation shall be as provided in section 1-10. 
(b)	Duty of licensee to report. It shall be the duty and responsibility of the licensee, his agent or employee, to promptly report any person misrepresenting his age for the purposes of purchasing alcoholic beverages to the city police department. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-14) 
Sec. 10-123. - Public intoxication; use of drugs. 
(a)	Prohibited. It shall be unlawful for any person to be intoxicated or under the influence of any narcotic, narcotic derivative, stimulant, depressant, hallucinogenic or other type of drug or medicine, now or hereafter controlled by state law, or any other intoxicant type material not prescribed and administered according to state law; to inject or administer orally any narcotic, narcotic derivative, stimulant, depressant, hallucinogenic or other type of drug or medicine controlled by state law, or not prescribed and administered according to law, or to take or use any other intoxicant type materials not according to law, upon the streets, lanes, roads and alleys in the city or in any motor vehicle, house, premises, building or enclosure in the city. 
(b)	Disorderly conduct. The same is hereby defined and declared to be disorderly conduct and injurious to the public morals, safety and welfare of the citizens of the city. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-7) 
State Law reference— Public drunkenness, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-41. 
Sec. 10-124. - Drinking or possessing alcoholic beverages in park, playground or school. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to drink or possess any alcoholic beverage upon real property of the city that is used as a city park, playground or school. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-8) 
State Law reference— Possession of alcoholic beverages on school grounds prohibited, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-21.1. 
Sec. 10-125. - Opened containers. 
It shall be unlawful within the city for any person to drink or have in the person's possession in opened containers any alcoholic beverage, the possession of which has been legalized under the laws of the state, except on the premises of private dwelling houses or inside a building; provided, that any building that is a public place of business must be duly licensed and authorized to sell and serve alcoholic beverages. 
(Ord. of 7-10-1995, § 3-9) 
Chapter 14 - ANIMALS AND FOWL[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Animals, O.C.G.A. § 4-1-1 et seq.; animal protection, O.C.G.A. § 4-11-1 et seq.; rabies control, O.C.G.A. § 31-19-1. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 14-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Animal control officer means an employee of the police department of the city whose duties specifically include enforcement of the provisions of this chapter. 
Dangerous dog means any dog that, according to the records of an appropriate authority: 
(1)	Inflicts a severe injury on a human being without provocation, on public or private property; or 
(2)	Aggressively bites, attacks or endangers the safety of humans without provocation after the dog has been classified as a potentially dangerous dog after the owner has been notified of such classification. 
Nuisance means an act or situation caused by or contributed to by an animal with or without the permission of the animal's owner or keeper, which act or situation substantially interferes with the rights of citizens to enjoyment of life or property or unreasonably annoys humans or endangers the life or health of persons or other animals. Such a nuisance shall include, but shall not be limited to the following acts by an animal: 
(1)	Molesting or threatening to molest pedestrians; 
(2)	Chasing vehicles; 
(3)	Causing loss or damage to the person or property of someone other than the owner or keeper of the animal; or 
(4)	Continually and repeatedly howling, barking, whining or otherwise making noises which cause unreasonable annoyance, disturbance or discomfort to neighbors and others. 
Owner means any natural persons or any legal entity, including but not limited to, a corporation, partnership, firm or trust, owning, possessing, harboring, keeping, or having custody or control of a dog within the territorial boundaries of the city. 
Potentially dangerous dog means any dog that has, without provocation, bitten a human being on public or private property. 
Proper closure means an enclosure for keeping a dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog, while on the owner's property, securely confined indoors or in a securely enclosed and locked pen, fence, or structure suitable to prevent the entry of young children and designed to prevent the dog from escaping. Any such pen or structure shall have secure sides and a secure top, and, if the dog is enclosed within a fence, all sides of the fence shall be of sufficient height, and the bottom of the fence shall be constructed or secured in such a manner so as to prevent the dog's escape either from over or from under the fence. Any such enclosure shall also provide protection from the elements for the dog. 
Rabies control officer means an employee of the county board of health whose specific duties include enforcement of the rabies control rules and regulations of the county. 
Records of an appropriate authority means records of any state, county, or municipal law enforcement agency, records of any county or municipal animal control agency; records of any county board of health; records of any federal, state, or local court; or records maintained by the animal control officer pursuant to this chapter 
Severe injury means any physical injury that results in broken bones or disfiguring lacerations requiring multiple sutures or cosmetic surgery or a physical injury that results in death. 
Secs. 14-2—14-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ANIMAL CONTROL 

Sec. 14-21. - City designated bird sanctuary. 
The entire area embraced within the corporate limits of the city is hereby designated as a bird sanctuary. 
Sec. 14-22. - Birds and wild fowl protected; exception. 
It shall be unlawful to trap, shoot or attempt to shoot or molest in any manner any bird or wild fowl or to rob bird nests or wild fowl nests; provided, however, if vandal birds are found to be congregating in such numbers in a particular locality that they constitute a nuisance or menace to health or property in the opinion of the proper health authorities of the city, such authority is authorized to approve the disposal of such birds. Any individual may prevent any vandal birds from destroying crops or fruit without the authority of the health officer. 
Sec. 14-23. - Hunting prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful to hunt within the city limits. 
Sec. 14-24. - Livestock and fowl prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful to have livestock or fowl in the city limits. 
Sec. 14-25. - Livestock running at large. 
(a)	Impoundment; redemption; fees. The police are required to seize and impound any livestock found at large in violation of section 14-24, and to safely keep the same until it shall be redeemed by its owner, upon the payment of a pound fee in the amount established by the city council for each head impounded, and all costs of care and feeding during impoundment. 
(b)	Sale of animals not redeemed. In case said livestock shall not be redeemed within five days from the date of its seizure, the police shall cause the same to be advertised and sold as an estray, as provided by the laws of the state, if the owner is unknown. But if the owner is known, and he shall fail to redeem such livestock within five days after notice of its impoundment, he shall be deemed guilty of an offense. 
State Law reference— Livestock running at large prohibited, O.C.G.A. § 4-3-3. 
Sec. 14-26. - Animal carcasses. 
No person shall deposit any carcass of any dead animal upon any ground, public or private, within the city. 
State Law reference— Disposal of diseased, disabled, or dead animals, O.C.G.A. § 4-5-1 et seq. 
Secs. 14-27—14-37. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - DOGS AND CATS[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Dogs, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-1 et seq. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Secs. 14-38—14-55. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - DOG CONFINEMENT AND CONTROL 

Sec. 14-56. - Restraint required. 
It shall be unlawful for the owner or keeper of any dog to allow the same to run upon the streets, sidewalks or alleys of the city, unless said dog is accompanied by its owner or other person having charge of said dog, in which event said dog must be tied with a cord or chain of sufficient strength to hold such dog. 
Sec. 14-57. - Control of females in heat. 
No person owning or having custody of any female dog shall permit such female dog off the premises of the owner or person having control of such dog when such dog shall be in heat, unless the same is under control and attached to a leash as herein provided. 
Sec. 14-58. - Duty of dog and cat owners. 
The owner and keeper of every dog and cat shall keep it from becoming a nuisance and from endangering or injuring any person. As a consequence thereof, it is the duty of every owner or keeper of any animal to exercise reasonable care and to take all reasonable steps and precautions necessary to protect persons, property, and animals from injury, loss, or damage that might be caused by or arise from the dog or cat's behavior, regardless of whether such behavior is motivated by mischievousness, playfulness or ferocity. 
Sec. 14-59. - Parental responsibility. 
If the owner or keeper of any animal is a minor, the parent or guardian of such minor shall be responsible for ensuring compliance with this section. 
Sec. 14-60. - Nuisance. 
If an animal is kept in such a manner as constitutes a nuisance as defined in this chapter or by state statute, a proceeding to abate the nuisance may be brought by the party aggrieved or the city. An animal found by the court to constitute a nuisance may be impounded by the city if the owner, after reasonable opportunity to do so, fails to abate the nuisance as ordered by the court. 
Secs. 14-61—14-78. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - VACCINATION AND REGISTRATION 

Sec. 14-79. - Adoption of county rules. 
All dogs and cats shall be inoculated against rabies in accordance with the procedures set forth in the rabies control rules and regulations of the county, as promulgated and from time to time amended by the county board of health, which by reference are expressly incorporated as part of this section as if fully set out herein. Violation of the adopted rules and regulations may be enforced by the rabies control officer in the municipal court of the city, upon citation, as an offense against the city. 
Sec. 14-80. - Vaccination tags. 
The numbered vaccination tag, issued by a licensed veterinarian upon inoculation, shall be attached to a collar or harness and worn by the animal at all times. 
Secs. 14-81—14-103. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - IMPOUNDMENT 

Sec. 14-104. - Dogs or cats running at large. 
Every dog found roaming or running free, whether tagged or untagged, shall be impounded; every tagged or untagged cat found roaming or running free shall be impounded. If a tagged animal is impounded, and it is found not to be registered or its current registration has expired, the owner may be cited for violation of this section. 
Sec. 14-105. - Care of impounded animals. 
All animals impounded by the city shall be held in a humane manner by the city or in accordance with an agreement between the city and some other entity as may from time to time be determined and established by action of the local government. 
Sec. 14-106. - Period of impoundment; fees. 
If a cat or dog is impounded for running at large or for creating a nuisance, the animal shall be retained and impounded for a period of not less than 48 hours unless previously claimed by the animal's owner, in which case said owner shall pay to the city clerk an impoundment fee and a daily boarding fee in the amount established by the city council, plus any veterinary or other incidental expenses associated with the proper care of the animal during the period of impoundment. If the dog or cat is not claimed within 48 hours, the city shall be authorized to dispose of the animal in a humane manner. 
Sec. 14-107. - Additional penalties. 
Nothing in this section relating to impoundment and fees charged in connection therewith shall limit the liability of the owner to the city for violation of this chapter. 
Secs. 14-108—14-127. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - DANGEROUS DOGS[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference— Dangerous dog control, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-20 et seq. 

Sec. 14-128. - Registration required. 
It shall be unlawful for an owner to have or possess within the city a dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog without a certificate of registration issued in accordance with this article. 
Sec. 14-129. - Report; investigation. 
Upon receiving a report of a dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog within the animal control officer's jurisdiction from a law enforcement agency, animal control agency, rabies control officer, or the county board of health, the animal control officer shall conduct such investigations and inquiries with regard to such report as may be necessary to carry out the provisions of this article. 
Sec. 14-130. - Classification; notice to owner. 
When the animal control officer classifies a dog as a dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog, and the dog is not registered as required by this article, notice shall be given to the dog's owner in writing, by certified mail, to the owner's last known address of such classification or reclassification. The notice shall be deemed complete upon mailing. 
Sec. 14-131. - Contents of notice. 
The notice to the owner shall meet the following requirements: 
(1)	Findings. The notice shall include a summary of the animal control officer's finding that formed the basis for the dog's classification as a dangerous or potentially dangerous dog. 
(2)	Date. The notice shall be dated. 
(3)	Notice of right to request hearing. The notice shall state that the owner, within 15 days after the date shown on the notice, has a right to request a hearing on the animal control officer's determination that the dog is a dangerous dog or a potentially dangerous dog before the governing authority. 
(4)	Effect of failure to request hearing. The notice shall state that if a hearing is not requested, the animal control officer's determination that the dog is a dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog will become effective for all purposes under this section on the day after the last day on which the owner has a right to request a hearing. 
Sec. 14-132. - Hearing procedure. 
(a)	Time for hearing. When the city receives a request for a hearing, it shall schedule such hearing within 30 days after receiving the request. 
(b)	Notice of hearing. The city shall notify the dog owner, in writing, by certified mail, of the date, time and place of the hearing. 
(c)	Conduct of hearing. At the hearing, the owner of the dog shall be given the opportunity to testify and present evidence, and in addition thereto, the city shall receive such other evidence and hear such other testimony as the city may find reasonably necessary to make a determination either to sustain, modify, or overrule the animal control officer's classification of the dog. 
(d)	Notice of determination; effective date. Within ten days after the date of the hearing, the city shall notify the owner in writing by certified mail of its determination on the matter. If such determination is that the dog is a dangerous dog or a potentially dangerous dog, the notice shall specify it is effective on the third day following the date of receipt by the owner. 
Sec. 14-133. - Requirements for registration. 
Subject to the requirements of this section, the animal control officer shall issue a certificate of registration to the owner of a dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog if the owner presents to the animal control officer or if the animal control officer finds sufficient evidence of: 
(1)	Proper enclosure. A proper enclosure to confine the dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog. 
(2)	Warning sign. The posting of the premises where the dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog is located with a clearly visible sign warning that there is a dangerous dog on the premises. The sign required to be posted must substantially conform to the design provided by the department of natural resources. 
(3)	Registration fee. Payment to the city of a fee in the amount established by the city council to defray the cost of administering and enforcing this section. 
(4)	Liability insurance. A policy of insurance in the amount of at least $15,000.00 issued by an insurer authorized to transact business within the state insuring the owner of the dog against liability for any personal injuries inflicted by the dangerous dog. 
(5)	Surety bond. A surety bond in the amount of $15,000.00 or more issued by a surety company authorized to transact business in the state, payable to any person or persons injured by the dangerous dog. 
Sec. 14-134. - Annual registration renewal. 
Certificates of registration shall be renewed on an annual basis. At the time of annual renewal of a certificate of registration, the animal control officer shall require evidence from the owner or make such investigation as may be necessary to verify that the dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog is continuing to be confined in a proper enclosure and that the owner is continuing to comply with all other provisions of this article. 
Sec. 14-135. - Compliance not guaranteed by city. 
Issuance of a certificate of registration or the renewal of a certificate of registration by the local government does not warrant or guarantee that the requirements specified in this article are maintained by the owner of a dangerous dog or a potentially dangerous dog on a continuous basis following the date of the issuance of the initial certificate of registration or following the date of any annual renewal of such certificate. 
Sec. 14-136. - Owner responsibility to notify city. 
The owner of a dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog shall notify the animal control officer within 24 hours if the dog is on the loose, is unconfined, has attacked a human, has died, or had been sold or donated. If the dog has been sold or donated, the owner shall also provide the name, address, and telephone number of the new owner of the dog. The owner of a dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog shall also notify the animal control officer if the owner is moving with the animal from the animal control officer's jurisdiction. 
Sec. 14-137. - Time for new residents to register. 
The owner of a dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog, who is a new resident of the city and the state, shall register the dog in the manner provided by this article within 30 days after becoming a resident. An owner who is a new resident of the city, but not of the state, shall register the dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog within ten days after becoming a resident of the city. 
Sec. 14-138. - Prohibited acts. 
(a)	Proper restraint required. It shall be unlawful for an owner of a dangerous or potentially dangerous dog to permit the dog to be outside a proper enclosure unless the dog is muzzled and restrained by a substantial chain or leash and is under the physical restraint of a responsible person. 
(b)	Warning sign required. It shall be unlawful for the owner of a dangerous dog to fail to post a warning sign on the premises where a dangerous dog is located in accordance with this article. 
Sec. 14-139. - Impoundment for violation. 
It shall be the duty of the animal control officer, and any person under his employ, to impound the dog if: 
(1)	The owner does not secure a certificate of registration in accordance with this article. 
(2)	The owner does not secure liability insurance or meet the bond requirement of this article. 
(3)	The owner does not keep the dog within a proper enclosure or permits the dog to roam or run free. 
Sec. 14-140. - Redemption of impounded dog. 
(a)	Compliance required; fees. Any dangerous or potentially dangerous dog impounded under the provisions of this article shall be returned to the owner upon the owner's compliance with the provisions of this article and upon payment of reasonable impoundment cost, as fixed by a schedule approved by the city, as from time to time amended. 
(b)	Notice to owner. Notice of impoundment under this section shall be given to the owner, in writing, by certified mail, at his last known address. This notice shall state that if the owner has not complied with the provisions of this article within 20 days from receipt of such notice, the dog shall be destroyed in an expeditiously and humane manner; provided, however, no dog shall have been destroyed under this section unless it has been held for a full 20 days, exclusive of the date of giving notice. 
Sec. 14-141. - Liability of owner. 
The owner of a dangerous dog or potentially dangerous dog shall be solely liable for any injury to or death of a person caused by such dog. 
Sec. 14-142. - Liability of city. 
Under no circumstances shall the city or any employee or official of the city that enforces or fails to enforce the provisions of this article be held liable for any damages to any person who suffers an injury inflicted by a dog that has been identified as being a dangerous or potentially dangerous dog, that the city has failed to identify as a dangerous or potentially dangerous dog, that has been identified as being a dangerous or potentially dangerous dog but has not been kept or restrained in the manner described in this article, or by a dangerous or potentially dangerous dog whose owner has not maintained insurance coverage or a surety bond as required in section 14-133. 
Chapter 18 - BUILDINGS AND BUILDING REGULATIONS 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 18-1—18-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - MINIMUM STANDARDS CODE 

Sec. 18-19. - Purpose and intent. 
The city declares it to be in the interest of public safety, health, and general welfare to adopt certain standard building, technical, mechanical, and maintenance codes, to facilitate property inspection by the city, the county, and the state related to construction and maintenance of buildings within the city. 
Sec. 18-20. - State minimum standards codes adopted. 
The city adopts by reference as if fully set forth herein, the following minimum standards codes as provided in O.C.G.A. § 8-2-20 and as published by the state department of community affairs: 
(1)	International Building Code, 2006 edition, with Georgia Amendments (2007). 
(2)	International Residential Code, 2006 edition, with Georgia Amendments (2007). 
(3)	International Plumbing Code, 2006 edition, with Georgia Amendments (2007). 
(4)	International Mechanical Code, 2006 edition, with Georgia Amendments (2007) and 2007 Errata for Georgia Amendments to the 2006 International Mechanical Code. 
(5)	International Fuel Gas Code, 2006 edition, with Georgia Amendments (2007). 
(6)	National Electrical Code, 2005 edition, with Georgia Amendments (2006). 
(7)	International Energy Conservation Code, 2000 edition, with Georgia Supplements and Amendments (2003), 2003 Errata for Georgia Supplements and Amendments to the 2000 International Energy Conservation Code, Supplements and Amendments (2005), 2005 Errata for Georgia Supplements and Amendments to the 2000 International Energy Conservation Code, Supplements and Amendments (2006), Supplements and Amendments (2007). 
(8)	International Property Maintenance Code, 2003 edition. 
(9)	International Existing Building Code, 2003 edition. 
(Ord. No. 589, § 5-1, 10-12-1998) 
Sec. 18-21. - Compliance required. 
No structure shall be constructed or altered, and no installation of gas, water, sewer, or other utility-related service shall be installed, except in compliance with the codes adopted in this article. All structures within the city shall be continuously maintained in compliance with the codes adopted in this article. 
Sec. 18-22. - Administration and enforcement. 
When reference is made in the codes adopted in this article to an enforcement official, it shall mean the city official or employee (public officer) who has duties corresponding to those of the official named in the code. 
(Ord. No. 589, § 5-3, 10-12-1998) 
Secs. 18-23—18-47. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - UNFIT BUILDINGS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 18-48. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Applicable codes means the applicable provisions of the codes adopted in article II of this chapter and any applicable county, state, or federal building or housing standards. 
Closing means causing a dwelling, building, or structure to be vacated and secured against unauthorized entry. 
Drug crime means an act that is a violation of the Georgia Controlled Substances Act, O.C.G.A. § 16-13-1 et seq. 
Dwellings, buildings, or structures means buildings or structures or parts thereof used and occupied for human habitation or commercial, industrial, or business uses, or intended to be so used, and includes any outhouses, improvements, and appurtenances belonging thereto or usually enjoyed therewith and also includes any building or structure of any design. The term "dwellings, buildings, or structures" shall not mean or include any farm, any building or structure located on a farm, or any agricultural facility or other building or structure used for the production, growing, raising, harvesting, storage, or processing of crops, livestock, poultry, or other farm products. 
Owner means the holder of the title in fee simple and every mortgagee of record. 
Parties in interest means: 
(1)	Persons in possession of said property and premises; 
(2)	Persons having of record in the county in which the dwelling, building, or structure is located any vested right, title, or interest in or lien upon the dwelling, building, or structure or the lot, tract, or parcel of real property upon which the structure is situated or upon which the public health hazard or general nuisance exists based upon a 50-year title examination conducted in accordance with the title standards of the State Bar of Georgia; 
(3)	Persons having paid an occupational tax to the governing authority for a location or office at the subject building or structure; or 
(4)	Persons having filed a property tax return with the governing authority as to the subject property, building, or structure. 
Public authority means any member of a governing authority who is in charge of any department or branch of the municipality relating to health, fire, or building regulations or to other activities concerning dwellings, buildings, or structures in the municipality. 
Public officer means the officer who is authorized by state law and by this chapter to exercise the powers prescribed by this article or any agent of such officer. 
Repair means altering or improving a dwelling, building, or structure so as to bring the structure into compliance with the applicable codes in the jurisdiction where the property is located and the cleaning or removal of debris, trash, and other materials present and accumulated which create a health or safety hazard in or about any dwelling, building, or structure. 
Resident means any person residing in the jurisdiction where the property is located on or after the date on which the alleged nuisance arose. 
Service means the connection or reconnection of water, sewer, electric, or sanitation services to any residential, commercial, or industrial building or structure. 
(Ord. No. 589, § 5-1, 10-12-1998; Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-1) 
Sec. 18-49. - Penalties. 
Persons violating this article shall be subject to penalties as provided in section 1-10. The owner or tenant of any building, structure, premises, or part thereof, and any architect, builder, contractor, agent, or person who commits, participates in, assists in, or maintains a violation may be found guilty of a separate offense and be subject to the same penalties. The penalties provided in this section are nonexclusive and in no way preclude or limit any other remedy available to the city under this Code or state law. 
(Ord. No. 589, § 5-5, 10-12-1998) 
Sec. 18-50. - Administration. 
The primary responsibility and authority for the enforcement of the provisions of this article shall be vested in the building inspector, or such inspector's duly authorized representative, who, for the purposes of this article, shall be deemed the public officer as more particularly defined in section 18-48. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-2) 
Sec. 18-51. - Compliance required for connection. 
No service shall be provided to any resident, commercial, or industrial building or structure within the city unless the building or structure conforms in all respects with the codes adopted pursuant to this article and any applicable county and state building or safety regulations. 
Sec. 18-52. - Defects rendering structure unfit. 
A dwelling, building, or structure is unfit for human habitation or is unfit for its current commercial, industrial, or business use if conditions exist in such building, dwelling, or structure that are dangerous or injurious to the health, safety, or morals of the occupants of the dwelling, building, or structure; the occupants of neighborhood dwellings, buildings, or structures; or other residents in the city. The conditions may include, but are not limited to, the following: 
(1)	Defects therein increasing the hazards of fire, accidents or other calamities; 
(2)	Lack of adequate ventilation, light, or sanitary facilities; 
(3)	Dilapidation; 
(4)	Disrepair; 
(5)	Structural defects; 
(6)	Uncleanliness; 
(7)	Exclusive of the foundation, if 33 percent or more of damage or deterioration of the supporting members, or 50 percent of the damage or deterioration of the nonsupporting enclosing or outside walls or coverings is present; 
(8)	Improperly distributed loads upon the floors or roofs in which the same are overloaded, or which have insufficient strength to be reasonably safe; 
(9)	Previous damage by fire, wind, vandalism, or other cause; 
(10)	Decayed, unsafe, unsanitary, or other such conditions likely to cause sickness or disease to occupants of such dwelling, building, or structure, or to the occupants of neighborhood dwellings, buildings, or structures; 
(11)	Inadequate means of ingress and egress, such as insufficient stairways, elevators, or fire escapes, so as to cause a danger to occupants or residents; 
(12)	Conditions that are otherwise unsafe, unsanitary, or dangerous to the health, morals, safety, or general welfare of the occupants or occupants of neighborhood dwellings, buildings, or structures, or other residents of the city; 
(13)	Dilapidation or disrepair to such an extent that portions of the dwelling, building, or structure may fall or cave in; 
(14)	Buildings existing in violation of any provision of any code previously adopted by the city, including, but not limited to, any building code and any fire prevention code, previously adopted; and 
(15)	Any conditions with respect to the dwelling, building, or structure that are described in section 202 of the Standard Unsafe Building Abatement Code. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-4(a)) 
Sec. 18-53. - Vacant and dilapidated structures. 
The public officer shall also be authorized to determine that a dwelling, building, or structure is vacant, dilapidated, and being used in connection with the commission of drug crimes upon personal observation by the public officer or upon the report of a law enforcement agency and evidence of drug crimes being committed at the location of such dwelling, building, or structure. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-4(b)) 
Sec. 18-54. - Duty of owner to maintain property. 
It is the duty of the owner of every dwelling, building, structure, or property within the municipal limits of the city to construct and maintain such dwelling, building, structure, or property in conformance with all applicable codes in force within the city and in conformance with such ordinances which regulate or prohibit activities on property and which declare it to be a public nuisance to construct or maintain any dwelling, building, structure, or property in violation of such codes or ordinances. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-5) 
Secs. 18-55—18-81. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - ENFORCEMENT[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Authority for adoption of ordinances enforcing nuisance of unfit buildings, O.C.G.A. § 41-2-9. 

Sec. 18-82. - Petition; notice; hearing. 
(a)	Complaint. Whenever a request is filed with the public officer by a public authority or by at least five residents of the municipality charging that any dwelling, building, structure, or property is: 
(1)	Unfit for human habitation or for commercial, industrial, or business use and not in compliance with applicable codes; 
(2)	Vacant and being used in connection with the commission of drug crimes; or 
(3)	Constitutes an endangerment to the public health or safety as a result of unsanitary or unsafe conditions; 
the public officer shall make an investigation or inspection of the specific dwelling, building, structure, or property. If the officer's investigation or inspection identifies that the dwelling, building, structure, or property satisfies the criteria stated in subsections (a)(1) through (a)(3) of this section, the public officer may issue a complaint in rem against the lot, tract, or parcel of real property on which such dwelling, building, or structure is situated or where such public health hazard or general nuisance exists. 
(b)	Summons; service. The public officer shall cause a summons and a copy of the complaint to be served on the owner and parties in interest in such dwelling, building, or structure. 
(c)	Contents of complaint. The complaint shall identify the subject real property by appropriate street address and official tax map reference, identify the owner and parties in interest, state with particularity the factual basis for the action, and contain a statement of the action sought by the public officer to abate the alleged nuisance. 
(d)	Contents of summons. The summons shall notify the owner and parties in interest that a hearing will be held before a court of competent jurisdiction at a date and time certain and at a place within the municipality where the property is located. The hearing shall be held not less than 15 days or more than 45 days after the filing of said complaint in the proper court. 
(e)	Answer and testimony of owner. The owner and parties in interest shall have the right to file an answer to the complaint and to appear in person or by attorney and offer testimony at the time and place fixed for hearing. 
(f)	Determination and order. If, after such notice and hearing, the court determines that the dwelling, building, or structure in question meets the criteria set forth in subsections (a)(1) through (a)(3) of this section, the court shall state in writing findings of fact in support of such determination and shall issue and cause to be served upon the owner, and any parties in interest that have answered the complaint or appeared at the hearing, an order: 
(1)	If the repair, alteration, or improvement of said dwelling, building, or structure can be made at a reasonable cost in relation to its present value, requiring the owner, within the time specified in the order, to repair, alter, or improve such dwelling, building, or structure so as to bring it into full compliance with the applicable codes relevant to the cited violation and, if applicable, to secure the structure so that it cannot be used in connection with the commission of drug crimes; or 
(2)	If the repair, alteration, or improvement of said dwelling, building, or structure in order to bring it into full compliance with applicable codes relevant to the cited violations cannot be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the its present value, requiring the owner, within the time specified in the order, to demolish and remove such dwelling, building, or structure and all debris from the property. 
(g)	Calculating cost to value comparison. 
(1)	For purposes of this section, the court shall make its determination of reasonable cost in relation to the present value of the dwelling, building, or structure without consideration of the value of the land on which the structure is situated; provided, however, that costs of the preparation necessary to repair, alter, or improve a structure may be considered. 
(2)	Income and financial status of the owner shall not be a factor in the court's determination. 
(3)	The present value of the structure and the costs of repair, alteration, or improvement may be established by affidavits of real estate appraisers with a state appraiser classification, qualified building contractors, or qualified building inspectors without the requirement that actual testimony be presented. 
(4)	Costs of repair, alteration, or improvement of the structure shall be the cost necessary to bring the structure into compliance with the applicable codes relevant to the cited violations in force in the jurisdiction. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-6(a)—(c)) 
Sec. 18-83. - Posting of structure. 
If the owner or other defendant fails to comply with an order to repair or demolish the dwelling, building, or structure, the public officer may cause such dwelling, building, or structure to be repaired, altered, or improved or to be vacated and closed or demolished. The public officer shall cause to be posted on the main entrance of the building, dwelling, or structure a placard with the following words: 
"This building is unfit for human habitation or commercial, industrial, or business use and does not comply with the applicable codes or has been ordered secured to prevent its use in connection with drug crimes or constitutes an endangerment to public health or safety as a result of unsanitary or unsafe conditions. The use or occupation of this building is prohibited and unlawful." 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-6(d)) 
Sec. 18-84. - Salvage of materials; distribution of proceeds. 
If the public officer has the structure demolished, reasonable effort shall be made to salvage reusable materials for credit against the cost of demolition. The proceeds of any moneys received from the sale of salvaged materials shall be used or applied against the cost of the demolition and removal of the structure, and proper records shall be kept showing application of sales proceeds. Any such sale of salvaged materials may be made without the necessity of public advertisement and bid. The public officer and governing authority are relieved of any and all liability resulting from or occasioned by the sale of any such salvaged materials, including, without limitation, defects in such salvaged materials 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-6(e)) 
Sec. 18-85. - Costs to be lien on property. 
The amount of the cost of demolition, including all court costs, appraisal fees, administrative costs incurred by the tax commissioner, and all other costs necessarily associated with the abatement action, including restoration to grade of the real property after demolition, shall be a lien against the real property upon which such cost was incurred. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-6(f)) 
Sec. 18-86. - Extensions of time. 
The court may, in its discretion, grant an extension of time within which to comply with any order entered by the court pursuant to this division, which extension shall be for a definite term and shall be in writing. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-7) 
Sec. 18-87. - Attachment of lien. 
(a)	Time of attachment. The lien provided for herein shall attach to the real property upon the filing of a certified copy of the order requiring repair, closure, or demolition in the office of the clerk of superior court in the county where the real property is located and shall relate back to the date of the filing of the lis pendens notice required by statute. 
(b)	Recording and indexing. The clerk of superior court shall record and index such certified copy of the order in the deed records of the county and enter the lien on the general execution docket. The lien shall be superior to all other liens on the property, except liens for taxes to which the lien shall be inferior, and shall continue in force until paid. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-8(a)) 
Sec. 18-88. - Collection; interest. 
After filing a certified copy of the order with the clerk of superior court, the public officer shall forward a copy of the order and a final statement of costs to the city clerk. It shall be the duty of the city clerk to collect the amount of the lien in conjunction with the collection of city ad valorem taxes on the property and to collect the amount of the lien as if it were a real property ad valorem tax, using all methods available for collecting real property ad valorem taxes; provided, however, that the limitation of O.C.G.A. § 48-4-78, which requires 12 months of delinquency before commencing a tax foreclosure shall not apply. The city clerk shall remit the amount collected to the city council. Thirty days after imposition of the lien, the unpaid lien amount shall bear interest and penalties in the same amount as applicable to interest and penalties on unpaid real property ad valorem taxes. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-8(a)) 
Sec. 18-89. - Waiver and release of lien. 
The city may waive and release any such lien imposed on property upon the owner of such property entering into a contract with the city agreeing to a timetable for rehabilitation of the real property or the dwelling, building, or structure on the property and demonstrating the financial means to accomplish such rehabilitation. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-8(b)) 
Sec. 18-90. - Service of notices and orders issued by public officer. 
Complaints issued by a public officer pursuant to this division shall be served in the following manner: 
(1)	Posting; service. In all cases, a copy of the complaint and summons shall be conspicuously posted on the subject dwelling, building, or structure within three business days of filing of the complaint and at least ten days prior to the date of the hearing. A copy of the complaint and summons shall be served in one of the following ways: 
a.	Personal service upon each owner and party in interest if such parties are residents of the county where the property is located. Service shall be perfected at least ten days prior to the date of the hearing. Service may be made by the public officer designated by ordinance to abate nuisances or by any law enforcement officer of the municipality whose ordinance is being enforced; and a return of service, filed with the clerk of the municipal court, shall be deemed sufficient proof that service was perfected; 
b.	Pursuant to the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 48-4-78; or 
c.	Statutory overnight delivery. 
(2)	Nonresidents of the city. If any owner or party in interest is a resident of this state, but resides outside of the county where the property is located, service shall be perfected by certified mail or statutory overnight delivery, return receipt requested, to the most recent address shown in county tax filings and mailed at least 14 days prior to the date of the hearing. 
(3)	Nonresidents of the state. Nonresidents of this state, whose mailing address is known, shall be served by certified mail or statutory overnight delivery, return receipt requested, mailed at least 14 days prior to the date of the hearing. For nonresidents whose mailing address is unknown, a notice stating the date, time, and place of the hearing shall be published in the newspaper in which the sheriff's advertisements appear in such county once a week for two consecutive weeks prior to the hearing. 
(4)	Service of guardians and personal representatives. In the event either the owner or any party in interest is a minor, an estate, an incompetent person, or person laboring under disabilities, the guardian or other personal representative of such person shall be served, and if such guardian or personal representative resides outside the county or is a nonresident of this state, he shall be served as provided herein for nonresidents. If such owner or party in interest has no guardian or personal representative, service shall be perfected by serving the judge of the probate court of the county wherein such property is located at least 30 days prior to the date of the hearing which judge shall stand in the place of and protect the rights of such minor, estate, or incompetent person or appoint a guardian ad litem for such person. 
(5)	Unknown persons and remaindermen. In the event of unknown persons or unborn remaindermen who are likely to have any rights in the property or interest or the proceeds thereof, the judge of the probate court of the county wherein such property or interest is located shall be personally served at least 30 days prior to the date of the hearing, and it shall be the duty of the judge of the probate court to stand in the place of and protect the rights of such unknown parties or unborn remaindermen. 
(6)	Whereabouts unknown. In the event the whereabouts of any owner or party in interest is unknown and the same cannot be ascertained by the public officer in the exercise of reasonable diligence, or if any owner or party in interest cannot, after due diligence, be served as provided in this section, the public officer shall make an affidavit to that effect and serve, by publication, in the manner provided in subsection (3) of this section, and such publication shall be sufficient proof that service was perfected. 
(7)	Filing of lis pendens. A notice of lis pendens shall be filed in the office of the clerk of superior court in the county in which the dwelling, building, or structure is located at the time of filing the complaint in the appropriate court. Such notice shall have the same force and effect as other lis pendens notices provided by law. 
(8)	Subsequent service. Orders and other filings made subsequent to service of the initial complaint shall be served in the manner provided in this section on the owner and any party in interest who answers the complaint or appears at the hearing. 
(9)	Waiver of notice. Any party who fails to answer or appear at the hearing shall be deemed to have waived all further notice in the proceedings. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-9) 
Sec. 18-91. - Temporary injunction. 
Any person affected by an order issued by the public officer may petition to the superior court of the county for an injunction restraining the public officer from carrying out the provisions of the order, and the superior court may, upon such petition, issue a temporary injunction restraining the public officer, pending the final disposition of the matter; provided, however, that such person shall present such petition to the court within 15 days of the posting and service of the order of the public officer. De novo hearings shall be had by the superior court on petitions within 20 days of the filing thereof. The superior court shall hear and determine the issues raised and shall enter such final order or decree as law and justice may require; provided, however, that it shall not be necessary to file bond in any amount before obtaining a temporary injunction pursuant to this section. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-10) 
Sec. 18-92. - Eminent domain. 
Nothing in this division shall be construed as preventing the owner of any property from receiving just compensation for the taking of such property by the power of eminent domain under the laws of this state, nor is permitting any property to be condemned or destroyed except in accordance with the police power of this state. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-11) 
Sec. 18-93. - Appeal. 
Review of an order of the magistrate court requiring the repair, alteration, improvement, or demolition of a dwelling, building, or structure shall be by direct appeal to the superior court as provided by state law. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-12) 
Sec. 18-94. - Appropriations. 
The city council is authorized to make such appropriations from its revenues as it may deem necessary or appropriate and may accept and apply for and utilize grants or donations to assist it in carrying out the provisions of this division. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-13) 
Sec. 18-95. - Authority; conflict of law. 
The powers and authority granted hereunder shall be in addition to and supplemental of any other powers and authority granted to the city and its agents by state statute or this Code. In the event of a conflict between this division and the minimum standards codes adopted in article II of this chapter, the provisions of this division shall apply. 
(Ord. of 6-13-2005, § 9-15) 
Chapter 22 - BUSINESS REGULATION AND TAXATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Professions and businesses, O.C.G.A. § 43-1-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 22-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Business means any business, trade, occupation, profession, avocation, or calling of any kind, subject, by the provisions of this chapter, to a business or occupation tax. 
Engaged in business means performing any act of selling any goods or services or soliciting business or offering goods or services for sale for payment in an attempt to make a profit, including the sales or services of the character as made by a wholesaler or retailer or when a person is involved in any of the functions performed as a manufacturer, either as an owner, operator, or agent in any business, trade, profession, occupation within the city. Any person deemed to be engaged in business is thus subject to the requirements of this chapter. 
Manufacturer means a person who, either directly or by contracting with others for the necessary labor or mechanical services, manufacturers for sale or commercial use any articles, substances or commodities; including all the activities of a commercial nature wherein labor or skill is applied, by hand or by machinery, to materials so that, as a result thereof a new, different, or useful article of trade or commerce is produced, and including the production or fabrication of specially or custom made articles, and including the making, fabricating, processing, refining, mixing, slaughtering, packing, aging, curing, preserving, canning, and preparing and freezing of fresh foods, fruits, vegetables, and meats. 
Retailer means a person who sells to the consumer or any other person for any purpose other than for resale in the form of tangible personal property. 
Services means accommodating or performing a duty or work by a person utilizing time or talents for direct or indirect remuneration. 
Wholesaler means a person who sells to jobbers or to another person other than the consumer anything in the form of tangible personal property. 
(Ord. of 12-11-1995, § 10-1) 
Secs. 22-2—22-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - MISCELLANEOUS BUSINESS REGULATIONS 

Sec. 22-21. - Lighting required. 
All proprietors or operators of business establishments shall be required to provide and maintain sufficient illumination on all parts of parking lots to render all positions of all persons upon such parking areas clearly visible to other patrons and proprietors, from the time of darkness until the time of closing. 
Secs. 22-22—22-45. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - REGISTRATION AND LICENSING 

Sec. 22-46. - Applicability. 
This article shall apply to all businesses other than businesses specifically addressed in other articles within this chapter, including, but not limited to: 
Accountants; 
Air conditioning sales, service; 
Amusement services; 
Appliances, sales and services; 
Appraisers, real and personal property; 
Architects; 
Arts and crafts; 
Attorneys; 
Auto dealers, sales and services; 
Bakers; 
Barbers; 
Beauty shops; 
Bookkeeping services; 
Building contractors; 
Bus lines; 
Billiard rooms; 
Canvassers, peddlers, traveling salesmen; 
Carpenters; 
Carpets, sales, installations, cleaning; 
Carwash; 
Certified public accountants; 
Cleaning and janitorial services; 
Clothing stores; 
Contractors, general; 
Cotton gins; 
Dancing schools; 
Day care centers, (senior, nursery, and kindergarten); 
Delicatessens; 
Department stores (general merchandise); 
Disco; 
Doctors; 
Drug stores; 
Dry cleaners; 
Dry goods stores; 
Electrical contractors, electricians; 
Express companies; 
Exterminators; 
Fabric shops; 
Farm produce (buyers and processors); 
Farm supplies; 
Fast food vendors; 
Feed and seed dealers; 
Funeral directors; 
Furniture sales; 
Game rooms; 
Gas companies; 
Gift shops; 
Grain dealers, driers; 
Grave markers, monuments; 
Grocers; 
Gunsmith; 
Hardware dealers; 
Heating/air conditioning, sales and services; 
Hotel/motel; 
Insurance sales; 
Interior decorators; 
Janitorial and cleaning services; 
Junk and scrap dealers; 
Laundromats; 
Laundry trucks; 
Lawyers; 
Loan agents; 
Lumber/timber dealers; 
Liquor stores; 
Manufacturers; 
Merchants, general merchandise; 
Monuments/grave markers; 
Motel/hotels; 
Mobile home parks;

Painters (buildings and signs, artistic for sale);

Real estate brokers and agents;

Roofing contractors;

Seeds and plants;
