Sec. 46-61. - Personal conduct. 
No officer shall exhibit anger, ill feeling, or desire for revenge, or use any profane or vulgar language in the performance of his duty. No officer shall engage in an altercation with another member of the police department, or with any other law enforcement officer, whether on or off duty, nor engage in any conversation likely to provoke an argument. 
Sec. 46-62. - Critical comment regarding officers and officials. 
Officers or other members of the department shall not criticize the work manner or performance of duties, or the personal actions or habits of other members of the police department. Any failure to perform duties, or wrongful acts or habits, shall be reported in writing to the chief of police. No officer or other member or the department shall criticize the work, manner of performance of duties or the personal actions or habits of officers of their or other departments, city attorneys, judges, or other public officials. Gossiping among members of this department concerning higher authority or any individual or anything pertaining to official business of the department, will be cause for disciplinary action. 
Sec. 46-63. - Frequenting disreputable places. 
No officer shall, while on duty, or when in uniform or wearing any part of the uniform that might identify him as a member of the police department, loiter in any place where beer, wine, or intoxicating liquors are sold or any place having such reputation, nor shall any officer enter a disreputable place unless required to do so in connection with his enforcement duties. 
Sec. 46-64. - Confidential communications. 
No officer or employee shall communicate with any person other than a member of the department any information relating to any service in which he is or has been engaged, or relating to any departmental business without permission of a superior officer, unless in obedience to other lawful authority after service of a subpoena. The foregoing rule shall also apply to news releases or other information to the press. 
Sec. 46-65. - Alertness to duty. 
Within his proper jurisdiction, no officer shall overlook any opportunity to perform his duty by making an arrest or give a warning to a violator or offering aid or information to persons in need, according to the policy of the department. 
Sec. 46-66. - Gratuities; solicitations. 
No officer shall receive or accept any present, fee or other reward for his services other than his regular salary, except as authorized by law. No officer shall request any person other than his superiors in the organization, to intervene or make representation in his behalf to secure his promotion or for any purpose related to his work, nor shall an officer solicit subscriptions, sign or circulate petitions. 
Sec. 46-67. - Borrowing vehicles. 
The practice of borrowing cars from dealers and garage men, and courting special favors, is strictly forbidden. 
Sec. 46-68. - Endorsements. 
No officer shall recommend or favor any garage, repair shop, insurance or other business to persons whom they contact in the line of duty, nor shall any officer furnish to any person any testimonial or endorsement of any product or equipment. 
Sec. 46-69. - Outside occupations. 
No officer shall engage in any business, occupation or profession that, in the opinion of the chief of police would affect or interfere with such officer's proper performance of his duty or be detrimental to his services to the department. 
Sec. 46-70. - Violations of law. 
Any officer who violates the laws of the commonwealth and is so charged shall be turned over to civil authorities. Should such person be found guilty of such charge, the officer will be dropped from the payroll of the police department. 
Sec. 46-71. - Making arrest for personal reasons. 
The making of any arrest for an act growing out of a personal argument on the part of the officer, or a quarrel in which any member of his family is involved, is forbidden. 
Sec. 46-72. - Disobedience; insubordination. 
Willful disobedience of an order issued verbally or in writing by the chief of police will be sufficient grounds for drastic disciplinary action or dismissal. Insubordination shall be any manifested resistance, physical or mental, to authority and shall be grounds for severe disciplinary action or dismissal. 
Sec. 46-73. - Smoking. 
Smoking is permissible, except when in the performance of official duties, while talking with a motorist, directing traffic, or in any place where it does not become an officer to do so. 
Sec. 46-74. - Report of injury. 
Any officer receiving an injury while on duty shall immediately report such incident to his immediate superior, and forward a report, in writing, to the chief of police within 24 hours. 
Sec. 46-75. - Surrender of property upon suspension. 
In all cases of suspension from duty, the suspended officer shall immediately surrender his badge, identification certificate and such other city property in his possession at the time of the suspension. During the period of suspension, the suspended officer shall not wear any part of the uniform of the police department. 
Sec. 46-76. - Uniforms. 
(a)	Generally. All officers shall wear the prescribed uniforms and equipment at all times when on duty, unless otherwise ordered by a superior officer. Uniforms shall be kept clean and pressed at all times. Footwear shall be kept in a neat and tidy condition. Any worn or damaged items of the uniform shall be replaced immediately upon the approval of the chief of police and purchasing agent. Shirts and blouses shall be kept buttoned, also pockets/flaps. No fraternal or other insignia shall be worn on the uniform except that are designated by the chief of police exemplifying, E.M.T. training, firearms, military, scholastic, police honors, etc. Pencils shall be kept in the pocket provided for that purpose. Notebooks, letters, and other papers shall be kept concealed. 
(b)	Fulltime officers. Each fulltime officer shall be issued five uniform shirts, with badge, nameplate, collar insignias, whistle, snake chain of appropriate season and color, five uniform pants, one uniform headgear with badge and accessories. Uniform leather will be basket weave type. Each fulltime officer shall also be issued one underbelt, one equipment belt, four belt keepers, one key holder with departmental keys, one security holster with .45 cal. semi-automatic Glock, cuff case with handcuffs, walkie talkie and case, flashlight and baton holder, double magazine case with magazines fully loaded, one ballistic vest, uniform raincoat, uniform. At season change, five uniform shirts are to be issued, e.g., winter long-sleeve with two ties and tie tack, one winter jacket. 
(c)	Parttime officers. Each parttime officer shall be issued two uniform shirts, with badge, nameplate, collar insignias, whistle, snake chain of appropriate season and color, two uniform pants, and any other equipment available in departmental inventory. 
Sec. 46-77. - Use of city vehicles. 
(a)	License required. Vehicle operators to be licensed. No officer of the police department or member of the department shall operate a motor vehicle without the proper license. 
(b)	Speeding. An officer while on patrol will travel at a rate of speed not to exceed 25 miles per hour, except when in pursuit of an automobile or in an emergency. Officers will observe the speed laws of all towns and cities, except in cases of extreme emergencies. 
(c)	Responsibility for damages. Officers to whom a motor vehicle is assigned will be held responsible for such motor vehicle and its equipment in its entirety. Where investigation shows that the damage to such vehicle was caused by negligence or in violation of state laws, the officer to whom such vehicle is assigned will be held responsible, and he will be responsible, and he will be required to repair or replace damaged parts at his own expense. 
(d)	Refueling. When a patrol car comes in from regular patrol or an emergency call, the driver will, immediately upon checking in at the station, refuel the gasoline tank and check the oil and water. 
(e)	Transporting females. No female person, other than a female police officer, shall be transported in any patrol car unless such person is under arrest, or has been injured in an accident or fight, is suffering from an illness and is being taken to a hospital or medical aid, or is a witness for the city in a trial. Otherwise, permission must be obtained from the chief of police. 
Sec. 46-78. - Hours of duty. 
Officers of the police department are subject to call for duty at any hour or for any emergency, and shall promptly respond to such calls from their superior officers. Officers shall work in such areas at such hours and on such services as may be assigned to them, and while on duty they shall not leave their respective posts, except in an emergency or upon specific instructions from a superior officer. 
Sec. 46-79. - Absence from duty. 
No officer shall be absent from duty without permission, and any officer who is unable to go on duty due to sickness or for other reasons shall immediately notify or cause the next higher authority to be notified accordingly. 
Chapter 50 - MANUFACTURED AND MOBILE HOMES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— The Uniform Standards Code for Manufactured Homes Act, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-130 et seq.; regulations for septic tanks in unincorporated areas; conformity prerequisite to building permit, O.C.G.A. § 31-3-5.1; registration and licensing of dealers, manufacturers and persons transporting mobile homes, O.C.G.A. § 40-2-36; removal of transportable housing from lands subject to writ of possession, O.C.G.A. § 44-7-59; ad valorem taxation of mobile homes, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-440 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 50-1. - Conflict of regulations. 
In any case where a provision of this chapter is found to be in conflict with a provision of any other ordinance or code of the city, the provision that establishes the higher standard for the promotion and protection of the health and safety of the people shall prevail. 
Sec. 50-2. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Manufactured home shall have the meaning provided in O.C.G.A. § 8-2-160. 
Mobile home means a manufactured home as defined herein. 
Mobile home lot means a parcel of land for the placement of a single mobile home and for the exclusive use of its occupants. 
Mobile home park means a parcel of land which has been planned and improved for the placement of mobile homes for nontransient uses. 
Mobile home stand means that part of an individual lot which has been reserved for the placement of one mobile home unit. 
Park management means the person who owns or has charge, care or control of the mobile home park. 
Park street means a street which affords principal means of access to mobile home lots or auxiliary buildings from any adjacent public street. 
Service building means a structure provided by the park management for nonresidential uses as a convenience to park occupants. 
Sewer connection means the connection consisting of all pipes, fittings and appurtenances between the drain outlet of a mobile home and the inlet of the corresponding sewer riser pipe of the sewage system serving the mobile home park. 
Sewer riser pipe means that portion of the sewer lateral which extends vertically to the ground elevation and terminates at each mobile home lot. 
Water connection means the connection consisting of all pipes, fittings and appurtenances between the water inlet pipe of the mobile home and the outlet of the corresponding water riser pipe of the water supply system serving the mobile home park. 
Water riser pipe means that portion of the water supply system which extends vertically to the ground elevation and terminates at each mobile home lot. 
Secs. 50-3—50-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - MANUFACTURED HOMES 

Sec. 50-23. - Authority of city clerk. 
The city clerk is hereby authorized and empowered, subject to the specific provisions of this article, to prescribe applications, moving permit, and location decal forms, and thereafter to alter and change the same, and said city clerk is empowered to require that applicants furnish the information in writing as may be reasonably required to effectuate the purpose hereof. 
Sec. 50-24. - Utility services withheld pending compliance. 
(a)	No utility services shall be provided to any mobile or manufactured home until the home is in full compliance with the provisions of this chapter and the city building department has issued a certificate of occupancy as provided herein. 
(b)	The building official is authorized to permit the applicable power company to provide temporary power not to exceed 110 volts for the express purpose of completing necessary installation of the mobile home or manufactured home. This provision specifically does not authorize permanent power hookup or occupancy of the mobile home or manufactured home. It shall be unlawful for temporary power to be utilized on a permanent basis or for occupancy of said home. 
Sec. 50-25. - Minimum requirements. 
No mobile home or manufactured home shall be moved into or relocated for permanent or temporary occupancy unless: 
(1)	Moving permit. The owner, mover, or hauler has obtained a moving permit from the office of the county tax commissioner. 
(2)	Age of home. The home is less than ten years old. 
(3)	Approved site. The home must be positioned on a site approved by the city's building department, evidenced by a building permit, as provided herein. 
(4)	Construction standards. The home complies with the minimum construction and installation standards of this chapter and with all applicable state, county, and city building and zoning regulations. 
(5)	Wastewater connection. The home has been approved for connection to the city wastewater system or has been issued a septic tank permit by the appropriate county officials. 
(6)	Building permit and certificate of occupancy. The city building department has issued a building permit for installation of the home, and final inspection and approval of the home and the installation of the home has resulted in issuance by the city of a certificate of occupancy. 
(7)	Mobile home decal. The county tax commissioner has issued a mobile home decal, as provided herein. 
(8)	Fees and taxes. All applicable permit and inspection fees, and all applicable taxes, have been paid in full. 
Sec. 50-26. - Minimum construction and installation standards. 
Each newly installed mobile home or manufactured home in the city shall conform to the minimum construction standards and the minimum installation standards provided by: 
(1)	The U.S. Housing and Urban Development, as set forth in the National Manufactured Housing Construction and Safety Standards Act, 42 USC 5401 et seq. 
(2)	Chapter 120-3-7, Rules and Regulations for Manufactured Homes, as promulgated by the Georgia Office of the Commissioner of Insurance Safety Fire division. 
(3)	The Uniform Standards Code for Manufactured Homes Act, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-130 et seq. 
Sec. 50-27. - Moving permit required. 
No mover, hauler, person, or other entity shall move a mobile home or manufactured home to any location beyond the limits of the lot or parcel of land upon which it presently is located, or upon which it was originally located, without first obtaining a moving permit from the county tax commissioner authorizing the relocation. 
Sec. 50-28. - Building permit required. 
Any person desiring to locate or relocate an approved mobile or manufactured home within the city must obtain a building permit from the city building department. Application for the building permit shall be made on the form provided by the building department and shall be accompanied by such documentation as the building department may require, including, but not limited to, a septic tank permit issued by the appropriate county authority as provided herein. The application shall also be accompanied by a building permit fee in the amount established by the city council. 
Sec. 50-29. - Certificate of occupancy required. 
A certificate of occupancy shall be issued indicating compliance with all applicable codes before any person is authorized to occupy any newly installed mobile home or manufactured home. Following installation of the mobile or manufactured home pursuant to a validly issued building permit, the city building department shall make final inspection to ensure compliance with the provisions of this chapter. Final inspection shall include, but not be limited to, inspection of the plumbing, electrical, and gas installations, the foundation, and all stairs and landings. Upon successful final inspection, the building department shall issue a certificate of occupancy. No certificate of occupancy shall be issued by the city building department unless a valid septic tank permit, if applicable, and decal have been issued as provided herein. 
Sec. 50-30. - Septic tank permit required. 
If a mobile or manufactured home is approved for relocation to a site having city water and wastewater available, an approved connection to city services shall be obtained as provided in this Code. If city services are not available at the approved installation site, the owner shall obtain a septic tank permit from the appropriate county authorities. No building permit shall be issued by the city unless the home is approved for connection to city water and wastewater system or until a septic tank permit is issued by the county. 
Sec. 50-31. - Decal required. 
Every person or other entity holding title to or possessing a mobile home or manufactured home that is moved into or relocated within the limits of the city, shall, prior to issuance of a certificate of occupancy, report the location of and obtain a location decal for the mobile home or manufactured home. Thereafter, decals must be renewed annually, no later than the date specified by the county tax commissioner. Decals are obtained from the office of the county tax commissioner. No decal shall be issued by the county tax commissioner unless all applicable fees and taxes have been paid. 
Sec. 50-32. - Location of modular housing units. 
All modular housing units placed in the R-1 zoning district must be placed parallel to the street on which they are situated with the front of the unit facing the street. 
(Ord. of 3-12-2001(2)) 
Sec. 50-33. - Additional administrative procedures. 
The planning commission is authorized to establish other administrative procedures so the regulations can be more effectively and consistently applied. The zoning administrator is authorized to address situations where the ordinance does not indicate a procedure, provided the planning commission at the next regular meeting ratifies the action. 
Sec. 50-34. - Standards for installation of preowned manufactured homes. 
(a)	Definitions. The following words, terms, or phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection: 
(1)	Applicant means any person seeking to install a preowned manufactured home in the city limits of the City of Ellaville. 
(2)	Building inspector means the person appointed, employed, or otherwise designated as the director of planning, permits and inspections; the municipal building official or any of his or her assistants. 
(3)	Certificate of occupancy means a document issued by the building inspector certifying that a preowned manufactured home is in compliance with applicable requirements set forth by this section, and indicating it to be in a condition suitable for residential occupancy. 
(4)	Guarantee of condition bond means a surety bond to guarantee that the affidavit and photographs, required by subsections (c)(1)a. and b. of this section, reasonably portray or represents the existing condition of the preowned manufactured home proposed for relocation. In lieu of the bond, a cash deposit may be deposited with the city. 
(5)	Install means to construct a foundation system and to place or erect a manufactured home on such foundation system. Such term includes, without limitation, supporting, blocking, leveling, securing, or anchoring such manufactured home and connecting multiple or expandable sections of such manufactured home. 
(6)	Jurisdiction means the areas within the city limits of the City of Ellaville, Georgia. 
(7)	Manufactured home means a structure, transportable in one or more sections, which, in the traveling mode, is eight body feet or more in width or 40 body feet or more in length or, when erected on site, is 320 or more square feet and which is built on a permanent chassis and designed to be used as a dwelling with or without a permanent foundation when connected to the required utilities and includes the plumbing, heating, air-conditioning, and electrical systems contained therein; except that such term shall include any structure which meets all the requirements of this paragraph except the size requirements and with respect to which the manufacturer voluntarily files a certification required by the secretary of housing and urban development and complies with the standards established under the National Manufactured Housing Construction and Safety Standards Act of 1974, 42 U.S.C. Section 5401 et seq. 
(8)	Preowned manufactured home means any manufactured home that has been previously used as a residential dwelling and has been titled. 
(b)	Conditions. All preowned manufactured homes located in the jurisdiction shall bear a label certifying it was constructed in compliance with the National Manufactured Housing Construction and Safety Standards Act of 1974, 42 U.S.C. Section 5401 et seq. (the HUD Code) and shall be installed in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 8-2-160 et seq. 
(c)	Permitting, inspection, certificate of occupancy and fees. A permit shall be required to locate a preowned manufactured home in the jurisdiction. 
(1)	Permit. To obtain a permit, applicants shall provide to the building inspector: 
a.	An affidavit signed by the applicant that the preowned manufactured home meets health and safety standards required by this Act; 
b.	Photographs of the interior and exterior of the preowned manufactured home providing evidence that home meets the minimum health and safety standards of subsection (d) of this section; 
c.	A $10,000.00 refundable guarantee of condition bond or $10,000.00 refundable cash deposit; and 
d.	The permit and inspection fee required by subsection (d) of this section. 
(2)	Inspection. Upon receipt of a permit, applicants may relocate the manufactured home on a residential site for the purposes of inspection. Applicant shall arrange for an inspection to be held once the installation of the manufactured home is complete. 
(3)	Certificate of occupancy. A certificate of occupancy shall be issued to the applicant at such time that the building inspector certifies that the requirements of this section have been met. 
(3)	Fee. A permit and inspection fee of $250.00 shall be charged to the applicant to cover the cost to the city to process the permit application and inspect the preowned manufactured home. Such fee shall cover the initial inspection and one follow-up inspection. The applicant shall be charged $100.00 for each additional follow-up inspection that may be necessary. 
(4)	Alternative inspection. At the request of the applicant, the building inspector may, at his or her discretion, inspect a preowned manufactured home prior to its being relocated if the home is then located at another site within the city. 
(d)	Minimum health and safety standards. All preowned manufactured homes shall comply with the following before being issued a certificate of occupancy by the building inspector: 
(1)	HUD code. Every preowned manufactured home located in the jurisdiction shall be in compliance with the Federal Manufactured Housing Construction and Safety Standards Act, 42 U.S.C. 5401-5445 (the HUD code) and shall not have been altered in such a way that the home no longer meets the HUD code. 
(2)	Interior condition. Every floor, interior wall, and ceiling of a preowned manufactured home shall be in sound condition. Doors and windows shall be operable, watertight and in good working condition. The floor system shall be in sound condition and free of warping, holes, water damage, or deterioration. 
(3)	Exterior condition. The exterior of all preowned manufactured homes shall be free of loose or rotting boards or timbers and any other conditions that might admit rain or moisture to the interior portions of the walls or to occupied spaces. The exterior siding shall be free of rot and rust. Roofs shall be structurally sound and have no obvious defects that might admit rain or cause moisture to collect on the interior portion of the home. 
(4)	Sanitary facilities. Every plumbing fixture, water, and waste pipe of a preowned manufactured home shall be in a sanitary working condition when properly connected, and shall be free from leaks and obstructions. Each home shall contain a kitchen sink. Each bathroom shall contain a lavatory and water closet. At least one bathroom shall contain a tub and/or shower facilities. Each of these fixtures shall be checked upon being connected to ensure they are in good working condition. 
(5)	Heating systems. Heating shall be safe and in working condition. Unvented heaters shall be prohibited. 
(6)	Electrical systems. Switches, receptacles, fixtures, etc., shall be properly installed and wired and shall be in working condition. Distribution panels shall be in compliance with the approved listing, complete with required breakers, with all unused openings covered with solid covers approved and listed for that purpose. The home shall be subject to an electrical continuity test to assure that all metallic parts are properly bonded. Each preowned manufactured home shall contain a water heater in safe and working order. 
(7)	Hot water supply. Each home shall contain a water heater in safe and working condition. 
(8)	Egress windows. Each bedroom of a manufactured home shall have at least one operable window of sufficient size to allow egress if necessary. 
(9)	Ventilation. The kitchen in the home shall have at least one operating window or other ventilation device. 
(10)	Smoke detectors. Each preowned manufactured home shall contain one operable battery-powered smoke detector in each bedroom and in the kitchen, which must be installed in accordance with the manufacturer's recommendations. 
(e)	Enforcement. 
(1)	Permanent connection to utilities shall not be approved until the building inspector has issued a certificate of occupancy. 
(2)	Owners of preowned manufactured homes that are not in compliance upon a third inspection shall have their permit revoked and shall be required to remove the home from the jurisdiction at their own expense. 
(3)	The guarantee of condition bond or cash deposit will be forfeited after 90 days from the date of inspection, unless all conditions and standards are met prior to the end of the 90 days or an extension has been issued in writing by the building inspector. 
(f)	Penalties. Failure to remove a preowned manufactured home from the jurisdiction, upon failure to receive a certificate of occupancy, shall be punishable by a fine of $1,000.00. Each day any violation under this section continues shall be considered a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 10-11-2010, §§ 1—6) 
Secs. 50-35—50-54. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - MANUFACTURED HOME AND RECREATIONAL VEHICLE PARKS 

Sec. 50-55. - Environmental protection. 
Condition of soil, groundwater level, drainage and topography shall not create hazards to the property or the health or safety of the occupants of a mobile home park. The site shall not be exposed to objectionable smoke, noise, odors, or other adverse influences, and no portion subject to unpredictable and/or sudden flooding, subsidence or erosion shall be used for any purpose which would expose persons or property to hazards. 
Sec. 50-56. - Responsibilities of the park management. 
(a)	The person to whom a license for a mobile home park is issued shall operate the park in compliance with this article and shall provide adequate supervision to maintain the park, its facilities and equipment in good repair and in a clean and sanitary condition. 
(b)	The park management shall notify all park occupants of all applicable provisions of this article and inform them of their duties and responsibilities under this article. 
(c)	The park management shall supervise the placement of each mobile home stand which includes securing its stability and installing all utility connections. 
(d)	The park management shall maintain a register containing the names of all park occupants identified by lot number or street address. The register shall be available to any authorized person inspecting the park. 
(e)	The park management shall notify the health officer immediately of any suspected communicable or contagious disease within the park. 
Sec. 50-57. - Responsibilities of park occupants. 
(a)	The mobile home park occupant shall comply with all applicable requirements of this article and shall maintain the occupant's mobile home lot, its facilities and equipment in good repair and in a clean and sanitary condition. 
(b)	Pets, if permitted in the park, shall be prohibited to run at large or create any nuisance within the limits of any mobile home lot or street. 
(c)	Skirtings, porches, awnings and other additions shall be installed only if permitted and approved by the park management. When installed, they shall be maintained in good repair. The space immediately underneath a mobile home shall be used for storage only if permitted by the park management. If permitted, the following conditions shall be satisfied: 
(1)	The storage area shall be provided with a base of impervious material. 
(2)	Stored items shall be located so as not to interfere with the underneath inspection of the mobile home. 
(3)	The storage area shall be enclosed by skirting. The park occupant shall store and dispose of all rubbish and garbage in a clean, sanitary and safe manner. The garbage container shall be rodentproof, insectproof and watertight. 
Sec. 50-58. - Barbecue pits, fireplaces, stoves and incinerators. 
Cooking shelters, barbecue pits, fireplaces, woodburning stoves and incinerators shall be so located, constructed, maintained and used as to minimize fire hazards and smoke nuisance both on the property on which used and on neighboring property. No open fire shall be permitted except in facilities provided. No open fire shall be left unattended. No fuel shall be used and no material burned which emits dense smoke or objectionable odors. 
Sec. 50-59. - Refuse handling. 
(a)	The storage, collection and disposal of refuse in the mobile home park shall be so conducted as to create no health hazards, rodent harborage, insect breeding areas, accident or fire hazards or air pollution. 
(b)	All refuse shall be stored in flytight, watertight, rodentproof containers. Containers shall be provided in sufficient number and capacity to properly store all refuse. 
(c)	Refuse collection stands shall be provided on each mobile home lot for all refuse containers. The container stands shall be designed to prevent containers from being tipped. 
(d)	All refuse containing garbage shall be collected at least once weekly. Where suitable collection service is not available from municipal or private agencies, the mobile home park operator shall provide this service. All refuse shall be collected and transported in covered vehicles or covered containers. 
(e)	Where municipal or private disposal service is not available, the mobile home park operator shall dispose of the refuse by burning in an approved incinerator or by transporting to a disposal site approved by the health officer. 
(f)	Refuse incinerators, if provided, shall be constructed in accordance with engineering plans and specifications which shall be reviewed and approved by the health officer. 
Sec. 50-60. - Insect and rodent control. 
(a)	All grounds, buildings, structures, and storage areas in any mobile home park shall be maintained free of accumulations of debris which may provide rodent harborage or breeding places for flies, mosquitoes, and other pests. 
(b)	The growth of brush, weeds and grass shall be controlled to prevent harborage for ticks, chiggers, and other noxious insects. Parks shall be so maintained as to prevent the growth of ragweed, poison ivy, poison oak, poison sumac and other noxious weeds considered detrimental to health. Open areas shall be maintained free of heavy undergrowth of any description. 
Sec. 50-61. - Permits. 
(a)	Required. It shall be unlawful for any person to construct, alter or extend any mobile home park within the limits of the city, unless the person holds a valid building permit approved by the building inspector. 
(b)	Application. Application for building permits required by this section shall contain the following: 
(1)	The name and address of the applicant. 
(2)	The location and legal description of the mobile home park. 
(3)	A master plan similar to a subdivision plat of the proposed park, including, but not limited to, the following: 
a.	The area and dimensions of the tract of land to be used for the proposed mobile home park. 
b.	The number, location and size of all existing and proposed mobile home lots. 
c.	The location and width of all existing and proposed street rights-of-way, pavements, widths, and walkways. 
(4)	Detailed plans and specifications including, but not limited to, the following: 
a.	Plans and specifications of the existing and proposed water supply and sewage disposal facilities, including the location of all existing and proposed water and sewer lines and riser pipes, as approved by the health officer; 
b.	The location and details of existing and proposed lighting and electrical systems; and 
c.	Plans and specifications for grading and storm drainage, as approved by the city engineer; provided, that where a mobile home park is to be developed by phases, complete engineering plans and specifications shall only be required as each phase is proposed for construction. All physical elements of future phases of the master plan, such as streets, mobile home lots or stands, buildings, recreation areas or other features, may be shown as proposed and subject to change as engineering, architectural or financial conditions warrant. 
(c)	Issuance. When, upon review of the application and approval by the health officer and the city engineer, the building inspector is satisfied that the proposed plan meets the requirements of this article, a permit shall be issued. 
Sec. 50-62. - Permanent occupancy of recreational vehicles. 
No recreational vehicle shall be permanently occupied nor connected to water or electrical power, and no mobile home or manufactured home location permits shall be issued by the county clerk for recreational vehicles located within the city. For the purpose of this section, any recreational vehicle occupied for less than 90 days shall be considered nonpermanent and temporary, and any occupancy of 90 days or greater shall be considered permanent. All recreational vehicles must display a current county permit before movement. This shall apply to all recreational vehicles regardless of location, including locations within approved recreational vehicle parks. 
Sec. 50-63. - Mobile home or manufactured home park regulations. 
All mobile or manufactured home parks hereafter developed shall conform to the following regulations: 
(1)	Site plan approval required. All mobile or manufactured home park developments shall require site plan approval by the city council. 
(2)	Location and frontage. A mobile or manufactured home park district development shall be located on property with a minimum frontage of 200 feet on a public street. 
(3)	Street requirements. Interior roads serving the development are required and shall be suitably drained and have a minimum pavement width of 22 feet plus four feet of drainage area on both sides of the road, for a total road width of 30 feet. If dedicated to the public, the roads within the development shall meet the same requirements as required for subdivision roads and streets. 
(4)	Lot area and width. A mobile or manufactured home park development shall have a minimum area of ten contiguous acres and a lot width of at least 200 feet. Each lot space within the park shall have a minimum of 14,000 square feet and shall have not less than 50 feet of frontage on the interior road. 
(5)	Recreation and other community facilities. Not less than ten percent of the total area of the development shall be devoted to recreation and other community use facilities for those mobile or manufactured homes parks containing ten acres or 25 units. 
(6)	Setbacks required. No mobile or manufactured home or other building or structure shall be located closer than 60 feet to any mobile or manufactured home park perimeter property boundary. Each mobile or manufactured home shall be setback from the front lot line and any other mobile or manufactured home by at least 60 feet. 
(7)	Perimeter buffer required. A buffer at least 60 feet in width shall be provided and maintained around the entire exterior perimeter of the mobile or manufactured home park. 
(8)	Lightning. All mobile or manufactured home parks shall have lighting at appropriate height, spacing and intensity so that each mobile or manufactured home site's access and parking is appropriately illuminated. Mercury vapor halogen or low pressure sodium lights that are placed at not less than 500 feet intervals with a minimum height of 18 feet. 
(9)	Utilities. All mobile or manufactured home parks shall be served by water and public sewer systems and shall be subject to approval by the city. 
(10)	Parking. Two spaces per dwelling unit plus one space for each resident manager and additional spaces for visitor parking. All parking spaces as well as walkways shall be of concrete or a pavement substance. 
(11)	Swimming pools. In the event that a swimming pool is developed or planned as a part of the park, a chainlink, masonry or wood fence not less than six feet high with a locking gate shall enclose this facility. Swimming pools must comply with all applicable provisions of this Code, including building and zoning regulations. 
(12)	Park grounds. All park grounds shall be maintained with grass, trees or shrubs to enhance the appearance of the park and to prevent soil erosion or the creation of dust. 
(13)	Use by recreational vehicles limited. Ten percent of the lot spaces may be allocated for temporary use by recreational vehicles, the length of the use to be limited to 90 days per vehicle occupying any of the space in the park. 
(14)	Service buildings. Accessory structures and community service facilities are hereby permitted for the convenience and well-being of park residents. The structures may include, but are not limited to, the following uses: 
a.	Park management offices, repair shops, and storage. 
b.	Community sanitary facilities. 
c.	Community laundry facilities. 
d.	Community postal facilities. 
e.	Indoor community recreation areas. 
f.	Commercial uses supplying essential goods and services. 
(15)	Listing of mobile or manufactured homes required. Every person, or other entity owning or operating a mobile or manufactured home park, and each entity engaged in the sale or rental of mobile or manufactured homes or lots upon which to place them, shall furnish the tax commissioner a complete list of all mobile or manufactured homes parked, rented or otherwise located upon the property of the entity or in a mobile or manufactured home park operated by the entity. 
(16)	Registration of park residents required. Park management must maintain a register of all park residents. The register must be available to any authorized person inspecting the park. 
Sec. 50-64. - Recreational vehicle park regulations. 
All recreational vehicle parks shall conform to the following regulations: 
(1)	Site plan approval required. All recreational vehicle parks shall require site plan approval by the city council. 
(2)	Location and frontage. All recreational vehicle parks shall be located on property with a minimum frontage of 200 feet on a public street. 
(3)	Street requirements. An interior road serving the development is required and shall be suitably graded, stabilized and covered with a dustfree material which shall be durable and well drained under normal use and weather conditions. Said interior road shall have unobstructed access to a public street or highway. The exception being, the first 200 feet of the entrance road from the public street shall be paved with either concrete or asphalt. 
(4)	Lot area and width. The minimum land area of any recreational vehicle park shall be five contiguous acres. Each space within the park shall have a minimum area of not less than 2,000 square feet, and lot lines shall be clearly delineated. Lots may be set at an angle, set parallel to the street, or varied in other ways provided that the arrangement is approved as a part of site plan approval. Each lot within the park shall have a minimum of 25 feet of street frontage, and shall have a minimum depth of 50 feet. 
(5)	Utilities and improvements. 
a.	Each vehicle/camping space shall be equipped with a suitable and approved electrical outlet, a threaded potable water standpipe and faucet, and approved connection to the community sewer system, except at tent-only sites, a fire pit with permanent masonry or stone enclosure, a picnic-type table and a covered trash and garbage container. Garbage shall be removed daily from campsites. 
b.	All recreational vehicle parks must be equipped with men's and ladies' restrooms with toilet, shower and lavatories at a ratio of two fixtures for each sex per vehicle spaces, and a central sanitary dump station. Each recreational park must provide on-site public telephone access. 
(6)	Recreation facilities required. Parks designed to accommodate 15 or more recreational vehicles, campers, etc, shall provide one or more recreation areas. The size of the recreation area shall be based on a minimum of 200 square feet for each travel trailer space. No recreation area shall be smaller than 3,000 square feet and each shall be equipped for family activity. 
(7)	Service building permitted. Community service facilities and accessory structures are hereby permitted, subject to site plan approval, for the convenience of park patrons. The structures may include, but are not limited to, the following uses: 
a.	Park management offices. 
b.	Community laundry facilities. 
c.	Indoor community recreation areas. 
d.	Commercial uses supplying goods or services for the use of park patrons. 
Sec. 50-65. - Lot numbers. 
To make the provisions of this article effective, every operator of every mobile home park within the limits of the city shall devise a system of numbering the lots in the mobile home park operated by him in the manner that the lots are consecutively numbered in the fashion as will permit one seeking the location of a lot to find it with relative ease, and through means of a sign on each lot or other similar device, each lot shall be identified by number so that a person traversing the thoroughfares of the mobile home park by automobile will be able to identify any lot by number. 
Sec. 50-66. - Operator to maintain records. 
Every operator of a mobile home park within the limits of the city shall maintain records showing the given name and last name of each adult occupant of a mobile home located within the mobile home park so operated, and the operator shall maintain the records in a current manner so that at all times the records shall accurately reflect the name of each actual adult occupant. The records required may be maintained in one or more alternative fashions, as follows: 
(1)	If the mobile home park has an office located at the site of the park, the records prescribed may be maintained in the office, provided that the records shall be available for reference by any person legitimately entitled thereto including, but not limited to, law enforcement officers, 24 hours a day. 
(2)	If the mobile home park does not have an office open 24 hours a day, then and in that event, the records required hereby shall be maintained in the office of the sheriff of the city. 
(3)	The records need not be maintained in any particular form so long as they disclose the information required hereby. The records may consist of a plat of the mobile home park showing the lots by number upon which are listed the names of the adults occupying the lot, or the records may consist of a list of the names of the occupants of the mobile home park alphabetically with an indication of the lot number upon which the mobile home occupied by them may be found or it may be a listing of lots by number showing the names of the adult occupants thereof. At a minimum, however, the records shall be such as will enable one inspecting them to determine the given and last names of every adult occupant of every mobile home in the park with a reference to the number of the lot upon which the mobile home occupied by them is located. 
Sec. 50-67. - Enforcement. 
(a)	Upon violation of this article, the city building department or its designee shall notify the owner of the property on which the violation is found by certified mail, sent to the address of the property owner as it appears in tax information. If the owner of the mobile or manufactured home is different from the property owner, the violation notice shall also be sent by certified mail to the owner of the mobile or manufactured home. In case no valid mailing address can be obtained, or if the certified mail is returned, the notice of violation may be hand delivered to the person deemed responsible for said violation. 
(b)	The notice of violation shall clearly state the nature of the violation, including specific provisions of this article which have not been complied with, and the date upon which said violations will be remedied. Said date will be determined by the zoning administrator based on the nature and extent of the violation, but in no case shall exceed 30 days from the date the certified mail was received, the date upon which said violations will be remade shall not exceed 30 days from the date of delivery. 
(c)	The city building department is authorized to issue stop work orders in any instance where a violation of this article is found. The procedure for issuance of stop work orders shall be the same as the notification procedure for violations as specified herein. 
(d)	If, after notice, the violator fails to remedy the violation within the specified time period, or in cases where stop work orders have not been fully complied with, the city building department shall issue a citation requiring appearance in the municipal court. The citation shall include any and all violations found by the building department. 
Chapter 54 - OFFENSES AND MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Crimes and offenses, O.C.G.A. § 16-1-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 54-1—54-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - OFFENSES AGAINST PERSONS, PROPERTY, AND PUBLIC ORDER 

Sec. 54-19. - Contemptuous or disorderly conduct toward mayor and council. 
Any person guilty of contemptuous or disorderly conduct towards the mayor and city council, or in their presence, shall be punished by a fine of not exceeding $50.00, or confinement not to exceed 20 days. 
Sec. 54-20. - Abiding by the lawful instructions. 
Individuals are required to abide by the lawful instructions given by police officers, code enforcement officer, or other city official (city manager, city attorney, city clerk). 
(Ord. of 9-10-2001(3)) 
Sec. 54-21. - Disorderly conduct; acts constituting. 
(a)	A person commits the offense of disorderly conduct when such person, within the corporate limits of the city, commits any of the following: 
(1)	Acts in a violent or tumultuous manner toward another, whereby any person is placed in danger of, or in fear of their safety, life, limb or health; 
(2)	Acts in a violent or tumultuous manner toward another, whereby public property or property of another person is placed in danger of being destroyed or damaged; 
(3)	Endangers or interferes with the lawful pursuits of another by acts of violence or threats of bodily harm; 
(4)	Causes, provokes or engages in any fight, brawl, or riotous conduct so as to endanger the life, limb, health or property of another or of public property; 
(5)	Assembles or congregates with another or others and causes, provokes or engages in any fight or brawl; 
(6)	Collects in bodies or in crowds and engages in unlawful activities; 
(7)	Assembles or congregates with another or others and engages or attempts to engage in gaming; 
(8)	Frequents any public place and obtains money from another by an illegal and fraudulent scheme, trick, artifice, or device, or attempts to do so; 
(9)	Assembles with another or others and engages in any fraudulent scheme, device or trick to obtain or attempt to obtain any valuable thing in any place or from any person; 
(10)	Utters, in a public place or any place open to the public, any obscene words or epithets; 
(11)	Frequents any place or vehicle where gaming or the illegal sale or possession of alcoholic beverages or narcotics or dangerous drugs is practiced, allowed or tolerated; 
(12)	Uses "fighting words" directed towards any person, causing said person to become outraged and thus creating turmoil; 
(13)	Assembles or congregates with another or others and does bodily harm to another or the property of another or public property; 
(14)	By acts of violence or threats thereof, interferes with another's pursuit of a lawful occupation; 
(15)	Congregates with another or others in or on any public way so as to halt the flow of vehicular or pedestrian traffic and refuses to clear such public way when ordered to do so by a peace officer or other person having authority; 
(16)	Damages, befouls or disturbs public property or the property of another so as to create a hazardous, unhealthy, or physically offensive condition; 
(17)	Appears in public in an intoxicated state or condition, whether said intoxication is by alcohol and/or drugs; 
(18)	Exposes any part of his or her body in an indecent or lewd manner; 
(19)	Creates loud noises, by and in any manner, which disrupts, disturbs, or otherwise interferes with the peace and tranquility of the public; 
(20)	Attempts to hinder, delay, obstruct or prevent any law enforcement officer from performing their duty; 
(21)	Keeps a disorderly house or house of ill fame; all adults residing in the house shall be considered its keeper; 
(22)	Lingers or loiters along public sidewalks, streets or public ways of the city; 
(23)	Fails or refuses to remove themselves from the private property of another when requested to do so by the owner or occupant(s) thereof; 
(24)	Either alone or in concert with others, with the intent of appropriating merchandise to his own use without paying for the same or depriving the owner of possession thereof (or the value thereof) in whole or in part, conceals or takes possession of the goods or merchandise from a retail establishment, alters the price tag or other price marking of goods or merchandise of any store or retail establishment, or wrongfully causes the amount paid to be less than the merchant's stated price for the merchandise, where the property or value thereof is $300.00 or less; 
(25)	Commits such words, acts or conduct upon public property, upon private property that is open to the general public, or within the curtilage of any private residence not his own other than by invitation of the owner or lawful occupant, which, under ordinary circumstances, will naturally tend to disturb the public peace, tranquility or decorum, scandalize the community, shock the public sense or morality, or cause a detriment to the health and welfare of the community; or 
(26)	Appears in a public place or in view of the public wearing pants, shorts, or a skirt more than three inches below the hips (crest of the ilium) exposing the skin, undergarments or underwear. For the purpose of this subsection, the term "underwear" shall include any article of clothing worn under the outer garments and next to the skin. At the discretion of the officer, any person violating this subsection may be warned to pull up their pants, and if they comply, said warning shall be the only penalty for violation of this subsection. 
(b)	Continued conduct. Continuation of the disorderly conduct constitutes additional offenses, and each day that the disorderly conduct continues shall constitute a new and separate offense. 
(c)	Any person who commits the offense of disorderly conduct within the corporate limits of the city shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished as provided in section 1-10 of this Code. 
(Ord. of 4-8-2013) 
State Law reference— Similar provision, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-44. 
Sec. 54-22. - Resisting arrest. 
(a)	Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Resist means any act of whatever kind and nature designed to prevent the effecting of a lawful arrest. 
(b)	Unlawful act. It shall be unlawful for any person to resist any police officer of the city who, at the time of encountering resistance, shall be in the act of making, or attempting to make, a lawful arrest of such person. 
State Law reference— Obstruction of officers, O.C.G.A. § 16-10-24. 
Sec. 54-23. - Throwing stones, other missiles. 
No person shall pitch, throw, or cast any stone or missile at or upon any house, window, lamp, electric light or telephone poles or fixtures, or shade trees in said city. 
Sec. 54-24. - Indecent exposure. 
Any person found in a state of nudity, or making any indecent exposure of his body or part or portion of his body shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
State Law reference— Public indecency, O.C.G.A. § 16-6-8. 
Sec. 54-25. - Impersonating police officers prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful for any person, not being a police officer in the city, to assume to act, or to act as or represent himself as a police officer. 
State Law reference— Similar provision, O.C.G.A. § 16-10-23. 
Sec. 54-26. - Theft by shoplifting. 
A person commits the offense of theft by shoplifting when he alone or in concert with another person, with the intent of appropriation merchandise to his own use without paying for the same or to deprive the owner of possession thereof or of the value thereof, in whole or in part, does any of the following: 
(1)	Conceals or takes possession of the goods or merchandise of any store or retail establishment; 
(2)	Alters the price tag or other price marking on goods or merchandise of any store or retail establishment; 
(3)	Transfers the goods or merchandise of any store or retail establishment from one container to another; 
(4)	Interchanges the label or price tag from one item of merchandise with a label or price tag for another item of merchandise; 
(5)	Wrongfully causes the amount paid to be less than the merchant's stated price for the merchandise. 
State Law reference— Theft by shoplifting, O.C.G.A. § 16-8-14. 
Sec. 54-27. - Penalty for theft by shoplifting. 
When the property that was the subject of the theft is $100.00 or less in value, the theft shall be punished as for a misdemeanor; provided, however, that: 
(1)	Upon the first conviction, the defendant is to be fined not more than $100.00, or imprisonment not to exceed 30 days. 
(2)	Upon conviction of a second such offense, in addition to or in lieu of any imprisonment which might be imposed, the defendant shall be fined not less than $250.00 and the fine shall not be suspended or probated, and any other violations of this section hereafter are to be prosecuted in superior court. 
Sec. 54-28. - Penalty for possession of one ounce of marijuana or less. 
Anyone convicted of possession of one ounce or less of marijuana shall be fined not less than $300.00 or more than $500.00, or be punished by imprisonment not to exceed 90 days, or any combination thereof. 
Sec. 54-29. - Vagrancy. 
It shall be unlawful for any person within the city, having no apparent means of subsistence, to neglect to apply himself to some honest and legitimate calling, or to be found habitually loitering about said city, or tramping from house to house through the city in quest of clothing or any other thing to the annoyance of the citizens and to the detriment of the peace and good order of the city. It is hereby made the duty of the police officers to arrest all vagrants and to take them before the proper authority, to be dealt with according to law. 
State Law reference— Loitering or prowling, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-36. 
Sec. 54-30. - Damaging, defacing park property. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to leave the walks laid out in any public park and trespass upon the grass, or to deface any of the seats, fountains or other property therein, or to cut or whittle thereon with a knife or other instrument, or to write or mark thereon with a pen, pencil or other instrument, or to cut or injure any of the shade trees in said park. 
Sec. 54-31. - Damaging, defacing public property. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to injure, deface, break, or destroy any of the property of the city. 
State Law reference— Criminal trespass and damage to property, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-20 et seq. 
Sec. 54-32. - Damaging, interfering with poles, wires, other fixtures. 
Anyone in the act of removing trees, tree limbs or anything that in anyway causes damage to city property, electric lines, poles, meters or lights, water lines, water meters or sewer lines, shall pay for any damages resulting from his actions. 
Sec. 54-33. - Posting signs on posts, trees, poles. 
It shall be unlawful to tack, nail or otherwise place any signs on posts, trees, or poles located on city property, and city rights-of-way, including all easements and other types of ownership. 
State Law reference— Placement of posters, signs, and advertisements on public or private property, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-58. 
Sec. 54-34. - Discharging firearms, other weapons. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge any firearm or gun, including an air rifle, outside of his home and off his premises, on the sidewalks or streets of the city. 
Secs. 54-35—54-56. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - MINORS 

Sec. 54-57. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Curfew hours means 10:00 p.m. until 6:00 a.m. on Sunday through Thursday and 11:00 p.m. until 6:00 a.m. on Friday and Saturday. 
Custodian means any person over the age of 21 years who is in local parentis to a juvenile. 
Emergency means an unforeseen combination of circumstances or the resulting state that calls for immediate action. The term "emergency" includes, but is not limited to, a fire, a natural disaster, an automobile accident, or any situation requiring immediate action to prevent serious bodily injury or loss of life. 
Guardian means any person other than a parent, who has legal guardianship of a minor. 
Minor means any person under the age of 18 years. 
Parent means the natural or adoptive parent of a minor. 
Public place means any street, alley, highway, sidewalk, park, playground or place to which the general public has access and a right to resort for business, entertainment, or other lawful purpose. The term "public place" shall include, but not be limited to, any store, shop, restaurant, tavern, bowling alley, cafe, theater, drug store, pool room, shopping center and any other place devoted to amusement or entertainment of the general public. It shall also include the front or immediate area of the above. 
Sec. 54-58. - Curfew imposed. 
It shall be unlawful for any minor to remain, idle, wander, stroll or play in any public place either on foot or to cruise about without a set destination in any vehicle, in, about or upon any place in the city during curfew hours. 
Sec. 54-59. - Responsibility of owners of public places. 
It shall be unlawful for any person operating or having charge of any public place to knowingly permit or suffer the presence of minors during curfew hours. 
Sec. 54-60. - Responsibility of parent or guardian. 
It shall be unlawful for the parent, guardian or other adult person having custody or control of any minor to suffer or permit or by inefficient control to allow such person to be on the streets or sidewalks or on or in any public property or public place within the city during curfew hours. 
Sec. 54-61. - Exceptions; defenses. 
(a)	It is a defense to prosecution under this article that the minor was: 
(1)	Accompanied by his parent or guardian; 
(2)	On an errand at the direction of the parent or guardian, without any detour or stop; 
(3)	In a motor vehicle involved in interstate travel; 
(4)	Engaged in an employment activity, or going to or returning home from an employment activity, without any detour or stop; 
(5)	Involved in an emergency; 
(6)	On the sidewalk abutting his residence or abutting the residence of a next-door neighbor if the neighbor did not complain to the police department about the child's presence; 
(7)	Attending an official school, religious, or other recreational activity supervised by adults and sponsored by the city, the county, a civic organization, or another similar entity that takes responsibility for the child, or going to or returning from, without any detour or stop, an official school, religious, or other recreational activity supervised by adults and sponsored by the city, the county, a civic organization, or other similar entity that takes responsibility for the minor; 
(8)	Exercising First Amendment rights protected by the United States Constitution, such as the free exercise of religion, freedom of speech, and the right of assembly; or 
(9)	Married or had been married or had disabilities of minority removed in accordance with law. 
(b)	It is a defense to prosecution of an owner, operator, or employee of a business establishment under this article if the owner, operator, or employee of an establishment promptly notified the police department that a minor was present on the premises of the establishment during curfew hours and refused to leave. 
Sec. 54-62. - Enforcement. 
(a)	Warning; notice to parent or guardian. Any police officer upon finding a minor in violation of this article shall ascertain the name and address of such minor and warn the minor that he is in violation of curfew and shall direct the minor to proceed at once to his home or usual place of abode. The police officer shall report such action to the chief of police who in turn shall notify the parents, guardian or person having custody or control of such minor. 
(b)	Detention. If such minor refuses to heed such warning or direction by any police officer or refuses to give such police officer his correct name and address, or if the minor has been warned on a previous occasion that he is in violation of curfew, he shall be taken to the police department and parent, guardian or other adult person having the care and custody of such minor shall be notified to come and take charge of the minor. If the parent, guardian or other adult person cannot be located or fails to come and take charge of the minor, the minor shall be released to the juvenile authorities. 
Chapter 58 - PEDDLERS AND SOLICITORS 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 58-1—58-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PERMITS 

Sec. 58-19. - Required, application, investigation. 
No person, except duly organized charitable organizations, shall be allowed to solicit within the city without first having obtained a permit from the mayor and council after making written application to the mayor and council stating the nature and purpose of such solicitation. The city may appoint any person to investigate and advise the mayor and council as to the necessity or need for said permit. 
Sec. 58-20. - Denial or issuance of solicitors' permits, violations. 
Upon authorization, after due hearing, the mayor and council has the right to grant or refuse a solicitors' permit. Should said permit be refused and such persons solicit after refusal of said permit, it shall be a violation of this Code. Each solicitation shall be a separate and distinct offense and punishable as a separate violation. 
Sec. 58-21. - Application; fees. 
Application for a solicitors permit shall be made at the office of the city clerk, on forms provided by the clerk, and shall be accompanied by a permit fee in the amount established by the city council. 
Chapter 62 - PERSONNEL 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 62-1—62-36. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PERSONNEL REVIEW BOARD 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 62-37. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Formal grievance means a written complaint made by an employee concerning the interpretation of these rules and regulations, departmental work rules, or disciplinary action affecting his employment with the city. 
Grievance and appeal procedure means the procedure that provides review and reconsideration of a decision that adversely affects a permanent employee. 
Permanent employee is an employee with six or more months continuous employment. 
Sec. 62-38. - Composition of board; chairman. 
The personnel review board shall be comprised of three persons appointed by the mayor each year and shall include one councilmember, one city administrative person and one local citizen. The board shall be chaired by the member of the city council to assure standard hearing procedure. 
Secs. 62-39—62-64. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PROCEDURE 

Sec. 62-65. - Initial informal grievance procedure. 
(a)	Review by immediate supervisor. An employee who has a problem or complaint should first attempt settlement through discussion with his immediate supervisor without undue delay. 
(b)	Review by councilmember-in-charge. If, after this discussion, the problem has not been satisfactorily resolved, the employee has the right to discuss it with the councilmember-in-charge, who should then attempt to mediate the complaint. Every effort should be made to find an acceptable solution by informal means. 
(c)	Employee's right to file formal grievance. If either the employee or immediate supervisor is not in agreement with the decision reached by discussion, the employee shall then have the right to file a formal grievance in writing. 
(d)	Consultation with mayor. The immediate supervisor must seek informal settlement through discussion with the mayor before having the right to file a formal grievance in writing. 
Sec. 62-66. - Formal grievance procedure. 
(a)	Submission to supervisor. A written grievance shall be presented to the employee's immediate supervisor, who shall render his decision in writing within five work days. If the immediate supervisor fails to provide acceptable resolution of the grievance, the employee may present the appeal in writing to his supervisor's councilmember-in-charge. Failure of the employee to take further action within five work days after receipt of the written decision of his superior, or within ten work days if no decision is rendered, will constitute a withdrawal of the grievance. 
(b)	Submission to councilmember-in-charge. The councilmember-in-charge shall discuss the grievance with the employee, his representative, if any, and other appropriate persons. The councilmember-in-charge shall render his decision in writing, within five work days after receiving the appeal. 
(c)	Submission to personnel review board. If the employee does not agree with the decision reached, or if the councilmember-in-charge fails to provide resolution of the grievance as outlined in subsection (b) of this section, he may present his appeal in writing to the personnel review board. Failure of the employee to take further action within five days after receipt of the written decision of the councilmember-in-charge, or within ten work days if no decision is rendered, will constitute a withdrawal of the grievance. 
(d)	Scheduling of hearing. Upon receiving a request for hearing, the board shall set a session date within five days. 
(e)	Conduct of hearing. The hearing shall be administrative in nature. The board shall have the right to summon city employees as witnesses and to examine appropriate city records. The board shall secure all pertinent facts and shall inform the employee, in writing, of its decision and the supportive reasons within five working days following the hearing. 
(f)	Appeal to city council. If the employee does not agree with the decision reached, he may appeal in writing to the city council. The city council, upon receiving the grievance, shall discuss the grievance with the employee, his representatives, if any, and with other appropriate persons. The city council shall render a decision in writing within five work days after receiving the appeal. 
(g)	Judicial review. If the employee does not agree with this decision, he may request a court hearing. 
(h)	Closed hearings; representation. The employee shall have the right, at all levels, to a closed hearing and may be represented at any the hearings. 
Secs. 62-67—62-90. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PERSONNEL RULES AND REGULATIONS 

Sec. 62-91. - Employee position classification and pay plans. 
The city manager shall be responsible for the preparation of a position classification and pay plan that shall be submitted to the city council for approval. Such plan may apply to all employees of the city and any of its agencies, departments, boards, commissions, or authorities. When a pay plan has been adopted, the city council shall not increase or decrease the salary range applicable to any position except by amendment of the pay plan. For purposes of this section, all elected city officials and the city manager are not city employees. 
Sec. 62-92. - City equipment and vehicles. 
(a)	Personal use prohibited. No city employees, other than designated personnel, will be allowed to drive city-owned vehicles home, or use city-owned vehicles or equipment for personal use. City-owned vehicles will not be used by employees to run personal errands, go to lunch, to the bank, or to the store. 
(b)	Assignment of vehicles; employee responsibility. A vehicle or equipment may be assigned to an employee to assist in the performance of his duties. The employee will be responsible for the general maintenance and upkeep of the vehicle or equipment. Any vehicle or equipment that is damaged by an employee, if the employee is found to be guilty of negligence or carelessness, the employee will be required to repair or pay for repairs of the vehicle or equipment. 
(c)	Driver's license requirements and driver assignments. All city employees must have and maintain a valid state of Georgia driver's license. Failure to do so will result in dismissal. The only exception to this rule will be identified handicapped employees. These employees can never drive a city vehicle. 
Sec. 62-93. - Tools; materials inventory. 
Employees will be responsible for lost tools or the breakage of tools or equipment assigned to them, except normal wear and tear. An inventory of all tools, equipment, and materials will be held as directed by the purchasing agent or higher authority at least once each quarter. 
Sec. 62-94. - Employee parking at utility plant. 
All city employees are responsible for adhering to the parking arrangement around the city utility plant. 
Sec. 62-95. - Physical examination. 
All city employees must be qualified as physically fit to perform assigned duties in order to be employed by the city. This applies to prospective employees and current employees. The cost for this examination will be paid by the city. 
Sec. 62-96. - Working hours. 
For all city employees assigned work stations other than city hall, working hours will be 7:00 a.m. to 4:00 p.m., Monday through Friday, with a lunch hour from 12:00 p.m. to 1:00 p.m. Working hours for other employees will be 8:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m., Monday through Friday, with a lunch hour from 12:00 p.m. to 1:00 p.m. These hours will be strictly adhered to by all employees. Any deviation without special permission will result in dismissal. 
Sec. 62-97. - Overtime. 
In order to maintain the current year budget, overtime must be used only for emergency situations, such as electrical failure after normal working hours and water leaks that must be repaired after normal working hours. To maintain budget status, designated employees are required to alternate Saturdays and Sundays for the purpose of routine checks on wells, lift stations, electrical stations and other equipment as needed. 
Sec. 62-98. - Tardiness. 
An employee is tardy or late for work if the employee reports for work eight or more minutes after the specified time to report. 
Sec. 62-99. - Absences. 
Any employee who fails to report for work for three or more consecutive days without prior approval or notification to the department head, shall be considered to have abandoned his position with the city, and shall no longer be considered employed. Absence for three or more days, with prior approval or notification, will require a doctor's statement if sickness is claimed. If sickness is not claimed, the absence shall be charged to annual leave (vacation); provided, however, that if the employee has no annual leave accrued or if the employee requests that the absence not to be charged to annual leave, then no payment will be made for this absence. An employee who habitually abuses the authorized leave policies shall be terminated at the discretion of the department head. 
Sec. 62-100. - Time keeping. 
(a)	Clocking in and out. Each employee is responsible for his own time card. Each employee will punch in at the start of each work period, and punch out at the end of each work period. Each employee must make certain that the date and time of entries on his time card are correct. 
(b)	Handwritten cards prohibited. Handwritten cards are not acceptable for any reason, even with the department head approval, except emergency call out of the electric department. There will be no pay for any time that the time clock is not used to report work hours, except emergency call out of the electric department. 
(c)	Clocking in or out for another employee. No employee is to punch in for another employee for any reason. If one employee punches in or out for another employee, both employees shall be dismissed. 
Sec. 62-101. - Annual leave. 
(a)	The city provides paid annual leave for all employees who have completed 12 full months of service. Annual leave is paid at the employee's normal rate of pay. Annual leave can not be carried over from year to year. Any accrued time not taken before December 31 will be lost. Annual leave will only be allowed in increments of one-quarter days. 
(b)	Annual leave is accrued based on the following schedule: 

 
(c)	A new employee may not request annual leave until they have worked continually for an initial period of 12 months with the city. This waiting period is necessary for orientation, training and evaluation purposes. 
(d)	Annual leave may be used for any purpose. Requests for foreseeable leave shall be submitted for approval to the city manager at least two weeks in advance of the employee's scheduled leave. Whenever possible, leave must be approved in advance to ensure that the timing is mutually convenient for the employee, other employees, and the city. Consequently, it is advisable to make requests well in advance for popular periods (e.g., school vacations). 
(e)	In the event that two or more staff request leave for the same time or period, and all requests cannot be accommodated, the city manager and supervisor will make a determination, taking into account individual circumstances and the time of application. 
(f)	In the event of unforeseeable leave, as with any absence, an employee must call in if he is unable to report to work. 
(g)	Upon resignation or termination, any accrued but unused annual leave will be included in the employee's final pay calculation. An employee who resigns without giving two weeks' notice will not receive payment for accrued but unused annual leave. Employees who are terminated will be paid for no more than 30 days of accrued, unused annual leave. 
Sec. 62-102. - Sick leave. 
Sick leave will be accumulated at the rate of one-fourth day per month for all city employees. Sick leave not taken will accumulate toward the employee's retirement credit. Any employee out of work for three consecutive days due to illness must have a certification from a doctor pertaining to the cause of illness. If the statement is not obtained, the employee will not be paid for this time off. 
Chapter 66 - SOLID WASTE 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 66-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Commercial solid waste refers to all types of solid waste generated by stores, offices, restaurants, warehouses and other nonmanufacturing activities, excluding residential and industrial wastes. 
Composting means the controlled biological decomposition of organic matter into a stable, odor-free humus. 
Garbage means food waste, including waste accumulation of animal or vegetable matter used for or intended for food or that attends the preparation, use, cooking, dealing in or storing of meat, fish, fowl, fruit, or vegetables. 
Hazardous waste means material in a solid or semi-solid resulting from the manufacturing or use of pesticides on drugs (other than normal household use), pathological wastes, chemical wastes, flammable or explosive materials, and similar waste material in a solid or semi-solid state, that the city may consider a likely hazard to the public health or safety, except radioactive waste materials, as provided in rules of the state department of natural resources with regard to radioactive materials. 
Industrial waste or industrial solid waste means the solid waste materials from factories, processing plants and manufacturing enterprises, and includes food processing wastes, meat and poultry processing waste, condemned food, ashes and cinders from power plants, agriculture products waste, land clearance waste, and similar waste. 
Leachate collection system means a system at a landfill for collection of the leachate that may percolate through the waste and into the soils surrounding the landfill. 
Municipal solid waste means any solid waste derived from households, including garbage, trash and sanitary waste in septic tanks and includes solid waste from single-family and multifamily residences, hotels and motels, bunkhouses, campgrounds, picnic grounds, and day use recreation areas. The term "municipal solid waste" includes yard trimmings and commercial solid waste, but does not include solid waste from mining, agricultural or silvacultural operations or industrial processes or operations.
