Municipal solid waste disposal facility means any facility or location where the final deposition of any amount or municipal solid waste occurs, whether or not mixed with or including commercial or industrial solid waste, including, but not limited to, municipal solid waste landfills. 
Municipal solid waste landfill means a disposal facility where any amount of municipal solid waste, whether or not mixed with or including commercial waste, industrial waste, nonhazardous sludge or small quantity generator hazardous waste, is disposed of by means of placing an approved cover thereon. 
Person means any person, partnership, public or private corporation, association, institution, individual or other entity. 
Premises means land, buildings or other structures, vehicles, watercraft, or parts thereof, upon or in which solid waste is stored. 
Rubbish means a variety of combustible and noncombustible waste not subject to rapid decomposition derived from places or residence, commercial areas and institutions and shall include paper, rags, plastics, cartons, boxes, tree and yard trimmings, furniture, appliances, metals, minerals, cans, bottles, glass, crockery, excelsior, bedding, rubber, discarded clothing and similar materials. 
Scavenge means uncontrolled picking from discarded solid waste materials. 
Solid waste means putrescible and nonputrescible waste, except human body waste, and shall include garbage, rubbish, paper, cartons, boxes, wood, tree branches, yard trimmings, furniture, appliances, metals, tin cans, glass, crockery, dunnage, ashes, street refuse, dead animals, waste materials generated in industrial operations, residue incineration, food processing wastes, demolition wastes, construction wastes, and any other wastes in a solid or semi-solid state, not otherwise defined in this article. 
Waste means unwanted or discarded material, except human body waste. 
Yard trimmings means leaves, brush, grass clippings, shrub and tree prunings, discarded Christmas trees, nursery and greenhouse vegetative residuals, and vegetative matter resulting from landscaping development and maintenance, other than mining, agricultural and silvacultural operations. 
(Ord. of 12-9-1996, § 1A; Ord. of 11-10-2014(2)) 
Secs. 66-2—66-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - GARBAGE COLLECTION 

Sec. 66-21. - Collection by city. 
All solid waste generated or accumulated in the areas served by the city shall be collected, transported and disposed of by the city through its designated agents, employees, or contract representative. No other person shall collect, transport or dispose of any solid waste generated or accumulated in the city unless specifically authorized by the city; provided, however, that this section shall not prohibit the producers of industrial solid waste or the owner of premises upon which industrial solid waste has accumulated from collecting, transporting and disposing of such waste in accordance with rules and regulations established by the state department of natural resources but only if such service is not provided by the city. 
(Ord. of 11-10-2014(2)) 
Sec. 66-22. - Prohibited disposal and accumulation. 
No person shall place any solid waste in any stream, lake or other body of water. Any unauthorized accumulation of solid waste on any premises is hereby declared to be a nuisance and is prohibited. Failure to remove any existing accumulation of solid waste within such reasonable time as may be fixed by written notice of the mayor and council shall be deemed a violation of these regulations and a public nuisance subject to the abatement provisions of chapter 38. 
(Ord. of 11-10-2014(2)) 
Sec. 66-23. - Garbage containers. 
(a)	Use required . No person shall dispose of any solid waste for collection or other purposes, except in the proper containers as provided by this article. 
(b)	Provided by city; fees . Solid waste containers shall be provided by the city for the fee established by the city council and shall be maintained in good condition by the city or its designees or contract representatives. 
(c)	Container specifications and maintenance . Each container shall be durable, rust-resistant, nonabsorbent, watertight, rodent proof, and easily cleaned. Containers shall be equipped with suitable handles and tightfitting covers and shall have a capacity of not more than 32 gallons. Containers failing to comply with these provisions or with sharp or jagged edges or with defects liable to hamper or injure the person collecting the contents thereof shall be promptly replaced. 
(d)	Plastic bags . Plastic bags of a type, size and material designed for solid waste storage and disposal may be used to contain garbage and rubbish for storage and collection. Disposable bags shall be unbroken and securely sealed and loaded in a manner that normal handling will not cause the bag to open. 
(Ord. of 11-10-2014(2)) 
Sec. 66-24. - Preparation and storage of garbage prior to collection. 
(a)	Draining maximum weight and length . Garbage and rubbish shall be drained of excess liquid before being placed for collection. Rubbish may be placed in containers not over 50 pounds gross weight when placed for collection or in bundles not over 50 pounds each. Limbs or cuttings shall be not over four feet in length and four inches in diameter. Larger items in size or weight may be handled at special fees to be determined by the city. All containers shall be free of sand and rocks. 
(b)	Placement for pickup . Solid waste to be collected by the city or its representative shall be placed on the curb or roadway in front of the residence or establishment in which it accumulated, but not on the sidewalk or in the gutter. City garbage personnel will not collect garbage inside any establishment or place of business. Business or establishment containers shall be in one central location for easy access by workers. If property is fenced in, cans will be placed outside of the fence for collection and placed back over the fence when emptied. Containers are to be placed on the city street property for garbage collection only and must be promptly removed after each collection. 
(Ord. of 11-10-2014(2)) 
Sec. 66-25. - Scavenging of containers. 
No person other than owner thereof, or an agent or employee of the city, or any employee of a person holding a contract with the city for collection of solid waste shall interfere with any container placed for the purpose of storing solid waste pending collection, or remove or take any of the contents thereof, or remove any such container from the location where the same shall have been placed by the owner thereof. 
(Ord. of 11-10-2014(2)) 
Sec. 66-26. - Classification of solid waste; prohibited classes. 
(a)	Acceptable solid waste . Only the following classes of solid waste shall be acceptable for collection by the city: 
(1)	Garbage and rubbish, as defined in this chapter. 
(2)	Ashes, the residue from burning of combustible materials for fuel. 
(3)	Small dead animals, not over 30 pounds in weight, if kept separate from garbage and rubbish, will be collected without change; provided that a charge will be made for all such animals collected from animal hospitals, kennels, pet shops and the like. Owners of large dead animals shall be responsible for their removal and disposal. 
(b)	Unacceptable solid waste . The following classes of solid shall not be acceptable for collection by the city: 
(1)	Materials resulting from the construction or demolition of a building, such as plaster, mortar, broken masonry, scrap lumber, roofing or similar materials. 
(2)	Hazardous waste as defined by state law. 
(3)	Dead animals weighing more than 30 pounds. 
(4)	Industrial solid waste as defined herein. 
(5)	Old vehicle tires. 
(6)	Fence wire. 
(Ord. of 11-10-2014(2)) 
Secs. 66-27—66-55. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - YARD TRIMMINGS 

Sec. 66-56. - Placement for disposal. 
It shall be unlawful to place or mix leaves or yard trimmings with municipal solid waste within the city. 
(Ord. of 12-9-1996, § 1B; Ord. of 11-10-2014(2)) 
Sec. 66-57. - Sorting, storing, composting and collecting. 
Leaves and grass clippings must be placed in a biodegradable container and placed by curbside for pickup. Brush, shrub, tree prunings, and discarded Christmas trees will be placed by curbside for pickup. 
(Ord. of 12-9-1996, § 1C; Ord. of 11-10-2014(2)) 
Chapter 70 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS, AND OTHER PUBLIC PLACES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Authority of municipality to improve and maintain streets, O.C.G.A. § 36-39-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 70-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Public place means a street, alley, sidewalk or other public property owned by the city or under its supervision. 
Sec. 70-2. - Littering prohibited. 
No person shall place any garbage, rubbish, trash, paper or any litter of any kind whatsoever upon any street, sidewalk, alley, park, lane or other public grounds of the city. 
Sec. 70-3. - Limited use of sidewalks. 
It shall be unlawful to ride bicycles, skates or skateboards on city sidewalks in front of business establishments during normal business hours. 
Secs. 70-4—70-24. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PROHIBITED OBSTRUCTIONS 

Sec. 70-25. - Obstructing ditches, drains. 
It shall be unlawful, and a public nuisance, for any person to fill up any ditch or drain in any of the streets or alleys of the city or to purposely place any obstruction therein to prevent the free flow of water. 
Sec. 70-26. - Obstructing streets, sidewalks. 
It shall be unlawful, and a public nuisance, for any person to convert any public street, sidewalk or alley in the city to his use, or place, or cause to be placed, any obstruction in or upon them, such as wood, barrels and boxes, merchandise, timber or lumber, except necessarily for building purposes and such obstruction shall be moved by the police or street department at the expense of the owner thereof or the person causing said obstruction; provided, however, that this section shall not prohibit the placing or goods, wares, merchandise, produce, boxes, barrels, or other articles on the sidewalks within three feet from the wall of a building owned by the person placing such article. 
Sec. 70-27. - Placing trash receptacles on right-of-way. 
It shall be unlawful, and a public nuisance, for any person to place or cause to be placed any dumpster or other type of trash receptacle in the right-of-way area of any city street except the placing of garbage on the sidewalk at the curb on garbage day. 
Sec. 70-28. - Obstructing view of intersection. 
It shall be unlawful, and a public nuisance, for the opener or person in charge of any lot, parcel or piece of land within the city to allow any obstructions to vision in the triangle formed by the lines of two intersecting streets, or a street and an alley and line joining points of such lines 25 feet distant from their point of intersection by permitting any vegetation to grow or be maintained between the heights of three feet and ten feet above the grade of the centerline of the intersection, or by constructing or maintaining any fence or other structure which constitutes an obstruction to view within the triangle. 
Secs. 70-29—70-59. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - EXCAVATIONS 

Sec. 70-60. - Permit required. 
No person shall dig or excavate in any public place within the city or do any other work in or on any public place, which requires the removal or breaking of the surface or under part of any such public place, unless and until such person shall have first secured, in the manner provided in this article, permission to do so. 
Sec. 70-61. - Application. 
Each person desiring permission to dig or excavate in any public place shall file with the city clerk a written or printed application, setting forth the character and location of such work to be done in any such public place, the probable number of square yards of surface to be removed and the probable date of beginning and completion of the work. 
Sec. 70-62. - Fees and deposits. 
In the event the applicant for the permit to excavate is qualified to perform the work himself, including replacing the street to its condition prior to the excavation, there shall be no charge for the issuance of the permit. If the city must fill and resurface the street or public way, the applicant shall deposit with the city at the time of application, a sum of money that shall be fixed by the city superintendent and shall be based on the cost per square yard of replacement plus ten percent. 
Sec. 70-63. - Grant or refusal of permit. 
Each application for an excavation permit shall be delivered by the city clerk to the city superintendent, who shall without unreasonable delay, either grant or reject such application. Upon rejection of the application, the applicant shall have the right to present the matter to the mayor and council, the order of which shall be final in such matter, and upon final rejection, the deposit shall be returned to the person who deposited the same. 
Sec. 70-64. - Failure to complete or restore. 
Upon the failure of any person, whose application to dig or excavate shall have been granted and who shall have begun the work, to complete the same without delay, or upon the completion of such work, to restore the public place to the same or as good a condition as the same was before such work was done, or to comply with any reasonable rules or regulations of the city superintendent from time to time given to such person for the completion and restoration of such public place, such person shall upon conviction, in addition to other penalties, forfeit to the city any deposit of money so made with the city clerk. 
Sec. 70-65. - Restoration by city. 
Upon the failure of any person to make such repairs, in the manner herein required, and in the time herein required, the city superintendent is empowered and authorized to cause such repairs to be made and such public place to be restored to its original condition, and the cost thereof, plus ten percent thereof, shall be charged to and paid by such person who so failed to make such repairs, and such sum of money shall constitute and be a debt due from such person to the city. 
Sec. 70-66. - Use or refund of deposit. 
The deposit required by this article shall stand as a guarantee and may be employed by the city for the replacement of such public place in as good condition as the same was immediately before the excavation or digging and upon default of the person so making such deposit to restore immediately the public place to as good condition as the same was immediately before such excavation or digging was done by him, the city superintendent may employ the whole or any part of such deposit of money necessary for such restoration. Upon the restoration of the public place to such condition as the same was immediately before such digging or excavating, the city clerk shall, upon the certificate of the city superintendent, restore to the person so making such deposit such sum of money so deposited, or in case any part thereof is employed by the city for such restoration of such public place, upon such certificate, the city clerk shall refund such part of such sum of money remaining. 
Sec. 70-67. - Prompt work. 
All digging or excavating to be done, as provided in this article, shall be promptly started and completed without delay after permission shall have been granted, and such public place shall be, immediately upon the completion of such work, restored to the same or as good condition as the same was before such work was done thereon. Such work or restoration shall be at all times and in all respects in compliance with the orders and supervision of the city superintendent from time to time given to such person for such purpose. 
Sec. 70-68. - Warning devices; posting permit. 
Upon the granting of an application for permission to dig or excavate in any public place, and in all other cases provided for in this article, it shall be the duty of the applicant, before beginning any such work, to enclose the place where such work is being done or otherwise afford adequate protection to street traffic. He shall post and keep posted at such place a placard showing that the work is being done under a permit granted by the city, with sufficient other information thereon to give ample warning to those using the public place that the same is out of repair or being repaired, and in addition thereto, he shall place sufficient markings at night with required lights, to notify those having the right to use the same that such public place, or part thereof, is closed. 
Sec. 70-69. - Decision of council final. 
Any controversy between the person making a deposit in order to dig or excavate in any public place and the city clerk or city superintendent respecting any of the duties to be performed by any of them, may be submitted to the mayor and council by any of the parties, and when so submitted, the action of the mayor and council thereon shall be binding on all the parties. 
Secs. 70-70—70-96. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - SPEED BRAKES 

Sec. 70-97. - Council approval required. 
Installation of speed brakes or ripples on any street within the corporate limits of the city shall require advance approval by the city council. Approval shall be sought using the procedure provided in this article. 
Sec. 70-98. - Petition. 
Persons desiring to have speed brakes or ripples installed on a city street shall file a written petition with the city clerk. The petition must include, at a minimum, the name of the street where such speed brakes or ripples are requested and the typewritten names and residence addresses and signatures of no less than 90 percent of property owners who own property bounding said street requesting that such speed brakes or ripples be installed. 
(Ord. of 10-13-2003; Ord. of 2-9-2004) 
Sec. 70-99. - Review by council; reconsideration. 
The clerk, after verifying that the petition contains the minimum requirements set forth in this article, shall submit the petition to the city council for consideration at the next regularly scheduled meeting occurring after the filing date of the petition. The city council shall either approve or deny the petition as it deems appropriate in its sole discretion. If the petition is denied, is shall not be again filed with the city until at least 12 calendar months has passed since the date of denial. 
(Ord. of 10-13-2003; Ord. of 2-9-2004) 
Secs. 70-100—70-126. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - CITY STREETS 

Sec. 70-127. - Standards for acceptance. 
Notwithstanding any other provision of this Code, a city street may be accepted and dedicated as a city street by the city council, provided that all of the following criteria are met: 
(1)	The city owns property that was formerly an airport runway, but which has been closed as an airport runway; 
(2)	The property is within the city limits; 
(3)	The property would be suitable for use as a public street, regardless of whether such property is paved, curbed, and guttered; and 
(4)	The persons or entities other than the city own property abutting such proposed street. 
Sec. 70-128. - Paving, guttering, and utility services. 
(a)	A proposed street may be accepted and dedicated as a public street notwithstanding the fact that it does not have existing curbing and guttering, and that it does not meet the standards for acceptance by the city as a public street as more particularly established in other provisions of the city Code. Upon acceptance of a street, the city shall be under no obligation to pave, curb, or gutter the street or to provide utility services to property or property owners abutting such city street. No unpaved street shall be accepted by the city for ownership and maintenance. 
(b)	No service roads, rights-of-way or driveways shall be accepted by the city for ownership and maintenance until such have been hard surfaced with asphalt or concrete and maintained in good condition for a period of two years. 
Secs. 70-129—70-154. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - STREET NAMING 

Sec. 70-155. - City council to have power, authority. 
The city council shall have the sole power and authority to name and rename new and existing streets owned by and located within the city and shall bear the costs thereof except as otherwise provided herein. 
(Ord. of 8-14-2006, §§ 2, 3) 
Sec. 70-156. - Petition for street renaming. 
Citizens may request the renaming of existing city streets upon the written petition of not less than 75 percent of the persons owning real property abutting the street sought to be renamed, filed with the city clerk. The petition shall indicate thereon the existing name of the street, the proposed new name of the street, the printed name, street address, and signature of each property owner signing such petition, and the date that each property owner signed such petition. The petition shall also include a brief written statement, in succinct detail, of the reasons for the proposed street renaming in honor of the particular person or business listed. Each of the factors to be considered by the board, as set forth in this article, shall be addressed by the petitioner in the written statement. 
(Ord. of 8-14-2006, § 5) 
Sec. 70-157. - Validation by clerk. 
The clerk shall have 30 calendar days from the date of filing of the petition to validate the petition. Validation occurs when the clerk verifies that the proper number of signatures are contained on the petition, that signatures to be counted toward the 75 percent threshold meet the requirements of this article, and that the persons signing the petition are owners of real property abutting the street sought to be renamed, except as otherwise provided herein. If the clerk finds that the petition is not valid, it shall be returned to the applicant. No petition shall be considered by the council until validated by the clerk. 
Sec. 70-158. - Calculation of percentage of property owners. 
In determining the proper percentage of persons signing a petition for street renaming: 
(1)	If property is owned by more than one person, the signature of only one such owner shall be counted. 
(2)	Persons who rent or lease real property abutting the street sought to be renamed may sign the petition, but their signatures shall not be counted toward the 75 percent threshold. 
(3)	Signatures dated more than 90 calendar days prior to the date of filing of the petition shall be invalid and shall not be counted toward the 75 percent threshold. 
Sec. 70-159. - Consideration of petition for renaming. 
Validated petitions for street renaming shall be submitted by the city clerk to the council. The council shall either grant or deny the petition within 90 calendar days of the date it is submitted to the council by the clerk. If the council does not act on the petition prior to the expiration of 90 calendar days from the date the petition is submitted to the council by the clerk, the street shall automatically be renamed as requested in the petition, subject only to the payment by the petitioners of the fees and costs required as provided in this article. 
Sec. 70-160. - Denial of petition. 
If the proposed renaming is not approved by the city council, then no petition seeking to rename said street shall be accepted by the city clerk for a period of six calendar months from the date of the denial of the street renaming petition. 
Sec. 70-161. - Approval of petition. 
If the petition for street renaming is approved by the city council, the name change shall take effect at such time as is established by the council, but not sooner than upon payment of the costs of renaming as provided in this article. 
Sec. 70-162. - Waiting list for street renaming. 
The council shall consider request to name or rename a particular street or to use a particular name in reference to any street. If, in the sole discretion of the council, the name proposed is acceptable, but there is no street appropriate for renaming, the approved name shall be placed on a waiting list to be maintained by the city clerk. The approved name will be assigned from the waiting list by the council as it deems appropriate. 
Sec. 70-163. - Costs of renaming; failure to pay. 
Upon approval of a petition for street naming, the petitioners shall pay to the city clerk the renaming fee established by the city council to cover the cost and expense of the renaming. Such payment shall be deposited into the general fund of the city. If the street renaming costs are not paid to the city clerk within 30 calendar days of the date of approval of the petition, the street renaming shall not be effective for any purposes whatsoever and shall be deemed repealed as of the 31st day after initial approval of the petition. 
(Ord. of 8-14-2006, § 4) 
Sec. 70-164. - Naming a street after a natural person. 
In making a determination regarding naming or renaming a street to a name derived from the name of a living or deceased natural person, the city council shall take into consideration the following: 
(1)	Whether the person has resided for a long period of time on such street; 
(2)	Whether the person has made significant and long-lasting contributions to the city and its citizens; 
(3)	Whether the person is a national or internationally prominent figure who has or may have a direct or indirect connection to the city and its citizens; 
(4)	Whether the person has provided charitable or philanthropic contributions to the city and its citizens; 
(5)	Whether the person has brought honor, prestige, or recognition in a positive manner to the city and its citizens; 
(6)	Whether the person is a leader in local governmental, civic, educational, or public affairs; 
(7)	Whether the person is a distinguished and accomplished scholar, scientist, educational leader, business leader, government leader, or civic leader; or 
(8)	Such other factors as the city council deems applicable. 
Sec. 70-165. - Naming a street after a business entity. 
No street shall be named after any ongoing business that is not located upon the street to be named in honor of such business. In considering naming or renaming a street to a name derived from or consisting of a business name, the city council shall consider the following: 
(1)	Whether the business is located upon such street; 
(2)	The length of time that such business has been located on such street; 
(3)	The length of time that such business has been located within the city; 
(4)	The civic, community, and educational contributions of the business to the city and its citizens; 
(5)	The length of time that such business is expected to remain in business under the same name on such street; or 
(6)	Such other factors as the city council deems relevant. 
Sec. 70-166. - Changing street signs without authority. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to place, or cause to be placed, any sign designating a street, avenue or other public place by a different name than that by which it is generally and legally known, or to refuse to remove the same from his property when requested to do so by an officer of the city. 
Sec. 70-167. - Injuring or removing street signs. 
It shall be unlawful for any person willfully and maliciously to injure, deface or remove any of the street signs posted at or near the corner of the streets in the city. 
Secs. 70-168—70-187. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - STREET NUMBERING 

Sec. 70-188. - Designation. 
All official addresses shall be designated by the 911 coordinator. 
Sec. 70-189. - Duty to number; removal of prior number. 
The owner, occupant or person in charge of any structure to which a number has been assigned shall affix the number in a conspicuous place as set forth in this article. It shall be the duty of such owner, occupant or person in charge of the structure upon affixing the new number to remove any different number that might be mistaken for or confused with the number assigned to the structure by the 911 coordinator. 
Sec. 70-190. - Placement of numbers. 
All structures shall have the correct address posted on the structure, or at the entrance to the property as provided for in this article, where it will be clearly visible to persons or vehicles approaching the structure. When a structure is more than 35 feet from the road, or when the view of the structure is blocked by trees, shrubs or other material, the numbers shall be on a tree, mailbox, fence, gate or lawn stake at the entrance to the property on the same side of the road as the entrance to the property and clearly visible and legible from the road. On corner lots, numbers shall be displayed on the frontage to which the structure is facing. If more than one structure has a single access, the principal address shall be displayed at the access and subaddresses displayed on the structure to which they apply. This is applicable to apartments, condominiums and manufactured home parks as well as other multi-structure facilities. 
Sec. 70-191. - Size and color of numbering. 
All addresses shall be legible and shall be large enough to be seen easily from the street. The 911 coordinator recommends that each number be a minimum of three inches square. Numbers shall be of contrasting color to their background for easy visibility. Numbers shall be easily visible at night. 
Sec. 70-192. - Enforcement. 
If the owner, agent or occupant of an officially addressed structure shall neglect or refuse to affix or inscribe the proper numbers as required by this article, the city building official or his designee shall serve notice on the owner, agent or occupant. The numbers shall be properly affixed to the property in accordance with this article within ten days of the service of notice. After expiration of this ten-day period, such owner, agent or occupant may be fined as set forth in this section and the numbers caused to be affixed by the city building official or his designee. Any person who fails to affix or takes down, alters, injures or defaces any number affixed or inscribed to a structure pursuant to this article, shall be subject to a fine not to exceed $100.00. 
Secs. 70-193—70-222. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VIII. - TENTS 

Sec. 70-223. - Use restricted. 
No tent measuring greater than ten feet by ten feet shall be erected in the city without prior permission of the city council. All requests for the raising of a tent larger than ten feet by ten feet shall be submitted 30 days prior to the date the tent is needed. The duration of the tent event shall not be greater than 21 days. This article shall not apply to tents erected for funeral or civic function purposes. 
(Ord. of 3-12-2001(1), §§ 1, 2, 6, 7) 
Sec. 70-224. - Electrical inspection; fee. 
If electricity will be used in the tent structure, an electrical inspection must be performed. The person seeking approval for the use of the tent shall pay a fee for each inspection in the amount established by the city council. 
(Ord. of 3-12-2001(1), § 3) 
Sec. 70-225. - Toilet facilities. 
The person authorized to use a tent must make arrangements for the disposal of human waste in accordance with the health codes of the state. 
(Ord. of 3-12-2001(1), § 4) 
Sec. 70-226. - Presentation of business license. 
If the tent is being used for commercial purposes, a copy of a valid business license must be presented at the time of request to raise a tent. 
(Ord. of 3-12-2001(1), § 5) 
Secs. 70-227—70-245. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IX. - PUBLIC ASSEMBLY 

Sec. 70-246. - Public addresses, demonstrations; consent required. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to participate in any public address or demonstration in the corporate limits of said city unless written consent therefor has been granted by the mayor and council. 
Sec. 70-247. - Permits for parades and processions. 
No funeral, procession, or parade containing 50 or more persons or five or more vehicles, excepting the United States military forces, shall march, or proceed along any street except in accordance with permission issued by the chief of police and such other regulations as are set forth in this chapter which may apply. 
Secs. 70-248, 70-249. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE X. - PERMITS FOR SPECIAL ACTIVITIES TO BE HELD ON PUBLIC PROPERTY 

Sec. 70-250. - Permits for special activities. 
(a)	This article is intended to apply to special activities proposed to be held on public property within the city. Any organization wishing to sponsor or hold a special activity upon or within public property in the city will be required to complete the city's special activity permit application and obtain approval of such special activity as provided in this article. 
(b)	As required by this article a special activity within the city that will be conducted on the streets, in the parks, in other public areas, or on or within public property owned or operated by the city, must be approved by the city manager. Applications to conduct a special activity must be made in writing to the office of the city manager. Applications shall be available from the city clerk's office. Applications shall be submitted to the city manager office no later than 30 days prior to the date of the actual event. No special activity shall be permitted within the city unless such special activity is approved by the city manager. 
(c)	The city may hold its own special activities, or it may contract with one or more organizations to perform special activity services, or it may jointly sponsor a special activity with one or more organizations. In such cases, the participating organization shall submit a special activity permit application that shall include a presentation of the city's financial participation, if any, and the financial participation of the related organizations. In the event that the city decides to hold its own special activities, no special activity permit shall be required. 
(d)	The city manager shall undertake a complete review of any special activity application, including consultation with the applicant as may be reasonably necessary to resolve problems, at no charge to event sponsors. Upon completion of such review, the city manager shall determine whether the special activity permit should be approved or denied based upon the provisions of this article. In the event that the city manager is unable to determine whether or not a special activity permit should be issued to an applicant, or in the event that the city manager has substantial concerns or reservations as to whether the special activity permit should be issued or denied, then the city manager may submit the application to the mayor and city council for a determination as to whether the special activity permit should be issued, and the decision of the mayor and city council shall be final. Otherwise, the decision of the city manager as to the grant or denial of a special activity permit is final and not subject to appeal. 
(e)	Nothing in this section shall be construed to alter, affect or repeal the provisions of this Code that require parade permits to be issued by the chief of police under the appropriate ordinances applicable thereto. 
(Ord. of 8-8-2016) 
Sec. 70-251. - Basis for city services. 
(a)	The city will provide support to special activities on the following basis: 
(1)	City-operated activities . The city will operate certain special activities directly. The full cost of these special activities, if any, will be funded by the city. 
(2)	Co-sponsored activities . The city will co-sponsor certain activities with other organizations when the city manager determines that the activity is of general interest to the public and advances the city's purposes. The city will provide financial support to these activities as determined in the city's annual budget appropriation. These activities must meet the requirements of the special activities policy and any city costs in excess of the support level authorized by the budget appropriation, must be reimbursed to the city by the city's co-sponsor. 
(3)	Other nonprofit activities . Unless otherwise provided by the mayor and city council, the city may provide one person, if necessary, to act as a liaison between the city and the sponsors of a special activity operated by nonprofit organizations. These activities must meet the other requirements of the special activities permit policy and the sponsor must reimburse the city for any city costs in excess of this support level. 
(4)	Other for-profit activities . The city will allow other special activities operated by for-profit sponsors that are beneficial to the city and the public, subject to a rent charge for the use of the public property that is approved for each activity. These activities must meet the other requirements of the special activity permit policy and the sponsor must reimburse the city for any city costs in addition to the payment of established rent charges. 
(b)	The final decision as to what services the city shall provide under this section shall be made by the city manager, subject both to the terms of this article and the funds available for such services in the city's annual budget. 
(Ord. of 8-8-2016) 
Sec. 70-252. - Fees. 
Fees shall be charged for city services provided to special activities as follows: 
(1)	Straight time shall be the hourly cost for any employee working on a special activity during the normal work day including the actual cost for fringe benefits. 
(2)	Overtime shall be the hourly cost for any employee working on a special activity during a time period that would be considered overtime for city payroll records, including the actual cost for fringe benefits. 
(3)	Purchased or rented materials shall include all direct costs for all materials purchased or rented by the city for use at the activity. 
(4)	Equipment charges shall be the current equipment rental rates charged by the city. In addition thereto, for any authorized special activity where city electricity is required by the applicant, there shall be a charge of $25.00 per day for each day electricity is used by the sponsor at the site of the special activity. If separate booths are part of the special activity, whether such booths are sponsored by the applicant or by a third party, then the charge for electricity shall be $25.00 per day for each booth, which charge for booth electricity shall be in addition to the daily electricity charge for the special activity where the activity sponsor uses any city electricity at the site of the special activity. Such charge shall not be subject to waiver, and in the event that it is determined that the applicant/sponsor, or the sponsor of any booth, utilized city electrical services without advising the city of its intent to do so in the application for a special activity permit, then the applicant/sponsor, or booth sponsor, as the case may be, shall pay the sum of $100.00 per day for the use of such electricity. 
(5)	An application fee in the amount established by resolution adopted in accord with section 70-253 shall be paid at the time of application. The application fee is intended to cover the city's expenses related to approval of the permit application and related expenses. If a waiver of such fee is requested by a nonprofit corporation under this section, such waiver must be approved by the city manager at the time the application is approved, and if such waiver is granted, then the city, in its discretion, may either refund the application fee to the applicant or credit the application fee against other amounts owed by the applicant to the city under this article. Denial of the application shall not be grounds for waiver or refund of the application fee. An applicant shall only be entitled to a waiver of the application fee where the applicant provides written proof to the city manager that the applicant is a then-current nonprofit corporation exempt from the payment of income taxes in accord with 26 U.S.C. § 501(c). 
(Ord. of 8-8-2016) 
Sec. 70-253. - Billing for special activities. 
The mayor and city council shall be authorized to establish the hourly charges payable to the city to reimburse the city for the city's costs and expenses incurred in connection with an approved special activity. Such hourly charges shall be established by resolution of the mayor and city council from time to time as determined by said governing body. Billing for such amounts shall be submitted by the city to the sponsor of the special activity, and such billed amounts shall be paid by such sponsor with 15 days of the date of the bill. 
(Ord. of 8-8-2016) 
Sec. 70-254. - Rental charges for private for-profit activities. 
Special activities that are exclusively sponsored by private for-profit organizations shall be charged a reasonable rent for use of public areas, such as parks or streets, in addition to the special activity fees provided herein. The rent shall be set by the mayor and city council by resolution adopted in accord with section 70-253 hereof. 
(Ord. of 8-8-2016) 
Sec. 70-255. - Civic organizations and merchants' participation encouraged. 
It is the desire of the mayor and city council that local nonprofit organizations and local merchants in the vicinity of the special activity being held are given the opportunity to participate in the special activity to the greatest extent practical, consistent with the nature and purpose of the special activity. 
(Ord. of 8-8-2016) 
Sec. 70-256. - Liability insurance requirements. 
(a)	Except as otherwise provided herein, the city shall require that all sponsors of special activities purchase and maintain during the special activity liability insurance with coverage limits of at least $1,000,000.00, except for low-hazard activities as defined in subsection (c) of this section. Where liability insurance is required, an activity sponsor shall be required to provide a valid certificate of insurance naming the city as an additional or named insured prior to the activity. The city manager may require higher levels of insurance based upon risk factors and past experience. 
(b)	The city manager shall conduct a risk assessment in reviewing each special activity permit application. Based upon such review, the city manager shall determine whether the level of risk to the city resulting from the special activity should require the sponsor to purchase no liability insurance, the amounts of liability insurance provided in subsection (a) of this section, or additional liability insurance in excess of the amounts provided in subsection (a) of this section. Any amount of liability insurance to be purchased by the applicant in excess of the amounts established in subsection (a) of this section shall be as determined by the city manager. 
(c)	It shall be the policy of the mayor and city council to not routinely require insurance coverage for activities classified by the mayor and city council as low-hazard activities. These would be activities that include no physical activity by participants and no substantial exposure to spectators. This waiver of the insurance requirements is meant to cover small gatherings or ceremonies that do not involve more than 50 people, are limited to passive participation by the public, and require no city services. The sponsors of all other special activities are required to provide insurance as established in the manner set out in this article. 
(d)	When approving a special activity permit, the city manager may impose additional requirements as a condition of permit issuance. Such additional requirements may include, but shall not be limited to, specific staffing levels for police, fire, public works, or other personnel in connection with the activity. Expenses incurred by the city in compliance with such requirements shall be billed to and paid by the sponsoring organization as provided in this article. Agreement by the sponsoring organization to pay such additional expenses may be established as a condition of the issuance of the permit by the city manager. 
(Ord. of 8-8-2016) 
Sec. 70-257. - Traffic control and safety requirements. 
The sponsor of the special activity shall be responsible for complying with all traffic control and safety procedures required by the city during the activity. The requirements will be indicated in the notice of approval, and additional requirements may be made by the city from time to time during the activity as may be necessary for the safety of the public. 
(Ord. of 8-8-2016) 
Sec. 70-258. - Participant waiver of liability. 
The sponsor of the special activity shall be responsible for obtaining all signed indemnification and waiver of liability agreements as required by the city. 
(Ord. of 8-8-2016) 
Sec. 70-259. - Multiple applications for the same activity date. 
In the event that two or more special activity permit applications are received for the same date and time prior to the approval of either activity, the date and time that each application was received by the city shall determine the order of preference. Once a special activity permit has been granted, it shall be the policy of the mayor and city council to not award further permits for the same date, time, and general location. 
(Ord. of 8-8-2016) 
Sec. 70-260. - Reservation of annual activity dates. 
If an activity is intended to be an annual activity at regularly scheduled dates, the current year's application may include the following year's requested dates. Approval of the current year's application will include reservation of the next year's proposed dates. However, it will not constitute approval of next year's special activity permit, which must have its own timely application submitted for city approval. In general, no special activity permits shall be approved more than one year in advance. 
(Ord. of 8-8-2016) 
Sec. 70-261. - Confirmation of city approval. 
Upon approval or denial of the special activity permit application, a written confirmation of the decision of the city manager will be forwarded by the city manager to the individual or organization requesting the special activity permit. If there are any special conditions that must be met as a condition of the issuance of an approved special activity permit, such conditions shall be included in the written notice of approval of the special activity permit application. If the terms of such special activity permit, or any special conditions applicable to the special activity permit, are not complied with by the sponsor, then the city manager shall be authorized to revoke such special activity permit and written notice of such revocation shall be provided by the city manager to the sponsor by regular mail, by statutory overnight delivery, or by personal delivery, whichever is deemed appropriate by the city manager. 
(Ord. of 8-8-2016) 
Chapter 74 - SUBDIVISIONS 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 74-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Land subdivision means all divisions of a tract or parcel of land into two or more lots, building sites, or other divisions for the purpose, whether immediate or future, of sale, legacy, or building development; and includes immediate or future, of sale, legacy, or building development; and includes all divisions of land involving a new streets, a change in existing streets or the extension of water, sewer or gas lines and includes resubdivision and, where appropriate to the context, relates to the process of subdividing or to the land or area subdivided; provided, however, that the following are not included within this definition: 
(1)	The combination or recombination of portions of previously platted lots where the total number of lots is not increased and the resultant lots are equal to the standards of these regulations. 
(2)	The division of land into parcels of five acres or more where no new street is involved. 
Manufactured home means a detached, single-family dwelling unit designed for longterm occupancy; designed to be transported on its own wheels, arriving at the site where it is to be occupied as a dwelling unit complete, usually including major appliances and furniture and ready for occupancy. 
Manufactured home lot means a parcel of land for the placement of a single manufactured home and the exclusive use of its occupants. 
Manufacture home park means a parcel of land which has been planned and improved for the placement of manufactured homes for nontransit use. 
Manufactured home stand means that part of an individual manufactured home lot which has been reserved for the placement of a manufactured home and appurtenance structures. 
Planning commission means the official planning body for the city. 
Street includes streets, avenues, boulevards, roads, highways, expressways, lanes, alleys and other ways. 
Sec. 74-2. - Violation and penalty. 
Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be subject to penalties as set forth in section 1-10. Each day such violation continues shall constitute a separate offense. The city of any owner of real estate who would be damaged by such violation, in addition to other remedies, may institute injunction, mandamus or other appropriate action in proceeding to stop the violation. 
Secs. 74-3—74-43. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PLATTING JURISDICTION AND ENFORCEMENT 

Sec. 74-44. - Platting authority. 
From and after the passage of the ordinance from which this article is derived, the planning commission shall be the platting authority. 
Sec. 74-45. - Preliminary plat approval required prior to initiation of construction. 
No construction work shall be undertaken on a proposed land subdivision until a preliminary plat has been approved by the planning commission. 
Sec. 74-46. - Land subdivision plat recording. 
No plat of a land subdivision shall be accepted for recording in the office of the clerk of the superior court of the county except a final plat on which is inscribed the approval of the planning commission. 
Sec. 74-47. - Use of plat. 
The transfer of, sale, agreement to sell, or negotiation to sell land by reference to or exhibition of, or other use of a plat of a subdivision that has not been given final approval by the planning commission and recorded in the office of the clerk of the superior court of the county is prohibited, and the description by metes and bounds in the instrument of transfer or other document shall not exempt the transaction from such penalties. 
Sec. 74-48. - Erection of buildings. 
No building permit shall be issued and no building shall be erected on any lot unless the street giving access thereto has been accepted as a public street in accordance with this article, or unless such street had attained the legal status of a public street prior to the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived or has been accepted as a public street by the city council. 
Sec. 74-49. - Acceptance of and improvements in unapproved streets. 
The city council or other public authority shall not accept as a public street or shall not itself undertake or authorize the layout, opening, improving, grading, paving, lighting or the installation of water mains, sewers, connections or other facilities or utilities in any street unless such street is shown on a final plat approved by the planning commission or it had attained the legal status of a public street prior to the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived; provided, however, that the city council may locate, construct or accept any other street if the ordinance for such a street is first submitted to the planning commission for its review and approval. 
Secs. 74-50—74-71. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PREAPPLICATION 

Sec. 74-72. - Procedures. 
Before proceeding with a proposed land subdivision, developers are invited and encouraged to discuss their proposed development with the secretary of the planning commission. A very preliminary sketch of the proposed subdivision, together with a map of the area showing its principal features, will be helpful in this discussion. 
Secs. 74-73—74-102. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - PROCEDURE FOR APPROVAL OF PRELIMINARY PLAT 

Sec. 74-103. - Application for preliminary plat approval. 
The subdivider shall submit to the secretary of the planning commission, at least 15 days prior to the next regular meeting of the planning commission, the following: 
(1)	A letter requesting review and approval of a preliminary plat, giving the name and address of the person to whom the notice of the hearing by the planning commission on the preliminary plat shall be sent. 
(2)	Five copies of the preliminary plat and other documents, as specified in article V of this chapter. 
(3)	A preliminary plat filing fee in the amount established from time to time by the city council. 
Sec. 74-104. - Review of preliminary plat. 
(a)	The secretary of the planning commission shall check the plat for conformance to the regulations of this article and report his findings and recommendations to the planning commission, which shall afford a hearing on the preliminary plat, notice of the time and place of which shall be sent by the secretary of the planning commission by registered or certified mail to the person designated in the letter requesting preliminary plat review and approval, not less than five days prior to the date of the hearing. 
(b)	Thereafter, the planning commission shall approve or disapprove the preliminary plat. A notation of the action shall be made on two copies of the preliminary plat, including a statement of the reasons for disapproval of the preliminary plat is disapproved. One copy shall be returned to the subdivider or his agent and one copy added to the records of the planning commission. 
(c)	Approval of a preliminary plat does not constitute approval of a final plat. It indicates only approval of the layout as a guide to the preparation of the final plat. Preliminary plat approval shall expire and be null and void after a period of one year unless an extension of time is approved by the planning commission. 
(d)	If action on a preliminary plat is not taken by the planning commission within 30 days of the date of submittal, the preliminary plat shall be considered approved and a certificate of approval shall be issued on demand; however, the applicant for approval may waive this requirement and consent to an extension of time. 
Secs. 74-105—74-121. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - PRELIMINARY PLAT SPECIFICATIONS 

Sec. 74-122. - Preparation guidelines. 
Preliminary plats for subdivisions shall be prepared as follows: 
(1)	Scale. The preliminary plat shall be clearly and legibly drawn at a scale not smaller than 100 feet to one inch. 
(2)	Sheet size. Sheet size shall be 42 inches by 36 inches. If the complete plat cannot be shown on one sheet of this size, it may be shown on more than one sheet with an index map on a separate sheet of the same size. 
(3)	Information to be provided on preliminary plat. The preliminary plat shall contain the following information: 
a.	The name and address of the owner of record and of the subdivider. 
b.	The proposed name of subdivision and its acreage. 
c.	North arrow, graphic scale and date. 
d.	The vicinity map showing the location of the subdivision and developments in its vicinity. 
e.	Exact boundary lines of the tract by bearing and distances. 
f.	The names of owners of record of adjoining land. 
g.	Existing streets, utilities and easements on the land adjacent to the tract. 
h.	Contour lines at intervals of not more than five feet. 
i.	Proposed layout including streets and alleys with proposed street names, lot lines with approximate dimensions, easements, land to be reserved or dedicated for public uses, and any land to be used for purposes other than single-family dwellings. 
j.	Block numbers and lot numbers. 
k.	Provisions for water supply, sewerage and drainage. 
l.	Minimum building front yard setback lines. 
m.	Such street cross sections and centerline profiles as may be required by the planning commission. 
Sec. 74-123. - Certificate of approval. 
A certificate of approval of the preliminary plat by the planning commission shall be inscribed on the plat as follows: 
"Pursuant to the city Land Subdivision Regulations, all the requirements of approval having been fulfilled, this preliminary plat was approved by the planning commission on ____________ / ____________ / ____________ , 20 ____________ . 
This approval of the preliminary plat does not constitute approval of a final plat. This certificate of approval of the preliminary plat shall expire and be null and void on ____________ / ____________ / ____________ (Date)." 

 
Sec. 74-124. - Waiver of the preliminary plat procedure. 
The approval of the preliminary plat can be waived if so recommended by the secretary and approved by the planning commission. It deems necessary prior to such a recommendation for the secretary to determine if the subdivider has successfully, with good standing, completed a minimum of three subdivisions, of which at least two are in the city. The final approval authority of the waiver of the preliminary plat rests on the planning commission. 
Sec. 74-125. - Initiation of improvements. 
After a preliminary plat has been approved, no improvements in the land subdivision shall be undertaken until final engineering plans and specifications have been approved by the city. 
Secs. 74-126—74-148. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - FINAL PLAT PROCEDURE 

Sec. 74-149. - Application for final plat approval. 
After the preliminary plat of a proposed land subdivision has been approved by the planning commission, the subdivider may, within one year from approval, submit to the planning commission: 
(1)	A letter requesting review and approval of a final plat, giving the name and address of the person to whom the notice of the hearing by the planning commission on the final plat shall be sent. 
(2)	Five copies of the final plat and other documents, as specified in article VII of this chapter, the original of which shall be drawn in permanent ink on cloth or film. 
(3)	A final plat filing fee and a recording fee in the amount established from time to time by the city council. 
Sec. 74-150. - Review of final plat. 
The secretary of the planning commission shall check the final plat for the following requirements: 
(1)	Conformance with the approved preliminary plat and with the regulations of this article, and report his findings and recommendations to the planning commission, which shall afford a hearing on the final plat, notice of the time and place of which shall be sent by the secretary of the planning commission by registered or certified mail to the person designated in the letter requesting final plat review and approval, not less than five days prior to the date of the hearing. 
(2)	If the preliminary plat is waived by the planning commission according to the procedures and requirements outlined in section 74-124, the planning commission shall examine and approve the final plat using the plat specifications outlined in article VII of this chapter. 
(3)	The planning commission shall approve or disapprove the final plat. A notation of the action shall be made on the original tracing and two prints of the final plat, including a statement of the reasons therefor if the final plat is disapproved. If action of a final plat is not taken by the planning commission within 30 days of the date of the submittal, the final plat shall be considered approved and a certificate of approval shall be issued on demand; however, the applicant for approval may waive this requirement and consent to an extension of time. 
Sec. 74-151. - Recording of final plat. 
Upon approval of the final plat, the secretary of the planning commission shall have the plat recorded in the office of the clerk of the superior court of the county. The subdivider shall be responsible for the payment of the recording fee at the time of submitting the final plat as provided in section 74-149. Subsequent to the recording of the final plat, one copy on cloth or film and one additional copy with all certificates endorsed thereon shall be filed with the records of the planning commission. The Map Book, volume and page numbers where the plat is recorded shall also be indicated on the copies. 
Secs. 74-152—74-170. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - FINAL PLAT SPECIFICATIONS 

Sec. 74-171. - Final plat requirements. 
The final plat shall conform to and meet the specifications of the preliminary plat and the following additional specifications: 
(1)	The final plat shall be clearly and legibly drawn in permanent ink on tracing cloth or tracing film at a scale not smaller than 100 feet to one inch. Sheet sizes shall be 42 inches by 36 inches, and where more than one sheet is required, an index map shall be provided on the same size sheet. The final plat shall show: 
a.	Bearings and distances of the subdivision boundaries to the nearest existing street lines or bench marks or other permanent monuments (not less than three) accurately described on the plat. 
b.	Municipal, county and land lot lines accurately tied to the boundary lines of the subdivision by distance and angles when such lines traverse or are reasonably close to the subdivision. 
c.	Exact boundary lines of the tract, determined by a field survey, giving distances to the nearest one-tenth foot and angles to the nearest minutes, which shall be balanced and closed with an error of closure not to exceed one to 5,000. 
d.	The name of the subdivision, exact locations, width, and names of all streets and alleys within and immediately adjoining the plat. 
e.	Street centerlines showing angles of deflection, angles of intersection, radii, and lengths of tangents. 
f.	Lot lines with dimensions to the nearest one-tenth foot. 
g.	Lots numbered in numerical order and blocks lettered alphabetically. 
h.	Location, dimensions, and purposes of any easements and any areas to be reserved or dedicated for public use. 
i.	Accurate location, material, and description of monuments and markers. 
j.	A statement, either directly on the plat or in an identified attached document, of any private covenants. 
k.	The following certifications: 
1.	An engineer's or surveyor's certification, directly on the final plat as follows: 
"It is hereby certified that this plat is true and correct and was prepared from an actual survey of the property by me or under my supervision; that all monuments shown thereon actually exist or are marked as 'future', and their location, size, type and materials are correctly shown; and that all engineering requirements of the City Land Subdivision Regulations have been fully complied with." 
By: ____________ Registered P.E. No. ____________ 

 
By: ____________ Registered Georgia Land Surveyor No. ____________ 
2.	An owner's certification, directly on the final plat as follows: 
"The owner of the land shown on this plat and whose name is subscribed hereto, in person or through a duly authorized agent, certifies that this plat was made from an actual survey, that all state and city taxes or other assessments now due on this land have been paid." 

 
3.	A certificate by the owner setting forth the description of the areas and improvements he dedicates to the public and the extent of the title which he is dedicating should be attached to the final plat. Because of the legal consideration here, this certificate shall be approved as to form by the city attorney. 
4.	A certificate of approval of the final plat by the planning commission, directly on the plat, as follows: 
"Pursuant to the City Land Subdivision Regulations, all the requirements of approval having been fulfilled, this final plat was approved by the planning commission on ____________ , 20 ____________ ." 

 
(2)	In addition to the final plat, the subdivider shall present to the city one complete set of construction plans and drawings, including the following: 
a.	The actual location of all utility lines. 
b.	Profiles and invert elevations of all stormwater and sanitary sewer lines, as built. 
c.	Centerline profiles of all streets, as built. 
Secs. 74-172—74-195. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VIII. - REQUIREMENTS FOR IMPROVEMENTS, RESERVATION, AND DESIGN 

Sec. 74-196. - General improvements. 
(a)	Conformance to applicable rules and regulations. In addition to the requirements established herein, all subdivision plats shall comply with the following laws, rules, and regulations: 
(1)	All applicable statutory provisions. 
(2)	Chapter 94 (building and housing codes) and all other applicable laws of the appropriate jurisdictions. 
(3)	The official master plan, official map, public utilities plan and capital improvements program of the local government, including all streets, drainage systems, and parks shown on the official map or master plan as adopted. 
(4)	The special requirements of these regulations and any rules of the health department and/or appropriate state agencies. 
(5)	The rules of the state highway department if the subdivision or any lot contained therein abuts a state highway or connecting street. 
(6)	The standards and regulations adopted by the city's consulting engineer and all boards, commissions, agencies, and officials of the city. 
(7)	All pertinent standards contained within the planning guides published by the city planning commission. 
(8)	Plat approval may be withheld if a subdivision is not in conformity with the guidelines or policy and purposes of these regulations. 
(b)	Self-imposed restrictions. If the owner places restrictions on any of the land contained in the subdivision greater than those required by chapter 94 or these regulations, such restrictions or reference thereto may be required to be indicated on the subdivision plat, or the planning commission may require that restrictive covenants be recorded with the county recorder of deeds in a form to be approved by the city attorney. 
(c)	Plats straddling municipal boundaries. Whenever access to the subdivision is required across land in another local government, the planning commission may request assurance from the city attorney that access is legally established, and from the city's consulting engineer that the access road is adequately improved, or that a performance bond has been duly executed and is sufficient in amount to ensure the construction of the access road. In general, lot lines should be laid out so as not to cross municipal boundary lines. 
(d)	Monuments. The applicant shall place permanent reference monuments in the subdivision as required herein and as approved by a registered land surveyor. 
(1)	Monuments shall be located on street right-of-way lines, at street intersections, angle points of curve and block corners. They shall be spaced so as to be within sight of each other, the sight lines being contained wholly within the street limits. 
(2)	The external boundaries of a subdivision shall be monumented in the field by monuments of stone or concrete, not less than 30 inches in length, not less than four inches square or five inches in diameter, and marked on top with a cross, brass plug, iron rod, or other durable material securely embedded; or by iron rods or pipes at least 30 inches long and two inches in diameter. The monuments shall be placed not more than 1,400 feet apart in any straight line and at all corners, at each end of all curves, at the point where a curve changes its radius, at all angle points in any line, and at all angle points along the meander line, said points to be not less than 20 feet back from the bank of any stream, except that when such corners or points fall within a street, or proposed future street, the monuments shall be placed in the side line of the street. 
(3)	All internal boundaries and those corners and points not referred to in subsection (d)(2) of this section shall be monumented in the field by like monuments as described in subsection (d)(2) of this section. These monuments shall be placed at all block corners, at each end of all curves, at a point where a river changes its radius, and at all angle points in any line. 
(4)	The lines of lots that extend to streams shall be monumented in the field by iron pipes at least 30 inches long and seven-eights inch in diameter or by round or square iron bars at least 30 inches long. These monuments shall be placed at the point of intersection of the stream lot line. 
(5)	All monuments shall be properly set in the ground and approved by a registered land surveyor prior to the time the planning commission recommends approval of the final plat. 
(e)	Character of the land. Land which the planning commission finds to be unsuitable for subdivision or development due to flooding, improper drainage, steep slopes, rock formations, adverse earth formations or topography, utility easements, or other features which will reasonably be harmful to the safety, health, and general welfare of the present or future inhabitants of the subdivision and/or its surrounding areas, shall not be subdivided or developed unless adequate methods are formulated by the developer and approved by the planning commission to solve the problems created by the unsuitable land conditions. Such land shall be set aside for uses as shall not involve such a danger. 
(f)	Subdivision name. The proposed name of the subdivision shall not duplicate, or too closely approximate phonetically, the name of any other subdivision in the area covered by these regulations. The planning commission shall have final authority to designate the name of the subdivision, which shall be determined at preliminary plat approval. 
Sec. 74-197. - Lot improvements. 
(a)	Lot arrangement. The lot arrangement shall be such that there will be no foreseeable difficulties, for reasons of topography or other conditions, in securing building permits to build on all lots in compliance with chapter 94 and health regulations and in providing driveway access to buildings on such lots from an approved street. 
(b)	Lot dimensions. Lot dimensions shall comply with the minimum standards of chapter 94. Where lots are more than double the minimum required area for the zoning district, the planning commission may require that such lots be arranged so as to allow further subdivision and the opening of future streets where they would be necessary to serve such potential lots, all in compliance with chapter 94 and these regulations. In general, side lot lines shall be at right angles to street lines (or radial to curving street lines) unless a variation from this rule will give a better street or lot plan. Dimensions of corner lots shall be large enough to allow for the erection of buildings, observing the minimum front yard setback from both streets. Depth and width of properties reserved or laid out for business, commercial, or industrial purposes shall be adequate to provide for the off-street parking and loading facilities required for the type of use and development contemplated, as established in chapter 94. 
(c)	Double frontage lots and access lots. 
(1)	Double frontage and reverse frontage lots shall be avoided except where necessary to provide separation of residential development from traffic arterials or to overcome specific disadvantages of topography and orientation. 
(2)	Access from major and secondary arterials to lots shall not, in general, derive access exclusively from a major or secondary street. Where driveway access from a major or secondary street may be necessary for several adjoining lots, the planning commission may require that such lots be served by a combined access drive in order to limit possible traffic hazards on such street. Where possible, driveways should be designed and arranged so as to avoid requiring vehicles to back into traffic on major or secondary arterials. 
(d)	Soil preservation, grading, and seeding. 
(1)	No certificate of occupancy shall be issued until final grading has been completed in accordance with the approved final subdivision plat and the lot precovered with soil with an average depth of at least six inches, which shall contain no particles over two inches in diameter over the entire area of the lot, except that portion covered by buildings or included in streets, or where the grade has not been changed or natural vegetation seriously damaged. Topsoil shall not be removed from residential lots or used as spoil, but shall be redistributed so as to provide at least six inches of cover on the lots and at least four inches of cover between the sidewalks and curbs, and shall be stabilized by seeding or planting. 
(2)	Lots shall be laid out so as to provide positive drainage away from all buildings and individual lot drainage shall be coordinated with the general storm drainage pattern for the area. Drainage shall be designed so as to avoid concentration of storm drainage water from each lot to adjacent lots. 
(e)	Debris and water. No cut trees, timber, debris, earth, rocks, stones, soil, junk, rubbish, or other waste materials of any kind shall be buried in any land, or left or deposited on any lot or street at the time of the issuance of a certificate of occupancy, and removal of the same shall be required prior to issuance of any certificate of occupancy on a subdivision. Nor shall any be left or deposited in any area of the subdivision at the time of expiration of the performance bond or dedication of public improvements, whichever is sooner. 
(f)	Fencing. Each subdivider and/or developer shall be required to furnish and install fences wherever the planning commission determines that a hazardous condition may exist. The fences shall be constructed according to standards established by the city consulting engineer and shall be noted as to height and material on the final plat. No certificate of occupancy shall be issued until said fence improvements have been duly installed. 
(g)	Waterbodies and watercourses. If a tract being subdivided contains a water body, or portion thereof, lot lines shall be so drawn as to distribute the entire ownership of the water body among the fees of adjacent lots. The planning commission may approve an alternative plan whereby the ownership of and responsibility for safe maintenance of the water body is so placed that it will not become a local government responsibility. No more than 25 percent of the minimum area of a lot required under chapter 94 may be satisfied by land which is under water. Where a watercourse separates the buildable area of a lot from the street by which it has access, provisions shall be made for installation of a culvert or other structures, or design approved by the city consulting engineer. 
(h)	Excess right-of-way. Right-of-way widths in excess of the standards designated in these regulations shall be required whenever, due to topography, additional width is necessary to provide adequate earth slopes. Such slopes shall not be in excess of three to one. 
(i)	Railroads and limited access highways. Railroad rights-of-way and limited access highways where so located as to affect the subdivision of adjoining lands shall be treated as follows: 
(1)	In residential districts, a buffer strip at least 25 feet in depth in addition to the normal depth of the lot required in the district shall be provided adjacent to the railroad right-of-way or limited access highway. This strip shall be part of the platted lots and shall be designated on the plat: "This strip is reserved for screening. The placement of structure hereon is prohibited." 
(2)	In districts designated for business, commercial, or industrial uses, the nearest street extending parallel or approximately parallel to the railroad shall, wherever practicable, be at a sufficient distance therefrom to ensure suitable depth for commercial or industrial sites. 
(3)	Streets parallel to the railroad when intersecting a street which crosses the railroad at grade shall, to the extent practicable, be at a distance of at least 150 feet from the railroad right-of-way. Such distance shall be determined with due consideration of the minimum distance required for future separation of grades by means of appropriate approach gradients. 
Sec. 74-198. - Drainage and storm sewers. 
(a)	General requirements. The planning commission shall not recommend for approval any plat of subdivision which does not make adequate provision for stormwater or floodwater runoff channels or basins. The stormwater drainage system shall be separate and independent of any sanitary sewer system. Storm sewers, where required, shall be designed by the rational method, or other methods as approved by the planning commission, and a copy of design computations shall be submitted along with the plans. Inlets shall be provided so that surface water is not carried across or around any intersection, not for a distance of more than 600 feet in the gutter. When calculations indicate that curb capacities are exceeded at a point, no further allowance shall be made for flow beyond that point, and basins shall be used to intercept flow at that point. Surface water drainage patterns shall be shown for each and every lot and block. 
(b)	Nature of stormwater facilities. 
(1)	Location. The applicant may be required by the planning commission to carry away, by pipe or open ditch, any spring or surface water that may exist either previously to, or as a result of, the subdivision. Such drainage facilities shall be located in the road right-of-way where feasible, or in perpetual unobstructed easements of appropriate width, and shall be constructed in accordance with the construction standards and specifications. 
(2)	Accessibility to public storm sewers. 
a.	Where a public storm sewer is accessible, the applicant shall install storm sewer facilities, or if no outlets are within a reasonable distance, adequate provision shall be made for the disposal of stormwaters, subject to the specifications of the city's consulting engineer. However, in subdivisions containing lots less than 15,000 square feet in area and in business and industrial districts, underground storm sewer systems shall be constructed throughout the subdivisions and be conducted to an approved out-fall. Inspection of facilities shall be conducted by the city's consulting engineer. 
b.	If a connection to a public storm sewer will be provided eventually, as determined by the city's consulting engineer and the planning commission, the developer shall make arrangements for future stormwater disposal by a public utility system at the time the plat receives final approval. Provision for such connection shall be incorporated by inclusion in the performance bond required for the subdivision plat. 
(3)	Accommodation of upstream drainage areas. A culvert or other drainage facility shall, in each case, be large enough to accommodate potential runoff from its entire upstream drainage area, whether inside or outside the subdivision. The city's consulting engineer shall determine the necessary size of the facility, based on the provisions of the construction standards and specifications assuming conditions of maximum potential watershed development permitted by chapter 94. 
(4)	Effect on downstream drainage areas. The city's consulting engineer shall also study the effect of each subdivision on existing downstream drainage facilities outside the area of the subdivision. Local government drainage studies together with such other studies as shall be appropriate, shall serve as a guide to needed improvements.
