Properly shredded garbage means the wastes from the preparation, cooking, and dispensing of food that have been shredded to the degree that all particles will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing in public sewers, with no particle greater than one-half inch in any dimension. 
Public sewer means a common sewer controlled by a governmental agency or public utility. 
Sanitary sewer means a sewer that carries liquid and water-carried wastes from residences, commercial buildings, industrial plants, and institutions together with minor quantities of groundwater, stormwater, and surface waters that are not intentionally admitted. 
Septic tank means a subsurface impervious tank designed to temporarily retain sewage or similar waterborne wastes together with: 
(1)	A sewer line constructed with solid pipe, with the joints sealed, connecting the impervious tank with a plumbing stub out; and 
(2)	A subsurface system of trenches, piping, and other materials constructed to drain the clarified discharge from the tank and distribute it underground to be absorbed or filtered. 
Sewage is the spent water of a community. The equivalent term is "wastewater," as defined herein. 
Sewage works (sewerage) means all facilities for collecting, pumping, treating, and disposing of sewage. 
Sewer means a pipe or conduit that carries wastewater. 
Sludge means any discharge of water or wastewater which in concentration of any given constituent or in quantity of flow exceeds for any period of duration longer than 15 minutes more than five times the average 24 hour concentration of flows during normal operation and shall adversely affect the collection system or performance of the wastewater facilities. 
Storm drain (sometimes termed storm sewer ) means a drain or sewer for conveying water, groundwater, subsurface water, or unpolluted water from any source, and excluding sewage and industrial wastes other than unpolluted cooling water. 
Suspended solids means total suspended matter that either floats on the surface of, or is in suspension in, water, wastewater, or other liquids, and that is removable by laboratory filtration as approved by the EPA and referred to as nonfilterable residue. 
Unpolluted water is water of quality equal to or better than the effluent criteria in effect or water that would not cause violation of receiving water quality standards and would not be benefitted by discharge to the sanitary sewers and wastewater treatment facilities provided. 
Wastewater means the spent water of a community. From the stand-point of source, it may be a combination of the liquid and water-carried wastes from residences, commercial buildings, industrial plants, and institutions, together with any groundwater, surface water, and stormwater that may be present. 
Wastewater facilities means the structures, equipment, and processes required to collect, carry away, and treat domestic and industrial wastes and dispose of the effluent. 
Watercourse means a natural or artificial channel for the passage of water either continuously or intermittently. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996) 
Sec. 86-111. - Other applicable law. 
The provisions of this chapter shall not be deemed as alleviating compliance with applicable state and federal regulations. Specific user charge and industrial cost recovery requirements, promulgated pursuant to Public Law 92-500 (33 USC 1292) shall be considered as a part of this chapter upon official adoption. All nonresidential users will be required to comply with pretreatment standards as outlined in 40 CFR 403. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 9.1) 
Sec. 86-112. - Conflict of law or regulation. 
In the event a wastewater discharge is made to a publicly owned treatment works (POTW) under the jurisdiction of an approved sewer use chapter for another governing authority, the more restrictive requirement shall prevail. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 13.3) 
Sec. 86-113. - Sewer charges and fees. 
Each consumer subscribing to use the sewer service of the city shall pay a connection fee as established by the city council. All additional pipe and man-hours to run to a customer's property will be paid for by the customer at time of completion of work. 
Sec. 86-114. - Sewerage charges related to filling of swimming pools. 
(a)	A residential homeowner that is a water and sewerage customer of the city and who has either an in-ground or above-ground swimming pool shall be entitled to fill the swimming pool using city water without being required to pay city sewerage charges for water used to fill the swimming pool upon the following conditions, and through the following procedure: 
(1)	The homeowner must provide written evidence to the city of the capacity of the pool in gallons; 
(2)	The homeowner must provide written evidence to the city as to the actual amount of water used to fill the pool; 
(3)	The homeowner must provide written evidence of the date upon which the pool was filled under this article; 
(4)	The elimination of the sewerage charge for water used to fill swimming pools under this section shall only be allowed for one filling of the residential homeowner's pool each calendar year. 
(b)	Any residential homeowner who desires to eliminate the sewerage charge for water used for filling a swimming pool shall complete the written application for the sewerage charge reduction as may be required by the city clerk, and no such sewerage charge reduction under articles I through IV of this chapter shall be authorized unless the application is completed in its entirety. The completed application shall be filed by the residential homeowner with the city clerk. 
(c)	Any such application submitted by a residential homeowner under this section shall be submitted no later than ten calendar days prior to the end of the applicant's water/sewerage billing cycle, and any application submitted less than ten days prior to the end of the applicant's billing cycle shall be considered in connection with the next succeeding billing cycle. 
(d)	Upon a determination by the city clerk that the application is complete, that the facts set out in the application are accurate, and that the residential homeowner is entitled to the sewerage charge reduction as authorized in this article, the city shall deduct or eliminate the sewerage charge for the water used to fill the residential homeowner's pool from the monthly water and sewerage bill of the residential homeowner for the calendar month immediately following approval of the application from the homeowner. The appropriate city departments shall be authorized to assist the city clerk, review each application for elimination of the sewerage charge under this chapter and confirm that the facts set out in the application are accurate. 
(Ord. of 9-11-2006, § 18-30) 
Secs. 86-115—86-141. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - USE OF PUBLIC SEWERS 

Sec. 86-142. - Required. 
If the public sewer is within 1,000 feet of the property line, the owner of all houses, buildings, or properties used for human occupancy, employment, recreation, or other purposes situated within the city jurisdiction and abutting on any street, alley, or right-of-way in which there is now located or may in the future be located a public sanitary sewer of the city is hereby required, at the owner's expense, to install suitable toilet facilities, as provided herein, and to connect the facilities directly with the proper public sewer in accordance with the provisions of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 3.5) 
Sec. 86-143. - Time for compliance. 
In the event that the city discovers any house, building, or property used for human occupancy, employment, recreation or other purposes within the city limits that is required to be, and is not, in compliance with articles I through IV of this chapter, the owner shall have 30 days after date of official notice to do so, to bring the property into compliance with articles I through IV of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 3.5) 
Sec. 86-144. - Toilet facilities; disposal of human excrement. 
All premises shall be provided by the owner with at least one toilet. All toilets shall be kept clean and in a sanitary working condition. No person shall dispose of human excrement except in a toilet. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, §§ 3.1, 3.2) 
Sec. 86-145. - Prohibited systems. 
Except as otherwise provided herein, it shall be unlawful to construct or maintain any privy, privy vault, septic tank, cesspool, or other facility intended or used for the disposal of wastewater. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 3.4) 
Sec. 86-146. - Appliances and plumbing fixtures. 
All sinks, dishwashing machines, lavatories, basins, shower baths, bathtubs, laundry tubs, washing machines, and similar plumbing fixtures or appliances shall be connected to the public sewer; provided, that where no sewer is available, septic tanks or other private subsurface disposal facilities approved by the health officer may be used. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 3.6) 
Secs. 86-147—86-175. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - PROHIBITED DISCHARGES 

Sec. 86-176. - Generally. 
It shall be unlawful to discharge to any natural outlet within the city, or in any area under the jurisdiction of the city, any wastewater or other polluted waters, including septic tank effluent or cesspool overflow to any open drain or well-penetrating, water-bearing formation, except where suitable treatment has been provided in accordance with subsequent provisions of articles I through IV of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 3.3) 
Sec. 86-177. - Unpolluted and sanitary discharges prohibited. 
No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any unpolluted waters such as stormwater, groundwater, roof runoff, subsurface drainage, cooling water, or unpolluted industrial process waters to any sanitary sewer. No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any sanitary wastewater into a storm sewer system. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, §§ 6.1, 6.2) 
Sec. 86-178. - Chemical, toxic, corrosive and obstructing wastes prohibited. 
No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the following described water or wastes to any public sewers: 
(1)	Chemicals; explosives. Any gasoline, benzene, naptha, fuel oil, or other flammable or explosive liquid, solid, or gas. 
(2)	Toxic, poisonous, and hazardous substances. Any waters containing toxic or poisonous solids, liquids, or gases in sufficient quantity, either singly or by interaction with other wastes, to injure or interfere with any waste treatment process, constitute a hazard to humans or animals, create a public nuisance, or create any hazard in the receiving waters of the wastewater treatment plant. 
(3)	Corrosive substances. Any waters or wastes having a pH lower than 5.5 or greater than 9.0, or having any other corrosive property capable of causing damage or hazard to structures, equipment, and personnel of the wastewater works. 
(4)	Obstructing substances. Solid or viscous substances in quantities or of the size capable of causing obstruction to the flow in sewers, or other interference with the proper operation of the wastewater facilities such as, but not limited to, ashes, bones, cinders, sand, mud, straw, shavings, metal, glass, rags, feathers, tar, plastics, wood, unground garbage, whole blood, paunch manure, hair and fleshings, entrails and paper dishes, cups, milk containers, etc., either whole or ground by garbage grinders. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 6.3) 
Sec. 86-179. - Restricted discharges. 
The following described substances, materials, waters, or waste shall be limited in discharges to municipal systems to concentrations or quantities which will not harm either the sewers, wastewater treatment process or equipment, will not have an adverse effect on the receiving stream, or will not otherwise endanger lives, limb, public property, or constitute a nuisance. The limitations or restrictions on materials or characteristics of waste or wastewater discharged to the sanitary sewer that shall not be violated without approval of the city are as follows: 
(1)	Hot substances. Wastewater having a temperature higher than 150 degrees Fahrenheit (65 degrees Celsius) or wastewater that will elevate the temperature of the influent to the publicly owned treatment works (POTW) to 104 degrees Fahrenheit (40 degrees Celsius) or higher. 
(2)	Oily substances. Wastewater containing more than 25 milligrams per liter of petroleum oil, nonbiodegradable cutting oils, or product of mineral oil origin. 
(3)	Viscous substances or substances that solidify. Wastewater containing more than 100 milligrams per liter of oils, fat, grease, or wax, whether emulsified or not, or containing substances which may solidify or become viscous at temperatures between 32 degrees Fahrenheit (0 degrees Celsius) and 130 degrees Fahrenheit (65 degrees Celsius). 
(4)	Shredded garbage. Any garbage that has not been properly shredded. Garbage grinders may be connected to sanitary sewers from homes, hotels, institutions, restaurants, hospitals, catering establishments, or similar places where garbage originates from the preparation of food in kitchens for the purpose of consumption on the premises or when served by caterers. 
(5)	Industrial discharges. All industrial discharges to the city sewer system must comply with the Federal Industrial Pretreatment Standards (40 CFR 403) and those Industrial Pretreatment Standards developed by the Georgia Environmental Protection Division. 
(6)	Taste or odor producing substances. Any waters or wastes containing taste or odor producing substances exceeding limits that may be established by the city. 
(7)	Radioactive substances. Any radioactive wastes or isotopes of the half-life or concentrations as may exceed limits established in compliance with applicable state or federal regulations. 
(8)	Sludge. Quantities of flow, concentrations, or both, that constitute a sludge as defined herein. 
(9)	Substances not amenable to treatment. Waters or wastes containing substances that are not amenable to treatment or reduction by the wastewater treatment processes employed, or are amenable to treatment only to the degree that the wastewater treatment plant effluent cannot meet the requirements of other agencies having jurisdiction over discharge to the receiving waters. 
(10)	Substances that produce gases. Any water or wastes that, by interaction with other water or wastes in the public sewer system, release obnoxious gases, form solids which interfere with the collection system, or create a condition deleterious to structures and treatment processes. 
(11)	Substances producing certain reactions. Materials that exert or cause: 
a.	Any unusual concentrations of inert suspended solids, such as, but not limited to, Fuller's earth, lime slurries, and lime residues, or of dissolved solids, such as, but not limited to, sodium chloride and sodium sulfate. 
b.	Excessive discoloration (such as, but not limited to, dye wastes and vegetable tanning solutions). 
c.	Unusual BOD (above 300 mg/l), chemical oxygen demand, or chlorine demand in the quantities as to constitute a significant load on the sewage treatment plant. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 6.4) 
Sec. 86-180. - Dilution prohibited; violation. 
Any dilution of the wastewater by the user for the purpose of decreasing the concentrations of toxic materials shall be considered a violation of articles I through IV of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 6.12) 
Sec. 86-181. - Options of city regarding restricted discharges. 
If any waters or wastes are discharged or are proposed to be discharged to the public sewers that contain the substances or possess the characteristics enumerated in section 86-179 and that in the judgment of the city, may have a deleterious effect upon the wastewater facilities, processes, equipment, or receiving waters, or which otherwise create a hazard to life or constitute a public nuisance, the city may: 
(1)	Reject the wastes; 
(2)	Require pretreatment to an acceptable condition for discharge to the public sewers; 
(3)	Require control over the quantities and rates of discharge; or 
(4)	Require surcharge payment to cover added cost of handling and treating the wastes. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 6.5) 
Sec. 86-182. - Grease, oil, and sand interceptors. 
(a)	Required. Grease, oil, and sand interceptors shall be provided when, in the opinion of the city, they are necessary for the proper handling of liquid wastes containing floatable grease in excessive amounts, sand, or other harmful ingredients; except that the interceptors shall not be required for private living quarters or dwelling units. 
(b)	Specifications. All interceptors shall be of a type and capacity approved by the designated city official and shall be located as to be readily and easily accessible for cleaning and inspection. 
(c)	Maintenance. In the maintenance of these interceptors, the owner shall be responsible for the proper removal and disposal by appropriate means of the captured material and shall maintain records of the dates and means of disposal which are subject to review by the designated city official. Any removal and hauling of the collected materials not performed by the owner's personnel must be performed by currently licensed waste disposal firms. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 6.6) 
Sec. 86-183. - Monitoring facility. 
When required by the city, the owner of any property serviced by a building sewer carrying industrial wastes shall install a suitable monitoring structure together with the necessary meters and other appurtenances in the building sewer to facilitate observation, sampling, and measurement of the wastes. The structure, when required, shall be accessible and safely located and shall be constructed in accordance with plans approved by the city. The structure shall be installed by the owner at his expense and shall be maintained by him so as to be safe and accessible at all times. This requirement will be imposed by the city on a case-by-case as needed basis. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 6.7) 
Sec. 86-184. - Information to be provided. 
Industrial users may be required to provide information needed to determine compliance with this article. These requirements may include, but are not limited to: 
(1)	Wastewater discharge peak rate and volume over a specified time period; 
(2)	Chemical analyses of wastewaters; 
(3)	Information on raw materials, processes, and products affecting wastewater volume and quality; 
(4)	Quantity and disposition of specific liquid, sludge, oil, solvent, or other materials important to sewer use control; 
(5)	A plot plan of sewers of the user's property showing sewer and pretreatment facility location; 
(6)	Details of wastewater pretreatment facilities; and 
(7)	Details of systems to prevent and control the losses of materials through spills to the public sewer. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 6.8) 
Sec. 86-185. - No limitation on discretion of city. 
No statement contained in articles I through IV of this chapter shall be construed as preventing any special agreement or arrangement between the city and any industrial concern whereby an industrial waste of unusual strength or character may be accepted by the city for treatment. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 6.9) 
Sec. 86-186. - Monitoring and testing standards. 
All measurements, tests, and analyses of the characteristics of waters and wastes to which reference is made in articles I through IV of this chapter shall be determined in accordance with the latest edition of Standard Methods for the Examination of Water and Wastewater, published by the American Public Health Association. Sampling methods, location times, durations, and frequencies are to be determined on an individual basis, subject to approval by the city. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 6.10) 
Sec. 86-187. - Pretreatment plans for industrial wastes. 
Persons discharging industrial wastes into the sewerage system may be required to pretreat the wastes. Plans for all pretreatment facilities shall be approved by the designated city official or the state environmental protection division prior to construction. At the time written plans are submitted for approval, written maintenance plans shall also be submitted and approved by the designated city official. The facilities shall be allowed to operate only as long as they are maintained in accordance with the approved maintenance plans. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 6.11) 
Sec. 86-188. - Minimum pretreatment requirements. 
Pretreatment requirements shall be determined on a case-by-case basis and shall include the following facilities as a minimum: 
(1)	Neutralization. If plans are submitted for the neutralization of strong acid or alkaline wastes, the plans shall include the necessary instrumentation and controls to ensure compliance with the regulations in this division at all times. 
(2)	Equalization. Holding tanks or equalization basins shall be required ahead of the receiving manhole of the city sewerage system when deemed necessary by the designated city official to prevent peak flows that exceed the capacity of the system or that result in operational problems. 
(3)	Maintenance. All pretreatment facilities shall be operated and maintained continuously in satisfactory and effective operation by the owner at his expense. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 6.11) 
Sec. 86-189. - Waiver of pretreatment requirements. 
There shall be no provision for the granting of variances for discharge of incompatible wastes. If a user begins to violate any of the provisions of articles I through IV of this chapter, it shall be his responsibility to apply to the designated city official that can issue a temporary permit along with a compliance schedule for planning and construction of necessary treatment or pretreatment works. Each case will be carefully evaluated with respect to its effect on the wastewater treatment system and the environment prior to issuance of a temporary permit and compliance schedule. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 6.12) 
Sec. 86-190. - Disconnection of service upon violation; procedure. 
Failure to comply with the provisions of articles I through IV of this chapter shall be cause for the discontinuance of sewer or water service to the offending person. The procedure shall be as follows: 
(1)	Written notice. A written notice, signed by the designated city official, shall be delivered personally to the person then responsible for the offending use, outlining the conditions of the wastes which violate the city Code. 
(2)	Service of notice. In the event that the person in charge will not accept the notice, it shall be conveyed by registered mail to the responsible person. The person notified shall have 24 hours from the time of receipt of the notice, either personally delivered or received by registered mail, to correct the offending conditions. 
(3)	Failure to comply; disconnection. If correction is not made or a request for extension is not received by the city within 24 hours, it shall be mandatory that water or sewer service shall be discontinued to the offending person without further notice. 
(4)	Request for extension. If a request for an extension of time is received by the city within 24 hours of the notice referenced in subsection (2) of this section, and if circumstances are such that, in the opinion of the designated city official, the best interest of the city would be served by extending the time for correction of the offending condition, then he may grant an extension of time up to a maximum limit of 30 days. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 6.13) 
Sec. 86-191. - Responsibilities of user. 
It shall be the responsibility of the person discharging industrial waste into the city sewerage system to: 
(1)	Monitoring structure. Build a monitoring and control structure in the discharge line from his premises, immediately prior to the entrance of the discharge line into the city sewerage system, suitable for the sampling and measuring of wastes. Plans for this structure must be approved by the city. This requirement may be waived at the discretion of the city. 
(2)	Control or other manhole. In the event that no special manhole is required, the control manhole shall be considered to be the nearest downstream manhole in the public sewer to the point at which the building sewer is connected. 
(3)	Notification of operation changes. Contact the designated city official prior to operation changes which will materially alter the characteristics of the waste from the last prior sampling. 
(4)	Payment of user charges. Make timely, periodic payments to the city of surcharges for excessive loadings in the amounts provided by the city council. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 6.14) 
Secs. 86-192—86-220. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - CONNECTION TO PUBLIC SEWERS 

Sec. 86-221. - Permit required. 
No unauthorized person shall uncover, make any connections with or opening into, use, alter, or disturb any public sewer or appurtenance thereof without first obtaining a written permit from the city. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 5.1) 
Sec. 86-222. - Permit application; fees. 
The owner or his agent shall make application for a permit on a special form furnished by the city. The permit application shall be supplemented by any plans, specifications, or other information considered pertinent in the judgment of the designated city official. A permit and inspection fee in the amount determined by the city council shall be paid at the time the application is filed. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 5.2) 
Sec. 86-223. - Cost of installation and connection. 
All costs and expenses incidental to the installation and connection of the building sewer shall be borne by the owner. The owner shall indemnify the city from any loss or damage that may directly or indirectly be occasioned by the installation of the building sewer. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 5.3) 
Sec. 86-224. - Separate connections; exceptions. 
A separate and independent building sewer shall be provided for every building; except where one building stands at the rear of another on an interior lot and no private sewer is available or can be constructed to the rear building through an adjoining alley, court, yard, or driveway, the front building may be extended to the rear building and the whole considered as one building sewer, but the city does not and will not assume any obligation or responsibility for damage caused by or resulting from any such single connection. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 5.4) 
Sec. 86-225. - Using old connections for new construction. 
Old building sewers may be used in connection with new buildings only when they are found, on examination and test by the designated city official, to meet all requirements of articles I through IV of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 5.5) 
Sec. 86-226. - Materials and construction specifications. 
(a)	Generally. The size, slope, alignment, and materials of construction of a building sewer, and the methods to be used in construction, shall all conform to the requirements of the building and plumbing code or other applicable rules and regulations of the city and any county regulations adopted or approved by the city. In the absence of code provisions or in amplification thereof, the materials and procedures set forth in appropriate specifications of the American Society for Testing and Materials (ASTM) and Water Pollution Control Federation (WPCF) Manual of Practice No. 9 shall apply. 
(b)	Specific regulations. Additionally, the following materials and methods shall apply to building sewers within city supervision: 
(1)	The building sewer shall be cast iron soil pipe, ASTM Specification A74, latest revision, or equal; ductile iron pipe, American National Standards Institute (ANSI) Specification A21.51, latest revision, or equal; or polyvinyl chloride (PVC) sewer pipe, ASTM Specification D3034, latest revision. All joints shall be tight and waterproof. 
(2)	Any part of the building sewer that is located within ten feet of a water service pipe shall be constructed of cast iron soil pipe, or ductile iron pipe with bolted mechanical joints may be required by the designated city official where the sewer is exposed to damage by tree roots. If installed in filled or unstable ground, the building sewer shall be of cast iron soil pipe, except that plastic pipe may be acceptable if laid on a suitable concrete bed or cradle as approved by the designated city official. 
(3)	The size and slope of the building sewer shall be subject to the approval of the designated city official, but in no event shall the diameter be less than four inches. The slope of the four inch pipe shall not be less than one-eighth inch per foot. Furthermore, the appropriate requirements of the Occupational Health and Safety Act (OSHA) shall be followed. 
(c)	Depth of trench; separate trench required. The depth shall be sufficient to afford protection from frost, and the building sewer shall be laid at uniform grade and with straight alignment insofar as possible. Changes in direction shall be made only with properly curved pipe and fittings. Building sewers shall not be placed in the same trench with water service lines. 
(d)	Excavations; pipe laying; backfill. An excavation required for the installation of a building sewer shall be open trench work, unless otherwise approved by the designated city official. Pipe laying and backfill shall be performed in accordance with ASTM Specification C12, latest revision, except that no backfill shall be placed until the work has been inspected and approved. 
(e)	Joints and connections. All joints and connections shall be made gastight and watertight. Push-on joints for cast iron soil pipe shall have neoprene gaskets in accordance with the requirements of ASTM C-564. Push-on joints for ductile iron pipe shall also have neoprene gaskets and be installed according to the manufacturer's recommendations. PVC pipe joint material shall be of the bell and spigot type, sealed with a rubber O-ring gasket, having a composition and texture which is resistant to the common ingredients of sewage, industrial wastes (including oils), and groundwater, and which will endure permanently under the conditions likely to be imposed by this use. Installation of gaskets shall be done in accordance with the pipe manufacturer's instructions using all the necessary materials, lubricants, and equipment recommended by the manufacturer. Other jointing materials may be used only when approved by the designated city official. 
(f)	Place and manner of connection. The connection of the building sewer into the public sewer shall be made at the Y branch, if the branch is available at a suitable location. If the public sewer is 12 inches in diameter or less, and no properly located Y branch is available, the city shall, at the owner's expense, cut a neat hole into the public sewer, with entry in the downstream direction at an angle of about 45 degrees, and install a 45-degree elbow with the spigot end cut so as not to extend past the inner surface of the public sewer. The invert of the building sewer at the point of connection shall be at an elevation of at least one-tenth of a foot above the invert of the public sewer. A neat smooth joint shall be made, and the connection made secure and watertight by encasement in concrete. Special fittings may be used for the connection only when approved by the designated city official. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 5.6) 
Sec. 86-227. - Connection elevation. 
Whenever possible, the building sewer shall be brought to the building at an elevation below the basement floor. No building sewer shall be laid parallel to or within three feet of any bearing wall that might thereby be weakened. In all buildings in which any building drain is too low to permit gravity flow to the public sewer, sanitary sewage carried by the building drain shall be lifted by an approved means and discharged to the building sewer. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 5.7) 
Sec. 86-228. - Prohibited connections. 
No person shall make connection of roof downspouts, foundation drains, areaway drains, or other sources of surface runoff or groundwater to a building sewer or building drain that in turn is connected directly or indirectly to a public sanitary sewer unless the connection is approved for purposes of disposal of polluted surface drainage. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 5.8) 
Sec. 86-229. - Inspection of finished installation. 
The applicant for the building sewer permit shall notify the designated city official when the building sewer is ready for inspection and connection to the public sewer. The connection and testing shall be made under the supervision of the designated city official or his representative. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 5.9) 
Sec. 86-230. - Excavation safety; restoration of city property. 
All excavations for building sewer installation shall be adequately guarded with barricades and lights so as to protect the public from hazard. Streets, sidewalks, parkways, and other public property disturbed in the course of the work shall be restored in a manner satisfactory to the city. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 5.10) 
Sec. 86-231. - Availability of connections; fees and costs. 
The city will define the availability of sewers and any costs associated with sewer permits or construction. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 5.11) 
Sec. 86-232. - Infiltration; inflow. 
If any sewer connection permits the entrance of infiltration or inflow, the city may: 
(1)	Require the owner to repair the sewer connection; 
(2)	Charge the owner a sewer rate that reflects the costs of the additional expense of sewage treatment from the owner's property; 
(3)	Require the owner to disconnect his sewer from the city sewer system. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 5.13) 
Secs. 86-233—86-257. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - PRIVATE WASTEWATER DISPOSAL 

Sec. 86-258. - When permitted. 
If a public sanitary sewer is not available under the provisions of articles I through IV of this chapter, the building sewer shall be connected to a private wastewater disposal system complying with city and state regulations. No septic tank or other subsurface disposal facility shall be installed where a public sewer is accessible to the premises involved, nor in any place where the health officer deems the use of the same to be a menace to human health or well-being. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, §§ 4.1, 4.5, 4.8) 
Sec. 86-259. - Availability of public sewer. 
Any private wastewater system serving a property to which public sewer subsequently becomes available, a direct connection shall be made to the public sewer within 30 days after notice. Any septic tanks, cesspools, and similar private wastewater disposal facilities shall then be cleaned of sludge and filled with suitable material. Premises with private water systems shall not be connected with the public sewerage system. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, §§ 4.6, 4.13) 
Sec. 86-260. - Operation and maintenance. 
The owner shall operate and maintain the private wastewater disposal facilities in a sanitary manner at all times, at no expense to the city. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 4.7) 
Sec. 86-261. - Toilet facilities. 
Every flush toilet shall be connected to a public sewer where available or to a septic tank. Flush toilets shall be provided at all times with sufficient running water under pressure to flush the toilet clean after each use. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 4.9) 
Sec. 86-262. - General specifications. 
The type, capacities, location, and layout of a private wastewater disposal system shall comply with all recommendations of the state department of human resources. No permit shall be issued for any private wastewater disposal system employing subsurface soil absorption facilities unless in compliance with state law and approved by and in conformity with all regulations of the county health department. No septic tank or cesspool shall be permitted to discharge to any natural outlet. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 4.4) 
Sec. 86-263. - Septic tanks. 
(a)	Permit required. No person shall construct, repair, alter, or enlarge any septic tank unless he shall hold a valid permit for the work issued by the health officer. The health officer may withhold the issuance of a permit pending the inspection and approval by the health officer of the site and location of the proposed work. 
(b)	Construction; maintenance. Septic tanks shall be constructed, repaired, altered, enlarged and maintained in accordance with plans and specifications approved by the health officer. Septic tanks shall be maintained in sanitary working order. 
(c)	Inspection. Before any septic tank or any part thereof may be covered after it has been constructed, repaired, altered, or enlarged, it shall be inspected and approved by the health officer. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, §§ 4.2, 4.3) 
Sec. 86-264. - Limitation on location of septic tanks and pit privies. 
No septic tank or pit privy shall be installed in the following locations: 
(1)	Where a public sewer is accessible to the premises involved; 
(2)	In areas where the designated city official deems the use of septic tanks or pit privies to constitute a nuisance or menace to the public health; 
(3)	Where septic tank or pit privy may pollute any water supply; or 
(4)	Where the use of septic tanks or pit privies is not in keeping with the standard of sanitation in adjacent areas. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 4.10) 
Sec. 86-265. - Discharge of septic tanks into sewer system. 
(a)	Restricted. It shall be unlawful to empty, dump, throw or otherwise discharge, into any manhole, catchbasin or other opening, into the city sewer system, or any system connected with and discharging into the sewer system, the contents of any septic tank, sludge, sewage, or other similar matter or material, except as provided in subsection (b) of this section. 
(b)	Permits. The designated city official is hereby authorized to grant permits to discharge the contents of septic tanks at locations specified by the designated city official and under his supervision. The permits may be revoked at any time if, in the opinion of the designated city official, continued dumping of the matter into the sewers will be injurious to the sewer system or treatment processes. 
(c)	Charges; payment; failure to pay. A charge shall be made for the privilege of dumping the contents of septic tanks, as provided in separate rules. A record shall be kept of the dumpings and statements rendered at the first of each month, the amount of the statements shall be payable within ten days after rendition. Failure to pay the amounts due within the ten-day period shall be cause for revoking the permit. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 4.11) 
Sec. 86-266. - Notice of unsanitary operation. 
Any premises that has a septic tank, privy, or any other sewage, industrial waste, or liquid waste disposal system, located thereon that does not function in a sanitary manner shall be corrected within 30 days from the receipt of written notification from the health officer that the system is not functioning in a sanitary manner, and order that the system be corrected. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 4.12) 
Sec. 86-267. - Discretionary requirements. 
No statement contained in articles I through IV of this chapter shall be construed to interfere with any additional requirements that may be imposed by the designated city official. 
(Ord. of 7-8-1996, § 4.14) 
Secs. 86-268—86-278. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - WATER 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Secs. 86-279—86-289. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - WATER SERVICE 

Sec. 86-290. - Connection required for drinking water. 
No wells shall be allowed in the city to be used for the purpose of potable drinking water. All residential, commercial, and industrial structures within the city, situated within 1,000 feet of available city water service, shall be required to connect to the city's system, as determined by the city, unless otherwise specifically permitted by the city council. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2004, § 18-6) 
Sec. 86-291. - Minimum charge; use of water. 
A minimum connection charge, as provided in the rate schedule established by the city council, shall be made for each water connection subscribed for. Water furnished for a given lot shall be used on that lot only, except for fire protection. The city shall not, under any condition, furnish water free of charge to anyone. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2004, § 18-4) 
Sec. 86-292. - City's rights and responsibilities. 
(a)	Service adjacent to lines. The city shall run a service line from its distribution line to the property where the distribution line exists or is to be constructed, and runs immediately adjacent and parallel to the property to be served. 
(b)	Service not adjacent to lines. The city may make connections to service other properties not adjacent to its lines upon payment of reasonable costs for the extensions of its distribution lines as may be required to render the service. 
(c)	Installation of meter. The city shall install its meter at or near the property line or, at the city's option, on the consumer's property within three feet of the property line. 
(d)	Refusal to provide service. The city reserves the right to refuse service unless the consumer's lines or piping are installed so as to prevent cross connection or backflow. 
(e)	Notifications of service interruptions. Under normal conditions, the consumer will be notified of any anticipated interruptions of service by the city. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2004, § 18-5) 
Sec. 86-293. - Consumer's responsibility, liability. 
(a)	Use of water restricted. Water furnished by the city shall be used for consumption by the consumer, members of his household and employees only. The consumer shall not sell water to any other person or permit any other person to use the water. Water shall not be used for irrigation, fire protection or other purposes, except when water is available in sufficient quantity without interfering with the regular domestic consumption in the area served. Disregard of this rule shall be sufficient cause for refusal or discontinuance of service. 
(b)	Access to city's meter. Where meter or meter boxes are placed on the premises of a consumer, a suitable place shall be provided by the consumer therefore, unobstructed and accessible at all times to the meter reader. 
(c)	Double check valve. The consumer shall be required to maintain a double check valve on the consumer's side of the meter. 
(d)	Installation and maintenance. The consumer's piping and apparatus shall be installed and maintained by the consumer at the consumer's expense in a safe and efficient manner and in accordance with the sanitary regulations of the city, county, and state. 
(e)	Disconnection of private wells. In order to be received as a consumer and entitled to receive water from the city's water system, all applicants must offer proof that any private wells located on their property are not physically connected to the lines of the city's water system, and all applicants by becoming consumers of the city covenant and agree that so long as they continue to be consumers of the city they will not permit the connection of any private wells on their property to the city's water system. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2004, § 18-6) 
Sec. 86-294. - Access to premises. 
Duly authorized agents of the city shall have access at all hours to the premises of the consumer for the purpose of installing or removing city property, inspecting piping, reading and testing meters, or for any other purpose in connection with the water service and its facilities and the sewer service and its facilities. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2004, § 18-7) 
Sec. 86-295. - Extensions of system; easements. 
Extensions to the system shall be made only when the consumer shall grant or convey or shall cause to be granted or conveyed to the city, a permanent easement or right-of-way across any property traversed by the water and sewer lines. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2004, § 18-7) 
Secs. 86-296—86-306. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - WATER CONSERVATION 

Sec. 86-307. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Commercial means any type of building other than residential. 
Construction means the erection of a new building or the alteration of an existing building in connection with its repair or renovation or in connection with making an addition to an existing building and shall include the replacement of a malfunctioning, unserviceable, or obsolete faucet, showerhead, toilet, or urinal in an existing building. 
Residential means any building or unit of a building intended for occupancy as a dwelling but shall not include a hotel or motel. 
(Ord. of 2-11-1991, § 1) 
Sec. 86-308. - Construction restrictions. 
No construction, including construction that involves the repair or renovation of or in addition to any existing building, when the repair or renovation of or in addition to the existing building includes replacement of toilets or showers or both, whether residential or commercial, may be initiated within the city of the following types: 
(1)	Employs a gravity tank-type, flushometer-value, or flushometer-tank toilet that uses more than an average of 1.6 gallons of water per flush; 
(2)	Employs a shower head that allows a flow of more than an average of 2.5 gallons of water per minute at 60 pounds per square inch of pressure; 
(3)	Employs a urinal that uses more than an average of 1.0 gallons of water per flush; 
(4)	Employs a lavatory faucet or lavatory replacement aerator that allows a flow of more than 2.0 gallons of water per minute; or 
(5)	Employs a kitchen faucet or kitchen replacement aerator that allows a flow of more than 2.50 gallons of water per minute. 
(Ord. of 2-11-1991, § 2) 
Sec. 86-309. - Exemption. 
The owner, or his agent, of a building undergoing new construction or renovation who is entitled to an exemption as specified in this section shall obtain the exemption by applying at the office of the building inspector of the city and paying the fee established by the city council for inspection and issuance of the exemption. New construction and the repair or renovation of an existing building shall be exempt from the requirements of this division when: 
(1)	The repair or renovation of the existing building does not include the replacement of the plumbing or sewage system servicing toilets, faucets or showerheads within the existing buildings; 
(2)	When the plumbing or sewage system within the existing building, because of its capacity, design, or installation would not function properly if the toilets, faucets or showerheads required by this article were installed; 
(3)	The system is a well or gravity flow from a spring and is owned privately by an individual for use in the individual's personal residence; or 
(4)	Units to be installed are specifically designed for use by the handicapped, specifically designed to withstand unusual abuse or installation in a penal institution, or toilets for juveniles. 
(Ord. of 2-11-1991, § 5) 
Sec. 86-310. - Enforcement; penalty. 
This division shall be enforced by the office of the building inspector of the city. Citations for violation may be issued by the city's chief building inspector. Any person or other entity in violation of this division shall be subject to penalties as provided in section 1-10. 
(Ord. of 2-11-1991, § 6) 
Secs. 86-311—86-329. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - DROUGHT CONTINGENCY PLAN 

Sec. 86-330. - Applicability. 
The drought contingency plan set forth in this division shall become effective and implemented upon the advice and recommendation of the designated city official or upon instructions from the state. 
(Res. of 10-13-1966) 
Sec. 86-331. - Regulations. 
Upon declaration by the designated city official that this plan is to be implemented, the following regulations shall immediately apply and shall continue to apply until the city declares that implementation of the plan shall cease: 
(1)	There shall be no outside watering of any kind, including street cleaning, public fountains, park irrigation, watering lawns, gardens, shrubbery, etc. 
(2)	There shall be no commercial, public or private water use, such as swimming pools, and motor vehicle washing of any kind. 
(3)	There shall be no commercial and home laundry use except during the hours of 7:00 p.m. to 7:00 a.m. only. 
(Res. of 10-13-1966, §§ 1—3) 
Sec. 86-332. - Enforcement. 
Compliance with this drought contingency plan when activated, shall be in the following manner: 
(1)	Inspection. Duly authorized officers bearing proper credentials and identification shall be permitted to enter all properties for the purpose of inspection, observation, measurement and testing. 
(2)	Written notice of first violation. Any person found to be violating the provisions of this resolution shall be served written notice stating the nature of the violation and shall be issued a warning for the violation. 
(3)	Disconnection and fine for second violation. On second violation, water service will be terminated and a reconnect fee in the amount established by the city council will be charged. 
(4)	Subsequent violations. For the third and all subsequent violations, the violator will be charged for each violation a reconnect fee equal to four times the reconnect fee for second violations. 
(Res. of 10-13-1966, §§ 1—3) 
Secs. 86-333—86-352. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - WELLHEAD PROTECTION 

Sec. 86-353. - Purpose and intent. 
The purpose of this division is to ensure the provision of a safe and sanitary drinking water supply for the city by the establishment of wellhead protection zones surrounding the wellheads for all wells which are the supply sources for the city water system and by the designation and regulation of property uses and conditions which may be maintained within the zones. 
(Ord. of 6-14-1993, § 1) 
Sec. 86-354. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Hazardous waste or hazardous material means any waste or material which because of its quantity, concentration or physical, chemical or infectious characteristics may: 
(1)	Cause or significantly contribute to an increase in mortality or an increase in serious irreversible or incapacitating reversible illness; or 
(2)	Pose a substantial present or potential hazard to human health or to the environment when improperly treated, stored, transported, disposed of or otherwise managed. 
Sanitary landfill means a disposal site where solid wastes, including putrescible wastes, or hazardous wastes are disposed of on land by placing earth cover thereon. 
Wellhead means the upper terminal of a well, including adapters, ports, seals, valves and other attachments. 
(Ord. of 6-14-1993, § 2) 
Sec. 86-355. - Establishment of wellhead protection zone. 
The city has established a use district to be known as a wellhead protection zone, identified and described as all the area within a circle the center of which is the center of any city water supply wellhead and the radius of which is feet. 
(Ord. of 6-14-1993, § 3) 
Sec. 86-356. - Permitted uses. 
The following uses shall be permitted within wellhead protection zones: 
(1)	Any use permitted within existing agricultural or single-family residential districts, except that the minimum residential lot size for a lot any portion of which lies within the wellhead protection zone, shall not be less one acre; and 
(2)	Any other open land use where any building located on the property is incidental and accessory to the primary open land use. 
(Ord. of 6-14-1993, § 4) 
Sec. 86-357. - Prohibited uses. 
The following uses or conditions shall be and are hereby prohibited within wellhead protection zones, whether or not the use or condition may otherwise be ordinarily included as a part of a use permitted under section 86-356. 
(1)	Surface use or storage of hazardous material, expressly including commercial use of agricultural pesticides; 
(2)	Septic tanks or drain fields appurtenant thereto; 
(3)	Impervious surfaces other than roofs of buildings, and streets, driveways and walks serving buildings permitted under section 86-356; 
(4)	Sanitary landfills; 
(5)	Hazardous waste disposal sites; 
(6)	Stormwater infiltration basins; 
(7)	Underground storage tanks; 
(8)	Sanitary sewer lines within 150 feet of a wellhead. 
(Ord. of 6-14-1993, § 5) 
Sec. 86-358. - Administration. 
The policies and procedures for administration of any wellhead protection zone established under this division, including without limitation those applicable to nonconforming uses, exceptions, enforcement and penalties, shall be the same as provided in chapter 94, as the same is presently enacted or may from time to time be amended. 
Secs. 86-359—86-389. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - ELECTRIC POWER 

Sec. 86-390. - Application for service; deposit. 
To connect to the city's electric service, the consumer shall make application for electric service, in person, at the city hall and at the same time, make a cash deposit in the amount established by the city council. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2004, § 18-17) 
Sec. 86-391. - Connect, disconnect, and reconnect fees. 
The city shall impose connect, disconnect, and reconnect fees in the amounts established by the city council. 
(Ord. of 6-14-2004, § 18-18) 
Sec. 86-392. - Irrevocable license granted to City of Ellaville for electric service line maintenance. 
(a)	With respect to any electric power line owned by the city which is either now or in the future located within the corporate limits of the city or which is otherwise a part of the city's electric distribution system, whether such electric power line is a primary service line or a secondary service line, upon installation of such line, the owner of the property, and any person or entity having any legal or equitable interest in said property, across which such primary service line or secondary service line runs above ground or below ground shall be considered to have granted to the city an irrevocable license to come upon the owner's property and repair and maintain such electric service lines from time to time. For the purposes of this section, reference to such repair and maintenance services shall specifically include, but shall not be limited to, the cutting or trimming of hedges, bushes, trees, and similar vegetation which the city determines are, or might become, a danger to such electric service lines or which might cause harm or damage to such lines. 
(b)	To the extent practicable and assuming no emergency situation, the city shall notify such property owners at least 48 hours in advance with respect to each period of time that the city deems it necessary or appropriate to come onto the property owner's property pursuant to the irrevocable license to perform the repair and maintenance services authorized by this section. Such notice may be in writing mailed or personally delivered by the city or its designee to the last known address of the property owner according to the city's electric service billing records, or personally delivered by the city or its designee to the owner or to the premises if the owner cannot be located at the time of such notice delivery. 
(c)	The decision of the city's electric service supervisor shall be final and binding upon the property owner as to the nature and the necessity of the repair and maintenance activities authorized hereunder; however, if the property owner refuses to authorize or allow the city to have access to the owner's property for such repair and maintenance services, and in the event that the power line is later damaged or destroyed, and such damage or destruction would not, by a preponderance of the evidence, have occurred if the owner had allowed the city to exercise its rights under the irrevocable license established in this section to undertake such repair and maintenance service (including, but not limited to, the removal of "danger trees"), as authorized in this section, then the property owner shall be obligated to pay one-half of the cost of repair or replacement of the damaged or destroyed line to the city, and such amount may be included upon the property owner's electric service bill, and collected by the city in the same manner as regular electric service bills are collected. 
(d)	Nothing in this section shall be construed or held to create or establish any liability of any kind or nature on the part of the city with respect to electric service line repair and maintenance services that the city undertakes or fails to undertake. 
(Ord. of 2-8-2016) 
Chapter 90 - VEGETATION 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 90-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Park trees means trees, bushes, shrubs and all other woody vegetation in public parks having individual names, and all areas owned by the city, or to which the public has free access as a park. 
Street trees means trees, shrubs, bushes, and all other woody vegetation on land lying between property lines on either side of all streets, avenues, or ways within the city. 
Topping means the severe cutting back of limbs to stubs larger than three inches in diameter within the tree's crown to such a degree so as to remove the normal canopy and disfigure the tree. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, §§ 1, 13) 
Secs. 90-2—90-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - CITY TREE BOARD 

Sec. 90-21. - Members; appointment; compensation. 
The city has created and established a city tree board that shall consist of five members, all citizens and residents of the city. All members shall be appointed by the mayor, with approval of the council, and shall serve without compensation. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, §§ 2, 4) 
Sec. 90-22. - Terms of office; vacancies. 
The term of the five board members shall be three years. In the event that a vacancy shall occur during the term of any member, his successor shall be appointed for the unexpired portion of the term. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 3) 
Sec. 90-23. - Duties and responsibilities. 
It shall be the responsibility of the board to study, investigate, develop or update annually, and administer a written plan for the care, preservation, pruning, planting, replanting, removal or disposition of trees and shrubs in parks, along streets and in other public areas. The plan will be presented annually to the city council, and upon the council's acceptance and approval, shall constitute the official comprehensive city tree plan. The board, when requested by the city council, shall consider, investigate, make findings, report, and make recommendations regarding any special matter or question coming within the scope of its work. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 5) 
Sec. 90-24. - Operation. 
The board shall choose its own officers, make its own rules and regulations and keep a journal of its proceedings. A majority of the members shall be a quorum for the transaction of business. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 6) 
Sec. 90-25. - Review by city council. 
The city council shall have the right to review the conduct, acts and decisions of the city tree board. Any person may appeal any ruling or order of the city tree board to the city council, who may hear the matter and make a final decision. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 19) 
Sec. 90-26. - Interference with board. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to prevent, delay or interfere with the city tree board, or any of its agents, while engaging in and about the planting, cultivating, mulching, spraying, pruning, or removing of any street trees, park trees, or trees on private grounds, as authorized in this article. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 17) 
Secs. 90-27—90-55. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - TREE REGULATIONS 

Sec. 90-56. - Approved street tree species. 
The following list constitutes the official approved street tree species for the city. No species other than those included in this list may be planted as street trees without permission of the city tree board. 

 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 7) 
Sec. 90-57. - Tree spacing. 
The spacing of street trees will be in accordance with the three species size classes listed in section 90-56, and no trees may be planted closer together than the following: small trees, 30 feet; medium trees, 40 feet; and large trees, 50 feet; except in special plantings designed or approved by a landscape architect. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 8) 
Sec. 90-58. - Distance from curb and sidewalk. 
The distance trees may be planted from curbs or curblines and sidewalks will be in accordance with the three species size classes listed in section 90-56, and no trees may be planted closer to any curb or sidewalk than the following: small trees, two feet; medium trees, three feet; and large trees, four feet. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 9) 
Sec. 90-59. - Distance from street corners and fireplugs. 
No street trees shall be planted closer than 35 feet of any street corner, measured from the point of the nearest intersection curbs or curblines. No street trees shall be planted closer than ten feet of any fireplug. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 10) 
Sec. 90-60. - Distance from utility lines and pipes. 
No street trees, other than those species listed as small trees in section 90-56, may be planted under or within ten lateral feet of any overhead utility wire, or over or within five lateral feet of any undergroundwater line, transmission line or other utility. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 11) 
Sec. 90-61. - Tree planting, maintenance, and removal. 
(a)	Landscaping and public safety. The city shall plant, prune, maintain and remove trees, plants and shrubs within the lines of all streets, alleys, avenues, lanes, squares and public grounds, as may be necessary to ensure public safety or to preserve or enhance the symmetry and beauty of such public grounds. 
(b)	Unsafe and injurious trees. The city tree board may remove or cause or order to be removed, any tree or part thereof which is in an unsafe condition or which by reason of its nature is injurious to sewer, electric power lines, gas lines, water lines, or other public improvements, or is affected with any injurious fungus, insect or other pest. 
(c)	Planting by property owners. This section does not prohibit the planting of street trees by adjacent property owners, providing that the selection and location of trees is in accordance with the provisions of this article. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 12) 
Sec. 90-62. - Tree topping prohibited. 
It shall be unlawful as a normal practice for any person or city department to top any street tree, park tree, or other trees on public property. Trees severely damaged by storms or other causes, or certain trees under utility wires or other obstructions where other pruning practices are impractical may be exempted from this section at the determination of the city tree board. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 13) 
Sec. 90-63. - Property owner duties. 
(a)	Pruning. Every owner of any tree overhanging any street or right-of-way within the city shall prune the branches so that such branches shall not obstruct the light from any street lamp or obstruct the view of any street intersection and so that there shall be a clear space of eight feet above the surface of the street or sidewalk. 
(b)	Removal. Every owner of any tree adjacent to any street or right-of-way within the city shall remove all dead, diseased or dangerous trees, or broken or decayed limbs which constitute a menace to the safety of the public. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 14) 
Sec. 90-64. - City pruning of privately owned trees. 
The city shall have the right to prune any tree or shrub on private property when it interferes with the proper spread of light along the street from a street light or interferes with visibility of any traffic control device or sign. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 14) 
Sec. 90-65. - City removal of privately owned trees. 
(a)	Dead and diseased trees. The city may cause the removal of any dead or diseased trees on private property within the city when such trees constitute a hazard to life and property or harbor insects or disease that constitute a potential threat to other trees within the city. 
(b)	Notice to owner. The city tree board shall provide written notice to owners or persons responsible for maintenance of any dead or diseased trees subject to removal. Removal shall be done by the owners or persons responsible for maintenance, at their own expense, within 60 days after the date of the service of notice. 
(c)	Failure of owner to remove trees. In the event of the failure of owners or persons responsible for maintenance to comply with such provisions, the city shall remove the trees and charge the cost of removal on the owner's property tax notice. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 15) 
Sec. 90-66. - Persons responsible for tree maintenance. 
(a)	Generally. The owner of any property, lot, building or premises, occupied or vacant, shall be deemed the party responsible for any nuisance occurring on his property. 
(b)	Multiunit buildings. If the property on which a nuisance exists includes a building containing between two and four living or business units or establishments, then the occupants of the living or business units or establishments shall be deemed the responsible party. 
(c)	Unit defined. A living or business unit or establishment is hereby defined as that portion of all of a building or structure that constitutes a separate and undivided family or business concern. 
(d)	Responsibility fixed by contract. If the lease or rental agreement or contract between the owner and the occupant specifically names the party responsible for the clearing or cutting of grass, weeds, or bushes, regardless of ownership and regardless of the number of living or business units or establishments on the premises, the specified party shall be held responsible for compliance with this section. 
Sec. 90-67. - Stump removal. 
All stumps of street and park trees shall be removed below the ground so that the top of the stump shall not project above the surface of the ground. 
(Ord. of 10-12-1992, § 16) 
Secs. 90-68—90-92. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - WEED CONTROL 

Sec. 90-93. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Living unit , business unit and business establishment refer to that portion of all of a building that houses a separate and undivided family or business concern. 
Sec. 90-94. - Height restricted. 
The owner of any lot, building or premises, occupied or vacant, within the city limits, shall not permit any grass, weeds, or wild bushes to grow to a height in excess of ten inches upon such property or premises. 
Sec. 90-95. - Responsible person. 
The person responsible for weed control shall be determined as set forth in section 90-66. 
Sec. 90-96. - Public nuisance; abatement. 
Any violation of this article is declared to be a public nuisance, subject to the procedure for abatement set forth in chapter 38, health and sanitation, in addition to subjecting the responsible party to penalties as set forth in section 1-10. 
Chapter 94 - ZONING[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Zoning procedures, O.C.G.A. § 36-66-1 et seq.; conflict of interest in zoning actions, O.C.G.A. § 36-67A-1. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 94-1. - Enactment clause. 
The mayor and city council enacts this chapter under the exercise of the powers conferred upon it by the Georgia State Constitution. 
Sec. 94-2. - Jurisdiction. 
The provisions of this chapter shall govern all land, buildings and structures within the corporate limits of the city. 
Sec. 94-3. - Intent. 
(a)	It is the intent of this chapter to provide for the uniform treatment of all housing classified as dwelling, single-family, to encourage the provision of affordable housing in a general residential environment by permitting the use of residential industrialized buildings and manufactured homes meeting the definition of dwelling, single-family, as hereinafter set out, in all residential districts in which similar dwellings constructed on site are permitted, subject to the requirements and procedures set forth herein, to ensure similarity in exterior appearance between such residentially designed manufactured homes and industrialized buildings and dwellings which have been constructed under these and other lawful regulations on adjacent lots in the same district, zoning classification or general area. 
(b)	Manufactured homes which do not conform to the standards established in the definition of dwelling, single-family and mobile homes, will be permitted in the agricultural districts and manufactured home community districts, provided that each home complies with the district standards in which it is located and also as a special exception in all zoning districts as provided within this chapter. 
(c)	For the purpose of this chapter, certain words or terms used herein are interpreted as follows: 
(1)	The term "lot" includes the terms "plot" or "parcel." 
(2)	The term "building" includes the term "structure." 
(3)	The term "used" or "occupied," as applied to any land or buildings, shall be construed to include the terms "intended," "arranged," or "designed to be used or occupied." 
(4)	The term "map" or "districting map" means the official districting map of the city. 
(Ord. of. 3-9-1992, § 3.1.1) 
Sec. 94-4. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Accessory use or building means a use or building, sometimes referred to as a utility building, customarily incidental and subordinate to the principal use or building and located on the same lot with such principal use or building. 
Board of appeals means the board of appeals appointed by the city council to hear various appeals and other matters. 
Building means any structure intended for the shelter, housing, or enclosure of persons, animals, or chattels, also including utility buildings. 
Building, front line of, means the line of that face of the building nearest the front line of the lot. This face includes sun parlors and covered porches, whether enclosed or unenclosed, but does not include steps. 
Centerline of streets means a line surveyed and monumented as such, or if a centerline has not been surveyed and monumented, it shall be that line running midway between the outside lines of rights-of-way of the street. 
City of Ellaville means the mayor and city council as formally constituted by the Charter. 
Coverage means that percentage of the plot or lot area covered by the building area. 
Development officer means the person appointed by the city council who is responsible for the enforcement of this chapter. 
Downtown area means the commercial district located at or near the center of the city, as noted on the current districting map. 
Dwelling means a building designed or used for permanent living quarters for one or more families or individuals. 
Dwelling, multifamily, means a building designed or used as a residence for three or more families living independently of each other in a complete dwelling unit. 
Dwelling, one-family , means a structure containing not more than one dwelling unit designed for residential use, which meets or exceeds the following standards: 
(1)	Minimum width in excess of 24 feet by 36 feet. 
(2)	Minimum square footage required by the zone in which located, as required by the board of appeals. 
(3)	The roof shall have a minimum 2½:12 roof pitch and shall have a surface of wood shakes, wood shingles, fiberglass or metal tiles, slate, or other materials approved by the building official. 
(4)	The exterior siding materials shall consists of wood, masonry, concrete, stucco, masonite, lap metal or lap vinyl or other materials of like appearance. 
(5)	Be attached to a permanent foundation as required by the state building codes. 
(6)	Be constructed according to standards established either by the state minimum standard codes as amended from time to time or the standard building code if locally adopted for site-built homes, or the National Manufactured Housing Construction and Safety Standards Act for manufactured homes, or the state Industrialized Buildings Act for the residential industrialized buildings. Each of these codes shall be applicable to the specific structure to which it applies. 
Dwelling, two-family, means a building designed for or occupied exclusively by two families living independently of each other. 
Dwelling unit means a structure or a portion of any structure designed, arranged and used for living quarters for one or more persons living as a single housekeeping unit with cooking facilities, but not including units in hotels, motels, boardinghouses or like uses. 
Family means one or more persons occupying a single dwelling unit; provided that unless all members are related by blood or marriage, no such family shall contain over five persons, but further provided that domestic servants employed on the premises may be housed on the premises without being counted as family. 
Feedlot means any parcel of land upon which the mechanical or handfeeding of five or more livestock animals per acre is performed for a period exceeding 30 days. 
Home occupation means any occupation conducted in a dwelling unit, provided that: 
(1)	No more than two persons other than members of the family residing on the premises shall be engaged in such occupations; 
(2)	The use of the dwelling unit for the home occupation shall be clearly incidental and subordinate to its use for residential purposes by its occupants, and not more than 30 percent of the floor area of the dwelling unit shall be used in the conduct of the home occupation; 
(3)	There shall be no change in the outside appearance of the building or premises, or other visible evidence of the conduct of such home occupation other than one sign, not exceeding four square feet in area, nonilluminated, and mounted flat against the wall of the principal building; 
(4)	Home occupations conducted in any accessory building shall not occupy an area larger than 30 percent of the floor area of the primary dwelling; 
(5)	No traffic shall be generated by such home occupation in greater volumes than would normally be expected in a residential neighborhood, and any need for parking generated by the conduct of such home occupation shall be met off the street and other than in a required front yard; 
(6)	No equipment or process shall be used in such home occupation which creates noise, vibration, glare, fumes, odors, or electrical interference detectable to the normal senses off the lot. In the case of electrical interference, no equipment or process shall be used which creates visual or audible interference in any radio or television receivers off the premises, or cause fluctuations in line voltage off the premises. 
Junkyard means any accumulation or storage of junked vehicles, machinery equipment or appliances, vehicle or machinery parts, rags, litter or other debris in excess of 400 square feet in area. A junked vehicle is hereby defined as any vehicle which is inoperable for more than one month. 
Lot means a parcel of land occupied or capable of being occupied by one or more buildings, including accessory buildings or uses incidental to them, and including such open spaces as are required by this chapter. 
Lot, corner, means a parcel of land at the junction of, and fronting on, two or more intersecting streets. 
Lot, depth of , means the mean horizontal distance between the front and rear lot lines, measured in the general direction of the side lines of the lot. 
Lot lines means the lines bounding a lot as defined herein. 
Lot of record means a lot which is duly recorded in the office of the clerk of superior court. 
Lot, width means the mean width measured at right angle to its depth. 
Manufactured home means a structure defined by and constructed in accordance with the National Manufactured Housing Construction and Safety Standards Act of 1974, as amended, 42 USC 5401 et seq. The definition at the date of adoption of this part is as follows: 
Manufactured home means a structure, transportable in one or more sections, which, in the traveling mode, is eight body feet or more in width or 40 body feet or more in length, or, when erected on site, is 320 or more square feet, and which is built on a permanent chasis and designed to be used as a dwelling with or without a permanent foundation when connected to the required utilities, and includes the plumbing, heating, air conditioning, and electrical systems contained therein; except that such shall include any structure which meets all the requirements of this definition except the size requirements and with respect to which the manufacturer voluntarily files a certification required by the secretary and complies with the standards established under this chapter. 
Manufactured home park means any parcel of land under single ownership designed to accommodate five or more manufactured homes to be used for living or sleeping purposes, including any land, building, structure, or other facilities used by the occupants of manufactured homes on the property. 
Mobile home means a structure, transportable in one or more sections, which, in the traveling mode, is 12 body feet or more in width or 40 body feet or more in length, or, when erected on site, is 480 or more square feet, and which is built on a permanent chasis and designed to be used as a dwelling with or without a permanent foundation when connected to the required utilities, and includes the plumbing, heating, air conditioning, and electrical systems contained therein and manufactured prior to June 15, 1976. 
Other manufactured homes means any manufactured home not meeting the definition of dwelling, single-family. 
Industrialized building means any structure or component thereof which is wholly or in substantial part mode, fabricated, formed, or assembled in manufacturing facilities for installation on a building site and has been manufactured in such a manner that all parts or processes cannot be inspected at the installation site without disassembly, damage to, or destruction thereof. Industrialized buildings are constructed and regulated in accordance with the Industrialized Buildings Act, 1982 Ga. Laws, pages 1637—1643, Part 1 of O.C.G.A. § 8-2-2. 
Modular structures means any structure which is prefabricated in part or whole and moved to the site for assembly. A modular type structure with attached wheels is considered a manufactured home. 
Planning commission means the planning commission appointed by the mayor and city council to review planning and districting matters. 
Sign means a single display surface or display device containing elements organized, related, and composed to form a unit. 
Sign, off-premises, means a sign other than an on-premises sign. 
Sign, on-premises , means a sign relating in its subject matter to the premises on which it is located, or to products, accommodations, services, or activities on the premises. On-premises signs do not include signs erected by the outdoor advertising industry to advertise products and the like located away from the premises. 
Sign, public or semipublic, directional, off-premises, means a sign which directs attention to a public or semipublic activity, such as a school, church, fraternal organization, or the like. Such signs shall not exceed ten square feet in area.
